Ruling on Raml, Sa'y, and Fasting for a Mutamatti
Ruling on raml, sa'y, and fasting timing for mutamatti

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on raml and sa'y for a mutamatti who performed tawaf and sa'y before Mina, and explain the validity of fasting after ihram for Umrah, contrasting with the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
A mutamatti who already performed tawaf and sa'y does not repeat raml or sa'y; fasting after Umrah ihram is valid in the Hanafi school.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses a specific scenario for the mutamatti: after performing tawaf and sa'y early, what are the obligations for raml and sa'y later? Additionally, the text clarifies when the fasting substitute for the dam can be performed, resolving a dispute with the Shafi'i school over the interpretation of 'fi al-hajj'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage first rules on whether a mutamatti who already performed tawaf and sa'y before Mina should repeat raml in Tawaf al-Ziyarah and repeat sa'y. The ruling: he does not do raml and does not repeat sa'y because he already did them once.
This applies only if he performed tawaf and sa'y after entering ihram for Hajj.
2
Understand the obligation of dam and substitute fasting
The mutamatti must sacrifice a dam (wajib). If unable, he must fast three days during Hajj and seven after returning. The fasting is a substitute for the dam and must be performed after the cause (tamattu) exists.
The cause is the combination of Umrah and Hajj in one journey.
3
Analyze the timing of fasting
The text specifies that fasting before tamattu (e.g., in Shawwal before Umrah) is invalid because the cause is not present. However, fasting after entering ihram for Umrah but before tawaf is valid in the Hanafi school.
The cause is contracted upon ihram for Umrah with intention of tamattu.
4
Examine the dispute with Shafi'i
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that 'fi al-hajj' means during the specific days of Hajj (8th-13th Dhul Hijjah). The Hanafi response is that 'Hajj' refers to the time of Hajj (the entire season), so fasting after Umrah ihram is within that time.
The practical consequence: Hanafis allow fasting earlier; Shafi'is restrict it to the Hajj days.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَ لَوْ كَانَ هَذَا الْمُتَمَعُ بَعْدَ مَا أَحْرَمَ بِالْحَج طَافَ وَ سَعَى قَبْلَ أَنْ يَرُوحَ إِلى مِنى لَمْ يَرْمَلُ فِي طَوَافِ الزِّيَارَةِ وَلَا يَسْعَى بَعْدَهُ لِأَنَّهُ قَدْأَتِي بِذَلِكَ مَرَّةً وَعَلَيْهِ دَمُ التَّمَتُّعِ لِلنَّحِ الَّذِى تَلَوْنَاهُ فَإِنْ لَمْ يَجِدُ صَامَ ثَلَثَةَ أَيَّامٍ فِي الْحَجَ وَ سَبْعَةٍ إِذَا رَجَعَ عَلَى الْوَجْهِ الَّذِي بَيَّنَاهُ فِي الْقِرَانِ فَإِنْ صَامَ ثَلَثَةَ أَيَّامٍ مِنْ شَقَالَ ثُمَّ اعْتَمَرَ لَمْ يَجُزهُ عَنِ الثَّلَثَةِ لَانَّ وُجُوبِ هَذَا الصَّوْمِ التَّمَتَّعُ لِأَنَّهُ بَدَل عَنِ الدَّمِ وَهُوَ فِى هَذِهِ الْحَالَةِ غَيْرُ مُتَمَتِعِ فَلا يَجُوزُ أَدَاءُ هُ قَبْلَ وُجُودِ سَبَبِهِ وَإِنْ صَامَهَا بَعْدَ مَا أَحْرَمَ بِالْعُمْرَةِ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَطُوفَ جَازَ عِنْدَنَا خِلَافًا لِلشَّافِعِي لَهُ قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى ﴿فَصِيَامُ ثَلَثَةِ أَيَّامٍ في الْحَجَ وَلَنَا أَنَّهُ آدَاءُ بَعْدَ الْعِقَادِ سَبَبِهِ وَالْمُرَادُ بِالْحَقِّ الْمَذْكُورِ فِى النَّصِ وَقْتُهُ عَلَى مَا بَيَّنَّا وَالْأَفْضَلُ تَأْخِيرُهَا إلى اخِرِ وَقُتِهَا وَهُوَ يَوْمُ عَرَفَةَ لِمَا بَيَّنَّا فِي الْقِرَان
And if this mutamatti, after having entered ihram for Hajj, performed tawaf and sa'y before going to Mina, he should not do raml in Tawaf al-Ziyarah and should not perform sa'y after it, because he has already done that once. And upon him is the dam of tamattu according to the text we recited. If he cannot find [an animal], he should fast three days during Hajj and seven when he returns, in the manner we explained in Qiran. If he fasts three days in Shawwal and then performs Umrah, it does not suffice for the three [days], because the cause for the obligation of this fast is tamattu, as it is a substitute for the dam, and he is not a mutamatti in that state. So performing it before its cause exists is not permissible. But if he fasts them after having entered ihram for Umrah before performing tawaf, it is permissible in our view, contrary to al-Shafi'i. His proof is the saying of Allah: 'So fasting of three days during Hajj'. And our proof is that he performed it after the cause was contracted, and the meaning of 'Hajj' mentioned in the text is its time, as we have explained. And it is better to delay them until the end of their time, which is the Day of Arafah, for the reason we explained in Qiran.
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage addresses several rulings regarding a mutamatti who, after entering ihram for Hajj, performs tawaf and sa'y before proceeding to Mina on the 8th. In such a case, he should not do raml (brisk walking) in the Tawaf al-Ziyarah (the obligatory tawaf on the 10th), nor should he repeat sa'y, because he already performed both once. The raml was only for his first tawaf in Hajj, and sa'y is only performed once in Hajj. The mutamatti must sacrifice a dam (animal) for tamattu. If he cannot afford it, he must fast three days during the days of Hajj (from the time he enters ihram for Hajj until the Day of Arafah) and seven days after returning home. A critical point: if he fasts the three days in Shawwal (the month after Ramadan) before even entering into tamattu (i.e., before performing Umrah), those fasts are not valid as the tamattu fast, because the obligation for the fast arises only when tamattu is performed. Fasting before the cause (tamattu) is not valid. However, if he enters ihram for Umrah and then fasts before performing tawaf, it is permissible in the Hanafi school, because the cause (the ihram for Umrah with intention of tamattu) is already present. There is a dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, who argues that the Quran says 'during Hajj' and the fasting must be within the Hajj period. The Hanafi response is that 'Hajj' in the verse refers to the time of Hajj (the entire season), not the specific days of Hajj rites. The best time to fast is on the Day of Arafah, but it is permissible earlier as long as it is after entering ihram for Umrah.

Key Terms
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal required for tamattu as a compensation.
صوم التمتع (sawm al-tamattu): Fasting three days during Hajj and seven after return as a substitute for the dam.
سبب (sabab): The cause (tamattu) that obligates the fast/dam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person performs Umrah in Shawwal intending tamattu, when can he fast the three days for tamattu?
A) Only on the 8th, 9th, and 10th of Dhul Hijjah.
B) Only after returning home from Hajj.
C) Anytime after entering ihram for Umrah and before tawaf is valid.
D) Anytime after completing Umrah and before the 8th of Dhul Hijjah.

Key Takeaway
A mutamatti does not repeat raml or sa'y if already performed; the substitute fasting is valid after ihram for Umrah, as the cause (tamattu) exists, according to the Hanafi interpretation of 'fi al-hajj' as the time of Hajj.

Raml, Sa'i, and Fasting for the Mutamatti: Hanafi Rulings and a Dispute with al-Shafi'i
Rulings on raml, sa'i, dam, and fasting for a mutamatti with a dispute on fasting timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on raml, sa'i, and the substitute fasting for a mutamatti, and explain the dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the timing of the three fasts.

Core Idea
Raml is only for tawafs followed by sa'i; if sa'i is already done, raml is omitted. The three fasts for a mutamatti are valid after ihram for Umrah, not before.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses two distinct yet related issues for a mutamatti (one performing Hajj al-Tamattu'): the performance of raml and sa'i after already having performed them, and the obligation of a substitute fast when unable to sacrifice. The latter involves a well-known ikhtilaf with Imam al-Shafi'i over the interpretation of the Quranic phrase 'fi al-Hajj' in verse 2:196. Understanding this passage equips you with both a specific ruling and a method of textual interpretation that underpins Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and initial rulings
The passage describes a mutamatti who, after entering ihram for Hajj, performs tawaf and sa'i before going to Mina. The ruling is that he does not perform raml in tawaf al-ziyarah and does not repeat sa'i after it.
This is because sa'i is performed only once in Hajj, and raml is tied to a tawaf that is followed by sa'i.
2
Understand the logic behind raml and sa'i omission
Raml is prescribed only in a tawaf after which sa'i is performed. Since sa'i has already been done after tawaf al-qudum, it is not repeated after tawaf al-ziyarah, hence raml is omitted as well.
Even if the mutamatti did not do raml in the first tawaf, he still does not do raml in the second.
3
Note the obligation of the dam and its substitute
The mutamatti is obligated to offer a sacrifice (dam). If unable, he must fast three days during the Hajj season and seven days after returning home, similar to a qarin.
The dam is wajib based on Quran 2:196.
4
Analyze the dispute on when to fast the three days
The dispute centers on the timing of the three fasts. The Hanafi position: valid after entering ihram for Umrah (cause exists) even before tawaf. The Shafi'i position: must be after entering ihram for Hajj.
Both schools cite the same verse but differ on the meaning of 'fi al-Hajj'.
5
Evaluate the proofs
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that 'fi al-Hajj' means in the state of Hajj (after ihram for Hajj). Hanafis interpret it as 'in the time of Hajj' (Shawwal to the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah), and argue that the cause of tamattu' exists after Umrah ihram.
The Hanafi interpretation relies on the principle that an act can be performed after its cause arises, even if the full obligation is not yet due.
6
Determine the preferred timing
Although the fasts are valid after Umrah ihram, it is better to delay them to the end of the time, specifically so that they conclude on the Day of Arafah (9th Dhu al-Hijjah).
This is based on the same reasoning explained in the section on qiran.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ كَانَ هَذَا الْمُتَمَعُ بَعْدَ مَا أَحْرَمَ بِالْحَج طَافَ وَ سَعَى قَبْلَ أَنْ يَرُوحَ إِلى مِنى لَمْ يَرْمَلُ فِي طَوَافِ الزِّيَارَةِ وَلَا يَسْعَى بَعْدَهُ لِأَنَّهُ قَدْأَتِي بِذَلِكَ مَرَّةً وَعَلَيْهِ دَمُ التَّمَتُّعِ لِلنَّحْوِ الَّذِى تَلَوْنَاهُ فَإِنْ لَمْ يَجِدُ صَامَ ثَلَثَةَ أَيَّامٍ فِي الْحَجَ وَ سَبْعَةٍ إِذَا رَجَعَ عَلَى الْوَجْهِ الَّذِي بَيَّنَاهُ فِي الْقِرَانِ فَإِنْ صَامَ ثَلَثَةَ أَيَّامٍ مِنْ شَوَّالَ ثُمَّ اعْتَمَرَ لَمْ يَجُزهُ عَنِ الثَّلَثَةِ لَانَّ وُجُوبِ هَذَا الصَّوْمِ التَّمَتَّعُ لِأَنَّهُ بَدَل عَنِ الدَّمِ وَهُوَ فِى هَذِهِ الْحَالَةِ غَيْرُ مُتَمَتِعِ فَلا يَجُوزُ أَدَاءُ هُ قَبْلَ وُجُودِ سَبَبِهِ وَإِنْ صَامَهَا بَعْدَ مَا أَحْرَمَ بِالْعُمْرَةِ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَطُوفَ جَازَ عِنْدَنَا خِلَافًا لِلشَّافِعِي لَهُ قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى ﴿فَصِيَامُ ثَلَثَةِ أَيَّامٍ في الْحَجَ وَلَنَا أَنَّهُ آدَاءُ بَعْدَ الْعِقَادِ سَبَبِهِ وَالْمُرَادُ بِالْحَقِّ الْمَذْكُورِ فِى النَّصِ وَقْتُهُ عَلَى مَا بَيَّنَّا وَالْأَفْضَلُ تَأْخِيرُهَا إلى اخِرِ وَقُتِهَا وَهُوَ يَوْمُ عَرَفَةَ لِمَا بَيَّنَّا فِي الْقِرَانِ

ترجمہ اور اگر اس متمتع نے حج کا احرام باندھ کر منی جانے سے پہلے طواف اور سعی کرلی ہو تو طواف زیارت میں ریل نہیں کرے گا اور نہ اس کے بعد سعی کرے گا کیونکہ وہ ایک بار سعی کر چکا۔ اور متمتع پرتمتع کی قربانی واجب ہے اس نص کی وجہ سے جو ہم تلاوت کر چکے۔ پھر اگر نہ پائے تو حج (کے وقت) میں تین روزے رکھے اور سات روزے رکھے جب وہ لوٹے اس وجہ پر جو ہم قران میں بیان کر چکے۔ اور اگر شوال میں تین روزے رکھے پھر عمرہ کیا تو یہ تمتع کے تین روزوں کی کفایت نہ کریں گے کیونکہ اس روزے کے واجب ہونے کا سبب تمتع ہے کیونکہ روزہ دم کا بدلہ ہے اور وہ اس حالت میں غیر متمتع ہے لہذا روزہ کا ادا کرنا اس کا سبب موجود ہونے سے پہلے جائز نہیں ہے اور اگر عمرہ کا احرام باندھنے کے بعد طواف سے پہلے روزے رکھے تو ہمارے نزدیک جائز ہے امام شافعی کا اختلاف ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول فَصِيَامُ ثَلَثَةِ أَيَّامٍ فِي الْحَج (البقرۃ (۱۹۶) ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ متمتع نے روزوں کو سبب موجود ہونے کے بعد ادا کیا ہے اور حج جو نص میں مذکور ہے اس سے مراد حج کا وقت ہے اس بنا پر جو ہم نے بیان کیا ہے اور آخر وقت تک ان روزوں کو مؤخر کرنا افضل ہے اور وہ یوم عرفہ ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے قران میں بیان کی ہے۔

تشریح سابق میں مذکور ہوا کہ متمتع ارکان عمرہ ادا کرنے کے بعد احرام کھول کر بحالت حلال مکہ میں قیام کرے گا اور جب ذی الحجہ کی آٹھویں تاریخ ہو تو حج کا احرام باندھے گا۔ اب اگر اس متمتع نے حج کا جرام باندھ کر مٹی میں جانے سے پہلے طواف قدوم اور سعی کر لی ہو تو یہ شخص طواف زیارت میں نہ رمل کرے گا اور نہ اس کے بعد سعی کرے گا خواہ طواف قدوم میں رمل کیا ہو یا ریل نہ کیا ہو۔ طواف زیارت کے بعد سعی تو اس لئے نہیں کرے گا کہ سعی طواف قدوم کے بعد ایک بار کر چکا اور سعی میں تکرار نہیں یعنی سعی ایک ہی بار مشروع ہے بار بار مشروع نہیں ہے اس لئے جب طواف قدوم کے بعد ایک بار سعی کر چکا تو طواف زیارت کے بعد سعی نہ کرے اور طواف زیارت میں ریل اس لئے نہ کرے کہ دمل ایسے طواف میں مشروع ہے جس کے بعد سعی ہو اور یہاں طواف زیارت کے بعد سعی موجود نہیں کیونکہ سعی ایک بار پائی گئی اس لئے طواف زیارت میں رمل نہ کرے گا۔ صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ حج تمتع کرنے والے پر تمتع کی قربانی واجب ہے۔ دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول فَمَن تَمَتَعَ بِالْعُمْرَةِ إِلَى الْحَجَ فَمَا اسْتَيْسَرَ مِنَ الْهَدَى (البقرة ١٩٢) ہے۔ اور اگر متمتع ہدی کے جانور کو حاصل کرنے پر قادر نہ ہو تو قارن کی طرح حج کے زمانہ میں تین روزے رکھے اور سات روزے حج سے فراغت پا کر رکھے - تفصیل اور دلیل حج قرآن میں گذر چکی ہے
صاحب قدوری کہتے ہیں کہ ایک شخص جس کا حج تمتع کرنے کا ارادہ ہے اس نے شوال میں تین روزے رکھ لئے پھر عمرہ کا احرام باندھا تو یہ تین روزے قربانی کا بدل ہو کر شرعاً معتبر نہ ہوں گے کیونکہ ان روزوں کے واجب ہونے کا سبب تمتع ہے اور تمتع اس لئے سبب ہے کہ یہ روزے دم تمتع کا بدل ہیں اور عمرہ کا احرام باندھے سے پہلے یہ شخص غیر متمتع ہے تو ان روزوں کا ادا کرنا ان کے وجوب کا سبب موجود ہونے سے پہلے پایا گیا اور سبب موجود ہونے سے پہلے کوئی چیز ادا نہیں ہوتی اس لئے یہ روزے دم تمتع کا بدل ہو کر واقع نہ ہوں گے۔ اور اگر عمرہ کا احرام باندھنے کے بعد طواف سے پہلے ان روزوں کو رکھ لیا تو ہمارے نزدیک جائز ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول فصِيَامُ ثَلثَةِ أَيَّامٍ فِی الْحَج ہے بایں طور کہ آیت میں حج کی حالت میں روزہ رکھنے کا حکم ہے اور حج کی حالت حج کا احرام باندھنے کے بعد شروع ہوتی ہے اس لئے حج کا احرام باندھنے کے بعد ان روزوں کا ادا کرنا جائز ہوگا اس سے پہلے جائز نہ ہوگا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس شخص نے سبب یعنی تمتع کے پائے جانے کے بعد ان روزوں کو ادا کیا اور سبب کے بعد ادا کرنا شرعاً معتبر ہے اس لئے عمرہ کا احرام باندھنے کے بعد یہ روز نے بھی معتبر ہوں گے۔ اور آیت فی الحج میں حج سے مراد فعل حج نہیں بلکہ وقت حج ہے اور حج کا وقت شوال، ذی قعدہ اور ذی الحجہ کے دس یوم ہیں پس وقت حج میں روزے پائے گئے ۔ لیکن افضل یہ ہے کہ ان روزوں کو آخر وقت تک مؤخر کر دیا جائے یعنی خاتمہ ان روزوں کا یوم عرفہ پر ہو اس طرح کہ ۹/۸/۷ ر کا روزہ رکھے۔
And if this mutamatti, after having entered ihram for Hajj, performed tawaf and sa'i before going to Mina, he does not do raml in tawaf al-ziyarah and does not do sa'i after it, because he has already done that once. And upon him is the dam of tamattu' according to the text we recited. Then if he cannot find (an animal), he fasts three days during Hajj and seven when he returns, in the manner we explained in qiran. If he fasts three days in Shawwal and then performed umrah, it does not suffice for the three, because the obligation of this fasting is due to tamattu', as it is a substitute for the blood (sacrifice), and in this state he is not a mutamatti, so it is not permissible to perform it before the existence of its cause. And if he fasts them after he entered ihram for umrah before he performs tawaf, it is valid according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i. His proof is the saying of Allah Most High: 'So fasting three days in Hajj' (2:196). And our proof is that he performed the fasts after the occurrence of its cause, and what is meant by 'Hajj' mentioned in the text is its time, as we explained. And it is better to delay them until the end of its time, which is the Day of Arafah, for the reason we explained in qiran.

Translation: And if this mutamatti, after entering ihram for Hajj, performed tawaf and sa'i before going to Mina, he will not do raml in tawaf al-ziyarah nor will he do sa'i after it, because he has already done sa'i once. And upon the mutamatti is the sacrifice of tamattu' wajib, due to the text we have recited. Then if he does not find (an animal), he fasts three days during Hajj and seven days when he returns, in the manner we explained in qiran. And if he fasts three days in Shawwal then performed umrah, these will not suffice for the three fasts, because the cause for the obligation of these fasts is tamattu', as the fast is a substitute for the blood, and in that state he is not a mutamatti, so performing the fast before the existence of its cause is not permissible. And if he fasts them after entering ihram for umrah before tawaf, it is valid according to us, contrary to Imam al-Shafi'i. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is the saying of Allah Most High: 'So fasting three days in Hajj' (2:196). And our proof is that the mutamatti performed the fasts after the cause existed, and what is meant by 'Hajj' in the text is the time of Hajj, based on what we have explained. And delaying them to the end of its time is better, and that is the Day of Arafah, for the reason we have explained in qiran.

Explanation: It was mentioned earlier that the mutamatti, after performing the acts of Umrah and removing his ihram, stays in Makkah in a state of halal. When the eighth of Dhul-Hijjah arrives, he enters ihram for Hajj. Now if this mutamatti, after entering ihram for Hajj, performed tawaf al-qudum and sa'i before going to Mina, this person will not do raml in tawaf al-ziyarah nor will he do sa'i after it, whether he did raml in tawaf al-qudum or not. He will not do sa'i after tawaf al-ziyarah because he has already performed sa'i once after tawaf al-qudum, and sa'i is not repeated—i.e., sa'i is prescribed only once, not repeatedly. So since he has done sa'i once after tawaf al-qudum, he will not do sa'i after tawaf al-ziyarah. And he will not do raml in tawaf al-ziyarah because raml is prescribed in a tawaf after which sa'i is performed, and here after tawaf al-ziyarah there is no sa'i because sa'i has already been done once. So he will not do raml in tawaf al-ziyarah. Sahib al-Quduri says that upon the one performing Hajj al-Tamattu', the sacrifice of tamattu' is wajib. The proof is the saying of Allah Most High: 'And whoever performs Tamattu' of Umrah to Hajj, then whatever is easy of the sacrificial animal' (2:192). And if the mutamatti is not able to obtain a sacrificial animal, then like the qarin, he fasts three days during the time of Hajj and seven days after completing Hajj—the detail and proof have passed in Hajj al-Qiran.

Sahib al-Quduri says: A person who intends to perform Hajj al-Tamattu' fasts three days in Shawwal then enters ihram for Umrah; these three fasts will not be considered valid as substitutes for the sacrifice, because the cause for the obligation of these fasts is tamattu', and tamattu' is the cause because these fasts are substitutes for the dam of tamattu'. Before entering ihram for Umrah, this person is not a mutamatti, so performing these fasts occurred before the existence of their cause, and nothing can be performed before the existence of its cause. Therefore, these fasts will not count as substitutes for the dam of tamattu'. And if he fasts them after entering ihram for Umrah but before tawaf, then according to us it is valid, and according to Imam al-Shafi'i it is not valid. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is the saying of Allah Most High: 'So fasting three days in Hajj' such that the verse commands fasting in the state of Hajj, and the state of Hajj begins after entering ihram for Hajj. So performing these fasts after entering ihram for Hajj would be permissible, not before. Our proof is that this person performed the fasts after the cause—i.e., tamattu'—had occurred, and performance after the cause is valid according to Shariah. So these fasts are valid after entering ihram for Umrah. And in the verse 'fi al-Hajj', the meaning is not the actions of Hajj but the time of Hajj, and the time of Hajj is Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah. So the fasts occurred within the time of Hajj. However, it is better to delay these fasts to the end of their time, i.e., concluding on the Day of Arafah, such that one fasts on the 7th, 8th, and 9th of Dhu al-Hijjah.
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains the rulings for a mutamatti (one performing Hajj al-Tamattu') who has already performed tawaf and sa'i after entering ihram for Hajj but before going to Mina. The author clarifies two key points: (1) such a person does not perform raml in tawaf al-ziyarah and does not repeat sa'i after it, because sa'i is performed only once in Hajj; raml is only done in a tawaf that is followed by sa'i, and since sa'i is already done, raml is omitted. (2) The mutamatti is obligated to offer a sacrifice (dam) as specified in the Quran (2:196). If unable, he must fast three days during the Hajj season and seven days after returning home, similar to a qarin. The passage then discusses a dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i regarding when these three fasts may be performed. The Hanafi position is that if a person fasts three days in Shawwal before performing Umrah, it does not count because the cause (tamattu') has not yet occurred. However, if he fasts after entering ihram for Umrah but before tawaf, it is valid because the cause (the intention of tamattu') is present. The Shafi'i argument based on the verse 'fi al-Hajj' is countered by the Hanafi interpretation that 'Hajj' here means the time of Hajj (Shawwal to the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah), not the state of ihram. The preferred time is to delay the fasts to the end, culminating on the Day of Arafah. This passage demonstrates the Hanafi reliance on istihsan and careful textual interpretation.

Key Terms
تمتع (tamattu'): A type of Hajj where one performs Umrah first, then removes ihram, and later enters ihram for Hajj in the same year. The mutamatti is obligated to offer a sacrifice.
رمل (raml): Walking briskly with short steps and shoulder movement during tawaf. It is a sunnah for men in the first three rounds.
سعي (sa'i): Walking seven times between Safa and Marwa. Once performed in Hajj, it is not repeated.
دم تمتع (dam al-tamattu'): The obligatory sacrifice (a sheep or goat) required from a mutamatti as thanks for the ease of combining two worships.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for a mutamatti who fasts three days after entering ihram for Umrah but before performing tawaf?
A) It is valid, because the cause (tamattu') exists.
B) It is invalid, because tawaf must be performed first.
C) It is valid only if the fasts are performed before entering ihram.
D) It is invalid, because the fasts must be during the state of Hajj ihram.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits a mutamatti to fast the three days of substitute after ihram for Umrah, interpreting 'fi al-Hajj' as the time of Hajj, not the state of ihram for Hajj.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner

Raml and Sa’ee for Mutamatti’ After Tawaf Ziyarah
Ruling statement on non-repetition of raml and sa’ee

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a mutamatti’ does not perform raml or sa’ee after tawaf ziyarah and explain the underlying principle of non-repetition of sa’ee.

Core Idea
Sa’ee is a single prescribed act in Hajj; once performed, it is not repeated, and raml follows suit.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario for the mutamatti’ pilgrim. After performing tawaf qudūm and sa’ee before proceeding to Minā, the pilgrim might wonder whether these acts need to be repeated after the obligatory tawaf ziyarah. The classical Hanafi ruling, as stated in the text, provides a clear answer based on the fundamental rule that sa’ee is not repeated and raml is only prescribed when sa’ee follows the tawaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The mutamatti’ has performed 'umrah, removed ihrām, and then re-entered ihrām for Hajj on 8th Dhul Hijjah. He performed tawaf qudūm and sa’ee before heading to Minā.
2
State the ruling
After tawaf ziyarah (the obligatory tawaf of Hajj), he does not perform raml (brisk walking) nor sa’ee again.
3
Understand the principle for sa’ee
Sa’ee is a single prescribed act in Hajj; it is not repeated regardless of the number of tawafs performed.
This is based on the established practice of the Prophet ﷺ and the consensus of the Companions.
4
Understand the principle for raml
Raml is prescribed only in a tawaf that is followed by sa’ee. Since sa’ee is not performed after tawaf ziyarah, raml is also omitted.
This holds true whether or not raml was performed in tawaf qudūm.
5
Apply to a variant
If a mutamatti’ forgot to perform sa’ee after tawaf qudūm, then after tawaf ziyarah he must combine both raml and sa’ee, because the condition for raml (sa’ee following) is now met.
This variant reinforces the conditional nature of raml.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح سابق میں مذکور ہوا کہ متمتع ارکان عمرہ ادا کرنے کے بعد احرام کھول کر بحالت حلال مکہ میں قیام کرے گا اور جب ذی الحجہ کی آٹھویں تاریخ ہو تو حج کا احرام باندھے گا۔ اب اگر اس متمتع نے حج کا جرام باندھ کر مٹی میں جانے سے پہلے طواف قدوم اور سعی کر لی ہو تو یہ شخص طواف زیارت میں نہ رمل کرے گا اور نہ اس کے بعد سعی کرے گا خواہ طواف قدوم میں رمل کیا ہو یا ریل نہ کیا ہو۔ طواف زیارت کے بعد سعی تو اس لئے نہیں کرے گا کہ سعی طواف قدوم کے بعد ایک بار کر چکا اور سعی میں تکرار نہیں یعنی سعی ایک ہی بار مشروع ہے بار بار مشروع نہیں ہے اس لئے جب طواف قدوم کے بعد ایک بار سعی کر چکا تو طواف زیارت کے بعد سعی نہ کرے اور طواف زیارت میں ریل اس لئے نہ کرے کہ دمل ایسے طواف میں مشروع ہے جس کے بعد سعی ہو اور یہاں طواف زیارت کے بعد سعی موجود نہیں کیونکہ سعی ایک بار پائی گئی اس لئے طواف زیارت میں رمل نہ کرے گا۔
Explanation: It was mentioned earlier that the mutamatti', after performing the pillars of 'umrah, opens his ihrām and stays in Makkah in a non-muhrim state. When the eighth of Dhul Hijjah arrives, he ties the ihrām for Hajj. Now, if this mutamatti', after tying the ihrām for Hajj, performs tawaf qudūm and sa'y before going to Minā, then he will not perform raml in tawaf ziyārah, nor will he perform sa'y after it, whether he performed raml in tawaf qudūm or not. He will not perform sa'y after tawaf ziyārah because he already performed sa'y once after tawaf qudūm, and sa'y is not repeated—meaning sa'y is prescribed only once, not repeatedly. Therefore, when he has performed sa'y once after tawaf qudūm, he does not perform sa'y after tawaf ziyārah. And he will not perform raml in tawaf ziyārah because raml is prescribed in a tawaf after which sa'y is performed, and here sa'y is not present after tawaf ziyārah because sa'y has already been performed once.
Source pages p. 395

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the commentary. The author clarifies the position of the mutamatti' who has performed tawaf qudūm and sa'y before tawaf ziyārah. The key principle is that sa'y is not repeated in Hajj; once performed, it suffices. Therefore, after tawaf ziyārah (the obligatory tawaf of Hajj), the mutamatti' does not repeat sa'y. Similarly, raml (brisk walking with chest out) in tawaf is only prescribed when sa'y follows that tawaf. Since sa'y is not performed after tawaf ziyārah, raml is also omitted. This applies regardless of whether raml was performed in tawaf qudūm or not.

Key Terms
متمتع (mutamatti'): A person performing tamattu' Hajj, who performs 'umrah first, then after a break performs Hajj in the same year.
طواف قدوم (tawaf qudūm): The tawaf performed upon arrival in Makkah by those entering ihrām for Hajj or 'umrah, before proceeding to Minā.
رمل (raml): Walking briskly with short steps and moving the shoulders in the first three circuits of tawaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a mutamatti' performs tawaf qudūm and sa'y before going to Minā, what should he do regarding sa'y after tawaf ziyārah?
A) He must perform sa'y again because tawaf ziyārah is obligatory.
B) He should not perform sa'y because it is already done once.
C) He may choose to repeat sa'y if he wishes.
D) He must perform sa'y only if he did raml in tawaf qudūm.

Key Takeaway
A mutamatti' who performed sa'y after tawaf qudūm does not repeat sa'y or perform raml after tawaf ziyarah, because sa'y is not repeated and raml requires a following sa'y.

Obligation of Hady and Timing of Substitute Fasts for Tamattu'
Ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that hady is wajib for mutamatti', explain the substitute fasting rules, and apply the Hanafi position on when the three fasts are valid.

Core Idea
Hady is wajib for tamattu'; when unable, fasting must occur after the cause (tamattu') exists, not before.

This passage from Al-Hidayah establishes the obligation of hady for the mutamatti' pilgrim and details the substitute fasting when hady is unavailable. It then addresses a critical timing issue: when exactly may the three fasts be performed? The Hanafi school permits fasting after entering 'umrah ihram, while Imam al-Shafi'i insists on waiting until Hajj ihram. The discussion hinges on interpreting 'during Hajj' in Quran 2:196 as time versus state of ihram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary obligation
State the ruling on hady for tamattu' and cite the Quranic evidence (2:196).
The ruling is wajib according to Hanafi school.
2
Recognize the substitute
When unable to offer hady, a mutamatti' must fast three days during the Hajj season and seven days after returning home. This is analogous to the qarin.
This substitute rule is derived by qiyas on the qarin.
3
Understand the cause (sabab)
The legal cause for the fasting obligation is tamattu' (performing 'umrah and then Hajj in one journey). The cause begins when one ties the ihram for 'umrah. Fasting before that cause is invalid because the obligation does not yet exist.
The author gives the example of fasting in Shawwal before 'umrah ihram – such fasts are not accepted.
4
Compare the dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i interprets 'during Hajj' (in the verse) as 'in the state of Hajj ihram', thus requiring the three fasts to be performed after Hajj ihram. The Hanafi response interprets 'Hajj' as the time of Hajj (Shawwal, Dhul Qa'dah, first ten of Dhul Hijjah), so fasting after 'umrah ihram falls within this time and is valid.
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafi allows fasting after 'umrah ihram; Shafi'i does not.
5
Determine the preferred practice
Although fasting any time after 'umrah ihram within the Hajj season is valid, it is better (afdal) to delay the three fasts to the 7th, 8th, and 9th of Dhul Hijjah.
This aligns the fasts with the end of the Hajj season, culminating on the Day of 'Arafah.

Source Text

صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ حج تمتع کرنے والے پر تمتع کی قربانی واجب ہے۔ دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول فَمَن تَمَتَعَ بِالْعُمْرَةِ إِلَى الْحَجَ فَمَا اسْتَيْسَرَ مِنَ الْهَدَى (البقرة ١٩٢) ہے۔ اور اگر متمتع ہدی کے جانور کو حاصل کرنے پر قادر نہ ہو تو قارن کی طرح حج کے زمانہ میں تین روزے رکھے اور سات روزے حج سے فراغت پا کر رکھے - تفصیل اور دلیل حج قرآن میں گذر چکی ہے۔ صاحب قدوری کہتے ہیں کہ ایک شخص جس کا حج تمتع کرنے کا ارادہ ہے اس نے شوال میں تین روزے رکھ لئے پھر عمرہ کا احرام باندھا تو یہ تین روزے قربانی کا بدل ہو کر شرعاً معتبر نہ ہوں گے کیونکہ ان روزوں کے واجب ہونے کا سبب تمتع ہے اور تمتع اس لئے سبب ہے کہ یہ روزے دم تمتع کا بدل ہیں اور عمرہ کا احرام باندھے سے پہلے یہ شخص غیر متمتع ہے تو ان روزوں کا ادا کرنا ان کے وجوب کا سبب موجود ہونے سے پہلے پایا گیا اور سبب موجود ہونے سے پہلے کوئی چیز ادا نہیں ہوتی اس لئے یہ روزے دم تمتع کا بدل ہو کر واقع نہ ہوں گے۔ اور اگر عمرہ کا احرام باندھنے کے بعد طواف سے پہلے ان روزوں کو رکھ لیا تو ہمارے نزدیک جائز ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول فصِيَامُ ثَلثَةِ أَيَّامٍ فِی الْحَج ہے بایں طور کہ آیت میں حج کی حالت میں روزہ رکھنے کا حکم ہے اور حج کی حالت حج کا احرام باندھنے کے بعد شروع ہوتی ہے اس لئے حج کا احرام باندھنے کے بعد ان روزوں کا ادا کرنا جائز ہوگا اس سے پہلے جائز نہ ہوگا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس شخص نے سبب یعنی تمتع کے پائے جانے کے بعد ان روزوں کو ادا کیا اور سبب کے بعد ادا کرنا شرعاً معتبر ہے اس لئے عمرہ کا احرام باندھنے کے بعد یہ روز نے بھی معتبر ہوں گے۔ اور آیت فی الحج میں حج سے مراد فعل حج نہیں بلکہ وقت حج ہے اور حج کا وقت شوال، ذی قعدہ اور ذی الحجہ کے دس یوم ہیں پس وقت حج میں روزے پائے گئے ۔ لیکن افضل یہ ہے کہ ان روزوں کو آخر وقت تک مؤخر کر دیا جائے یعنی خاتمہ ان روزوں کا یوم عرفہ پر ہو اس طرح کہ ۹/۸/۷ ر کا روزہ رکھے۔
Sahib al-Quduri says: The sacrifice of tamattu' is obligatory upon the one performing tamattu' Hajj. The proof is the statement of Allah Most High: 'And whoever performs 'umrah and then Hajj (tamattu'), then [offer] whatever is easy of the sacrificial animal' (al-Baqarah 2:196). And if the mutamatti' is unable to obtain the sacrificial animal, then he should fast three days during the time of Hajj and seven days after completing Hajj, like the qarin. The details and proof have passed in Hajj Qur'an. Sahib al-Quduri says: If a person who intends to perform tamattu' Hajj fasts three days in Shawwal, then ties the ihrām for 'umrah, these three fasts will not be valid as a substitute for the sacrifice because the cause for these fasts being obligatory is tamattu', and tamattu' is the cause because these fasts are a substitute for the dam of tamattu'. Before tying the ihrām for 'umrah, this person is not a mutamatti', so the performance of these fasts occurred before the existence of their cause, and nothing is performed before the existence of the cause. Therefore, these fasts will not occur as a substitute for the dam of tamattu'. And if he fasts them after tying the ihrām for 'umrah but before tawaf, then according to us (Hanafis) it is permissible, but according to Imam al-Shafi'i it is not permissible. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is the statement of Allah Most High: '...fasting three days during Hajj' (al-Baqarah 2:196), meaning that the verse commands fasting during the state of Hajj, and the state of Hajj begins after tying the ihrām for Hajj. Therefore, fasting after tying the ihrām for Hajj is permissible, before that it is not. Our proof is that this person performed the fasts after the existence of the cause, which is tamattu', and performance after the cause is valid. So these fasts after tying the ihrām for 'umrah are valid. And in the verse 'during Hajj', the meaning of Hajj is not the actions of Hajj but the time of Hajj, and the time of Hajj is Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the first ten of Dhu al-Hijjah. Thus, the fasts occurred within the time of Hajj. However, it is better to delay these fasts to the end of the time, i.e., the last of them being the Day of 'Arafah, such that he fasts the 7th, 8th, and 9th.
Source pages p. 395

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, including an inter-madhhab dispute. Sahib al-Quduri first states that the tamattu' sacrifice (hady) is wajib, citing the Quran (2:196). If unable, substitute fasting: three days during the Hajj season and seven after returning home. The key discussion is about the timing of the three fasts. If one fasts before tying the ihrām for 'umrah, those fasts are invalid because tamattu' has not yet occurred—the cause (sabab) is not present. The Hanafi position, supported by Abu Hanifa, is that fasting after tying the ihrām for 'umrah (but before tawaf) is valid because the cause (tamattu') exists after entering ihram. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that 'during Hajj' means the state of ihram for Hajj, not for 'umrah. The Hanafi response interprets 'Hajj' as the time of Hajj (Shawwal to 10th of Dhul Hijjah), so fasting in this period after 'umrah ihram is acceptable. The preferred time is the last days before 'Arafah.

Key Terms
ہدی (hady): The sacrificial animal (camel, cow, or sheep) sent to the Haram by pilgrims, especially in tamattu' and qiran.
تمتع (tamattu'): Performing 'umrah during the Hajj season and then Hajj in the same year with a break in between.
سبب (sabab): Legal cause that triggers an obligation. In this context, tamattu' (the act of combining 'umrah and Hajj) is the cause for the obligation of hady or substitute fasting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is it valid for a mutamatti' to fast the three substitute days?
A) Only after tying the ihrām for Hajj.
B) At any time during Shawwal, even before 'umrah ihram.
C) After tying the ihrām for 'umrah, any time during the Hajj season.
D) Only on the 7th, 8th, and 9th of Dhul Hijjah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that the substitute fasts for tamattu' are valid when performed after 'umrah ihram within the Hajj season, based on interpreting 'during Hajj' as the time of Hajj.

Driving the Hady: Taqlid, Talbiyah, and Mode of Leading
Procedure for mutamatti' driving a hady

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended actions for a mutamatti' who drives a hady and explain why taqlid is preferred over tajlil.

Core Idea
For hady, taqlid (garland) is better than tajlil (covering) because it is Quranic and serves as a clear sign.

When performing Tamattu', it is commendable to bring a sacrificial animal (hady). The Hanafi school details the proper procedure, emphasizing that driving the hady is superior to not doing so, and that taqlid (garlanding) is better than covering. This lesson unpacks the sequence and reasoning from the text of al-Quduri.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a mutamatti' driving a hady. The ruling is mustahabb (recommended), based on the Prophet's practice.
It is not wajib; it is a sunnah muakkadah.
2
Understand the sequence of actions
The mutamatti' enters ihram, then drives the hady. For a camel (badanah), he performs taqlid with a leather strip or sandal. He recites talbiyah before taqlid, as taqlid alone can make him muhrim, but talbiyah is preferred.
Taqlid is done after ihram, not before.
3
Distinguish taqlid from tajlil
Taqlid is putting a garland on the animal; tajlil is covering it. Taqlid is better because it is mentioned in the Quran (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:97) and serves to notify people that the animal is for sacrifice, while tajlil is for adornment.
The word 'al-qala'id' in the Quran refers to garlanded animals.
4
Choose the mode of leading
It is better to drive the animal from behind (sawn) rather than leading it from the front, because the Prophet's hady was driven before him, and it makes the animal more conspicuous. If the animal refuses, leading is allowed.
Driving from behind emphasizes the sacrificial nature.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن أرَادَ المُتَمَعُ أنْ يَسُوق الْهَدَى أَحْرَمَ وَ سَاقَ هَدْيَهُ وَهَذَا أَفَضَلَّ لأنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ سَاقَ الهَدَايَا مَعَ نَفْسِهِ وَلانَّ فِيهِ اسْتِعْدَادٌ أَوْ مُسَارَعَةٌ فَإِنْ كَانَتْ بَدَنَةً قَلَّدَهَا بِمَزَادَةٍ أَوْ نَعْلِ لِحَدِيثِ عَائِشَةَ عَلَى مَا رَوَيْنَاهُ وَالتَّقْلِيد أولى مِنَ التَّجْلِيْلِ لِأَنَّ لَهُ ذِكْرًا فِى الْكِتَابِ وَلانَّهُ لِلاعْلَامِ وَالتَّجْلِيلُ لِلزَيْنَةِ وَيُلبّى ثُمَّ يُقَدِّدُ لأنَّهُ يَصِيرُ مُحْرمًا بِتَقْلِيدِ الْهَدَى وَالتَّوَجَهِ مَعَهُ عَلَى مَا سَبَقَ وَالأولى أنْ يَعْقِدَ الْإِحْرَامَ بالتَّلْبِيَّةِ وَيَسُوق الْهَدَى وَهُوَ أفضل أن يُقُوْدَهَا لِأَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ أحْرَم بذِي الْحُلَيْفَةِ وَهَدَايَاهُ تُسَاقُ بَيْنَ يَدَيْهِ وَلانَّهُ ابْلَعُ فِى الشهير إِلَّا أَنْ لَا تَنْقَادُ فَحِينَئِذٍ يَقُودُهَا۔
And if the mutamatti' wants to drive the hady, he should enter ihram and drive his hady. This is better because the Prophet (peace be upon him) drove the hady with himself, and because in it there is preparedness or haste. Then if it is a badanah (camel), he should put a taqlid (garland) on it with a leather strip or a sandal, due to the hadith of 'A'ishah as we have narrated. And taqlid is better than covering (tajlil) because it is mentioned in the Book, and because it is for notification, while covering is for adornment. He should say talbiyah then make taqlid, because he becomes muhrim by making taqlid of the hady and proceeding with it, as previously mentioned. And it is better that he tie the ihram with talbiyah and drive the hady, and it is better to drive it from behind (yasūquhā) rather than leading it (yaqūduhā), because the Prophet (peace be upon him) entered ihram at Dhul Hulaifah while his hady was driven before him, and because it is more effective in making it known, unless it does not obey, in which case he may lead it.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proofs from sunnah. The author, quoting Sahib al-Quduri, explains that if a mutamatti' wishes to bring a sacrificial animal (hady), he should tie ihrām for 'umrah and drive the animal along. This act is superior because the Prophet himself did so, and it demonstrates eagerness. For a camel (badanah), he should put a garland (taqlid) made of leather or a sandal around its neck, following the practice of the Prophet. Taqlid is better than covering the animal with a cloth because taqlid is mentioned in the Quran (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:97) and serves as a clear sign that it is a sacrificial animal, while covering is more for adornment. The sequence: he should first recite talbiyah and then perform taqlid, as taqlid alone can make him muhrim (if done with intention). However, it is better to use talbiyah because it is the original method. Regarding how to drive the animal, driving it from behind (sawn) is superior to leading it from the front, because the Prophet's hady was driven before him, and this makes the animal more conspicuous to the people. Only if the animal refuses to move, he may lead it from the front.

Key Terms
بدنہ (badanah): A camel (or cow) that is marked for sacrifice in the Haram.
تقلید (taqlid): Placing a garland or mark around the neck of the sacrificial animal to indicate it is hady.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is taqlid (garlanding) preferred over tajlil (covering) for a hady animal?
A) Because covering is not allowed in ihram.
B) Because taqlid is mentioned in the Quran and serves as a clear sign, while covering is for adornment.
C) Because taqlid is easier to apply.
D) Because the Prophet only did taqlid and never covered.

Key Takeaway
Driving hady, performing taqlid, and driving from behind are all sunan muakkadah for the mutamatti'.

Preferable Practices for Leading and Marking the Hadi
States ruling that driving the hadi is superior, taqlid over covering, and driving from behind.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the preferred methods for a mutamatti' pilgrim regarding leading the hadi and marking it, and explain the evidence for each preference.

Core Idea
Driving the hadi from behind, marking it with a garland, and reciting talbiyah first are recommended sunnah acts.

In this lesson, based on the commentary of Al-Hidayah and Al-Quduri, we explore the preferred practices for a mutamatti' pilgrim who brings a sacrificial animal (hadi). The text explains why personal driving, taqlid, and leading from behind are superior, citing the Prophet's actions and Quranic mention. Understanding these details helps a pilgrim follow the sunnah more fully.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and ruling level
List the three main acts discussed: driving the hadi, marking it (taqlid vs. covering), and the manner of leading (from behind vs. pulling). Determine that each is recommended (sunnah muakkadah) based on the Prophet's practice.
The ruling is not obligatory (wajib) but preferred (afdal).
2
Locate the dalil for each act
For driving the hadi, the text cites the hadith of Jabir in Sahih Muslim about the Prophet driving his animals. For taqlid, it cites Aisha's hadith and Quranic verse (Al-Ma'idah 5:97). For leading from behind, the Prophet's practice at Dhul-Hulaifah is proof.
These are ahad hadiths, thus zanni al-thubut, indicating sunnah not fard.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's consistent action (fi'l) demonstrates the desirability of these acts. For taqlid, the Quranic mention of 'qala'id' indicates its significance over covering.
Covering (jul) may serve comfort, so taqlid is a purer sign of sacrifice.
4
Note the superiority of one practice over another
Taqlid is better than covering because it is mentioned in the Quran and is a definitive mark. Leading from behind is better than pulling because it publicizes the hadi more effectively, as the Prophet did.
If the animal is stubborn, pulling from front is permissible.
5
Consider the sequence and exception
The recommended sequence is: first recite talbiyah, then perform taqlid. Talbiyah is primary; taqlid is secondary. Exception: if the animal does not move when driven, it may be pulled from the front.
This shows flexibility within the sunnah.

ترجمہ اور اگر متمتع ہدی کا جانور چلانا چاہے تو احرام باندھے اور اپنی ہدی چلائے اور یہ افضل ہے کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اپنے ساتھ اپنے ہدی کے جانوروں کو چلایا اور اس لئے کہ ہدی چلانے میں سامان خیر اور جلدی ہے۔ پھر اگر ہدی ، بد نہ ہو تو اس کو چمڑے کے ٹکڑتے یا جوتی کے ساتھ قلادہ پہنا دے۔ دلیل حدیث عائشہ ہے جیسا کہ ہم روایت کر چکے۔ اور قلادہ پہنا نا جھول ڈالنے سے بہتر ہے کیونکہ قلائد کا ذکر قرآن پاک میں ہے اور اس لئے کہ تقلید کرنا آگاہ کرنے کے لئے اور جھول ڈالنا زینت کے لئے ہے۔ اور تلبیہ کہے پھر تقلید کرے۔ اس لئے کہ یہ شخص ہدی کو تقلید کرنے اور اس کے ساتھ متوجہ ہونے سے محروم ہو جائے گا۔ چنانچہ سابق میں بیان ہو چکا اور بہتر یہ ہے کہ تلبیہ سے احرام باندھے اور بدی کو ہانکے اور ہانکنا اسکو کھینچنے سے افضل ہے۔ کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ذوالحلیفہ میں احرام باندھا اور آپ کے ہدایا آپ کے سامنے ہانکے جاتے تھے۔ اور اس لئے کہ شہرت دینے میں یہ زیادہ بلیغ ہے۔ لیکن اگر ہدی انقیاد نہ کرے تو اس وقت آگے سے کھینچے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ متمتع اگر ہدی کو لے جانا چاہے تو عمرہ کا احرام باندھے اور اپنے ہدی کو ہی کا کر لے جائے ۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ متمتع کا ہدی کو ساتھ لے جانانہ لے جانے سے افضل ہے کیونکہ اللہ کا رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم اپنے ساتھ ہدی کے جانوروں کو لے کر چلا تھا۔ جیسا کہ مسلم میں حدیث جابر صلى الله عليه وسلم سے ظاہر ہے اور دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ہدی کو ساتھ لے کر چلنے میں خیر کی تیاری اور واجب ادا کرنے میں جلدی ہے اور یہ دونوں باتیں محمود ہیں اس لئے ہدی کو ساتھ لے جانا نہ لے جانے سے افضل ہے۔ اب اگر ہدی کا جانور بدنہ یعنی اونٹ یا گائے ہو تو اس کے گلے میں چمڑے کے ٹکڑے یا جوتی کے ٹکڑے کا قلادہ ڈال دے۔ جیسا کہ حديث عائشہ كُنتُ افْتِلُ قَلائِدَ هَدَى رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم سے ظاہر ہے۔ صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ ہدی کو جھول پہنانے کی بہ نسبت ، قلادہ پہنانا بہتر ہے۔ دلیل اولویت یہ ہے کہ قلائد کا ذکر قرآن پاک میں ہے چنانچہ ارشاد ہے جَعَلَ اللهُ الْكَعْبَةَ الْبَيْتَ الْحَرَامَ قِيَامًا لِلنَّاسِ وَالشَّهْرَ الْحَرَامَ وَالْهَدَى وَالقَلائِد - (المائدۃ: ۹۷) دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ تقلید فقط ہدی کا جانور ہونے کی خبر دینے کے لئے ہے اس کے سوا کوئی دوسرا فائدہ نہیں ہے۔ اور جھول ڈالنا زینت کے لئے بھی ہوتا ہے اور گرمی اور سردی کو دور کرنے کے لئے بھی ہوتا ہے۔ پس تقلید بلا کسی احتمال کے بدی ہونے کی علامت ہے اور جھول ڈالنا قطعی علامت نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے تقلید ، جھول ڈالنے سے اولیٰ اور بہتر ہے۔ صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ پہلے تلبیہ سے احرام باندھے پھر تقلید کرے کیونکہ ہدی کو تقلید کرنے اور اس کے ساتھ متوجہ ہونے سے محرم تو ہو جائے گا۔ جیسا کہ پہلے گزر چکا لیکن بہتر یہ ہے کہ تلبیہ کہہ کر احرام باند ھے۔ کیونکہ تلبیہ اصل ہے اور تقلید اس کے قائم مقام ہے اور بصورت امکان اصل پر عمل کرنا اولیٰ ہے اس لئے تلبیہ کے ساتھ احرام کو شروع کرنا اولی ہو گا۔ صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ ہدی کو پیچھے سے ہنکا کر لے جانا بہتر ہے بمقابلہ اس کو آگے سے بھینچ کر لے جانے کے۔ کیونکہ اللہ کے نبی صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ذوالحلیفہ میں احرام باندھا اور آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے ہدی کے جانور آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے آگے سے ہنکائے جاتے تھے ۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ تقلید ہدی سے مقصود اس کو عوام میں شہرت دینا ہے۔ اور ہنکا کر لے جانے میں یہ بات زیادہ حاصل ہے اس لئے ہنگا کر لے جانا ہی افضل ہے۔ ہاں اگر ہدی کا جانور ہانکنے سے نہ چلے تو ایسی صورت میں اس کو آگے سے پکڑ کر کھینچا جا سکتا ہے۔ اس میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔
Translation: If a mutamatti' wants to drive the sacrificial animal, he should enter ihram and drive his hadi, and this is better because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) drove his sacrificial animals with him, and because driving the hadi involves preparation for good and haste. Then if the hadi is a badanah (camel or cow), he should put a garland of a piece of leather or a sandal around its neck. The proof is the hadith of Aisha as we have narrated. Garlanding is better than covering because garlands are mentioned in the Quran, and because taqlid is for notification while covering is for adornment. He should say the talbiyah then do taqlid, because the person will be deprived of doing taqlid to the hadi and directing it. As has been stated earlier, it is better to enter ihram with talbiyah and drive the hadi from behind, and driving it from behind is better than pulling it from the front because the Prophet (peace be upon him) entered ihram at Dhul-Hulaifah and his sacrificial animals were driven before him, and because this is more effective in publicizing. But if the hadi is not compliant, then it may be pulled from the front. Explanation: The issue is that if a mutamatti' wants to take the hadi, he should enter ihram for Umrah and take his hadi with him. The author of Hidayah has said that the mutamatti' taking the hadi with him is better than not taking it, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) took his sacrificial animals with him, as is clear from the hadith of Jabir in Muslim. The second proof is that taking the hadi involves preparation for good and haste in performing the obligation, both of which are praiseworthy. Therefore, taking the hadi is better than not taking it. If the hadi is a badanah (camel or cow), put a garland of a piece of leather or a sandal around its neck, as is clear from the hadith of Aisha: 'I used to twist the garlands for the sacrificial animals of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him).' Al-Quduri states that garlanding is better than covering. The first proof is that garlands are mentioned in the Quran, as Allah says: 'Allah has made the Ka'bah, the Sacred House, a means of support for mankind, and the sacred month, and the sacrificial animals, and the garlands.' (Al-Ma'idah: 97) The second proof is that taqlid is only for informing that it is a sacrificial animal, with no other benefit. Covering is for adornment and for warding off heat and cold. Therefore, taqlid is an unequivocal mark of being a sacrificial animal, while covering is not a definitive mark. Hence, taqlid is superior to covering. Al-Quduri states: First, enter ihram with talbiyah, then do taqlid, because by doing taqlid to the hadi and directing it, the person will become a muhrim. As previously mentioned, but it is better to enter ihram by reciting talbiyah, because talbiyah is the original practice and taqlid is its substitute, and when possible, acting on the original is better. Therefore, beginning ihram with talbiyah is better. Al-Quduri states: Driving the hadi from behind is better than pulling it from the front, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) entered ihram at Dhul-Hulaifah and his sacrificial animals were driven before him. The second proof is that the purpose of taqlid is to publicize the hadi among the people, and driving it from behind achieves this more effectively. Therefore, driving from behind is superior. However, if the hadi does not move by driving, then it may be pulled from the front; there is no harm in that.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah (Ashraf Al-Hidayah) deals with the rulings for a mutamatti' pilgrim who brings a sacrificial animal (hadi) to be slaughtered in Mina. The commentary expands on the original matn of Al-Hidayah and incorporates the rulings of Al-Quduri. The first part establishes that it is preferable (afdal) for the mutamatti' to drive his hadi himself rather than leave it behind. Proof is taken from the Prophet's own practice during his farewell pilgrimage. The second part discusses how to mark the animal: if it is a camel or cow (badanah), a garland (qiladah) of leather or a sandal piece is placed around its neck. The commentary cites the hadith of Aisha who used to prepare such garlands. A comparison is made between garlanding (taqlid) and covering the animal with a cloth (jul). Taqlid is considered superior because it is mentioned in the Quran (Al-Ma'idah: 97) and serves the clear purpose of identifying the animal as a sacrifice, whereas covering may also serve comfort. The next ruling concerns the sequence: the pilgrim should first recite talbiyah, then perform taqlid. Talbiyah is the primary act of ihram, and taqlid is secondary. Finally, the preferred method of leading the animal is driving it from behind, as the Prophet did. Only if the animal is stubborn may it be pulled from the front. The commentary is structured as a tashrih (explanation) of the matn, providing additional juristic reasoning and hadith evidence.

Key Terms
ہدی (hadi): The sacrificial animal brought to the Haram by a pilgrim, especially for tamattu' and qiran.
تقلید (taqlid): Placing a garland (qiladah) around the neck of the sacrificial animal to mark it.
بدنہ (badanah): A camel or cow; animals large enough to be garlanded and marked.
تلبیہ (talbiyah): The recitation 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' which is the essential utterance of ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the preferred method of leading a sacrificial animal for a mutamatti' pilgrim?
A) Pulling it from the front
B) Driving it from behind
C) Leaving it to be carried by someone else
D) Neither; the hadi should not be led but left at the miqat

Key Takeaway
For a mutamatti' pilgrim, the sunnah is to personally drive the hadi from behind, mark it with a garland (taqlid), and recite talbiyah before marking.

The Ish'ar Dispute: Makruh or Hasan?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ish'ar of the camel

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on ish'ar, identify the proofs for each, and explain why the later Hanafi position favors the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Ish'ar is makruh to Abu Hanifa but hasan to the Sahibayn – a clash between prohibition of muthlah and prophetic practice.

This lesson examines a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the practice of ish'ar – incising the hump of the sacrificial camel to mark it. Imam Abu Hanifa considers it makruh because it resembles muthlah (mutilation), which is prohibited. The two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, consider it hasan (good) because it effectively marks the animal and is reported from the Prophet and caliphs. We will unpack the reasoning behind each position and see how later Hanafi jurists resolved the conflict.

Guided Path
1
State the Ikhtilaf
Identify the two positions: Abu Hanifa says ish'ar is makruh; the Sahibayn say it is hasan. Note that the Shafi'i school considers it sunnah.
This is an intra-madhhab dispute within the Hanafi school.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's Proof
Abu Hanifa argues that ish'ar is a form of muthlah (mutilation), which is prohibited generally. Since the purpose of marking can be achieved through taqlid (garlanding) without injury, ish'ar is disliked.
The general prohibition of muthlah takes precedence over the specific practice.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's Proof
The Sahibayn argue that ish'ar is more effective than taqlid in achieving the goals of marking the hadi: preventing disturbance and enabling recovery if lost. They also cite the Prophet's own practice and that of the caliphs.
They acknowledge the muthlah concern but consider the benefit outweighs it, hence 'hasan' not 'sunnah'.
4
Examine the Hanafi Response
The Hidayah commentary explains that the Prophet's ish'ar was a special measure due to polytheist interference. In normal circumstances, the prohibition of muthlah prevails. Later scholars also suggest Abu Hanifa's ruling was specific to his time's excesses.
The tarjih (preference) in the school leans towards the Sahibayn for general practice.
5
Apply the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical difference: following Abu Hanifa, only taqlid should be done for camels; following the Sahibayn, ish'ar is permissible and recommended. Mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view.
Even those following the Sahibayn should avoid excessive wounding that risks infection.

قَالَ وَأَشْعَرَ الْبُدْنَةَ عِنْدَ أَبِى يُوْسَفَ وَ مُحَمَّدٍ وَلَا يُشْعِرُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَيَكْرَهُ وَالْإِشْعَارُ هُوَ الْإِدْمَاء بِالْجَرْحِ لُغَةً وَ صِفَتهُ أنْ يَشُقَ سِنَامُهَا بِأنْ يَطْعَنَ فِي أَسْفَلِ السَّامِ مِنَ الْجَانِبِ الْأَيْمَنِ قَالُوا وَالأشْبَهُ هُوَ الْأَيْسَرُ لأنَّ النبى عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ طَعَنَ فِي جَانِبِ الْيَسَارِ مَقْصُودَ اوَ فِي جَانِبِ الْأَيْمَنِ إِتِّفَاقًا وَيَلْطَحُ سِنَامَهَا بِالدَّمِ إِعْلَامًا وَهَذَا الصُّنَعُ مَكْرُوهُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَعِندَهُمَا حَسَنُ وَعِندَ الشَّافِعِي سُنة لأنَّهُ مَرْوِيٌّ عَنِ النَّبِي عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ وَعَن الْحُلَفَاءِ وَلَهُمَا إِنَّ الْمَقْصُودَ مِنَ التَّقْلِيدِ أنْ لَايُهَاجَ إِذَا وَرَدَمَاء أَوْ كَلَا اَوْيُرَدُّ إِذَا ضَلَّ وَإِنَّهُ فِي الْإِشْعَارِ اتَهُ لِأَنَّهُ الرمُ فَمِنْ هَذَا الْوَجْهِ يَكُونُ سُنَّةً إِلَّا إِنَّهُ عَارَضَتْهُ جِهَهُ كُونِهِ مُثْلَةَ فَقُلْنَا بِحُسْنِهِ وَلا بِي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّهُ مُثْلَةٌ وَأَنَّهُ مَنْهِى عَنْهُ وَلَوْ وَقَعَ التَّعَارُضُ فَالتَّرْجِيحُ لِلْمُحَرِمِ وَإِشْعَارُ النَّى عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لِصَيَانَةِ الْهَدَى لِأَنَّ الْمُشْرِكِيْنَ لَا يَمْنَعُونَ عَنْ تَعَرُّضِهِ إِلَّا بِهِ وَقِيلَ إِنَّ أَبَا حَنِيفَةَ كَرَة إِشْعَارَ أَهْلِ زَمَانِهِ لِمُبَا لَغَتِهِمْ فِيهِ عَلَى وَجهِ يُخَافُ مِنْهُ السّرَايَةُ وَقِيلَ إِنَّمَا كَرِهَ أَبْنَارَهُ عَلَى التَّقْلِيدِ
ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا اور ابو یوسف اور امام محمد کے نزدیک بدنہ کو اشعار کرے اور ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اشعار نہ کرے اور اشعار مکروہ ۔۔ اور اشعار لغت میں زخم لگ کر خون نکالنے کا نام ہے۔ اور اشعار کی کیفیت یہ ہے کہ بدنہ کی کو ہان پھاڑ دے بائیں طور کہ دائیں جانب وبان کے اسفل میں نیز ہمارے۔ متأخرین نے کہا کہ زیادہ مشابہ بایاں کو بہان ہے۔ کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بائیں جانب بالقصد نیزہ مارا اور دائیں جانب اتفاقا مارا اور اس کے بدی کا جانور ہونے کی اطلاع کے لئے اسکے کو بان کو خون سے آلودہ کر دے۔ اور یہ عمل ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک مکروہ ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اچھا ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک سنت ہے۔ کیونکہ اشعار رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم اور خلفاء راشدین سے مروی ہے اور صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ تقلید کا مقصود یہ ہے کہ ہدی کا جانور جب پانی یا گھاس پر جائے تو اس کو دھتکارا نہ جائے یا جب گم ہو جائے تو اس کو واپس لوٹا دیا جائے۔ اور یہ معنی اشعار میں اتم ہیں کیونکہ اشعار الزم ہے پس اسی وجہ سے سنت ہوگا لیکن چونکہ اس کو مثلہ ہونے کی جانب معارض ہو گئی اس لئے ہم اس کے حسن ہونے کے قائل ہو گئے اور ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ مثلہ ہے اور منہی عنہ ہے اور رانی رض واقع ہو تو ترجیح محرم کو ہوتی ہے اور رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا اشعار ہدی کی حفاظت کے لئے تھا اس لئے کہ مشرکین ہدی کے ساتھ تعرض کرنے سے باز نہیں آتے تھے مگر اشعار کے ساتھ ۔ اور کہا گیا کہ ابو حنیفہ نے اپنے زمانہ والوں کا اشعار مکروہ قرار دیا ہے کیونکہ وہ لوگ اشعار میں ایسے طریقہ پر مبالغہ کرتے تھے کہ اس سے سرایت کا خوف ہوتا۔ اور کہا گیا کہ اشعار کو تقلید پر ترجیح دینا مکروہ قرار دیا ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ بدی کا جانور اگر بکری یا بھیڑ ہو تو بالا تفاق اس کو اشعار نہ کرے اور اگر بد نہ یعنی اونٹ یا گائے ہو تو صاحبین کے نزدیک اس کو اشعار کیا جائے گا اور امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اس کو اشعار کرنا مکروہ ہے۔ لغت میں اشعار، زخم لگا کر خون نکالنے کا نام ہے۔ اور طریقہ یہ ہے کہ دائیں جانب کو بان کے نیچے نیزہ مار کر اس کو پھاڑ دے۔ علما ، متاخرین فرماتے ہیں کہ درستگی کے زیادہ مشابہ بائیں جانب ہے یعنی بائیں جانب اشعار کرنا زیادہ اچھا ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم سے دونوں جانب اشعار کرنا مروی ہے مگر آپ نے بائیں جانب بالقصد نیزہ مارا۔ اور دائیں جانب اتفاقا مارا۔ اور یہ ظاہر ہے کہ پیغمبر جو کام بالقصد کرتا ہے امت کے لئے وہی قابل اتباع ہوتا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اشعار کرتے وقت خون سے اس جانور کے کو ہان کولت پت کر دے تا کہ لوگ سمجھ جائیں کہ
He said: And one should make ish'ar to the badanah according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, but according to Abu Hanifa he should not make ish'ar, and it is makruh. Ish'ar lexically means causing blood to flow by wounding. Its description is that one splits its hump by stabbing in the lower part of the hump from the right side. They (the later scholars) said: The more similar is the left side, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) stabbed the left side intentionally and the right side incidentally. And he smears its hump with blood as a mark. This act is makruh according to Abu Hanifa, good (hasan) according to them (the Sahibayn), and sunnah according to al-Shafi'i, because it is reported from the Prophet and the caliphs. Their (the Sahibayn's) proof is that the purpose of taqlid is that it should not be driven away when it comes to water or grass, or that it should be returned if it is lost, and this is more perfect in ish'ar because ish'ar is more binding. Therefore from this perspective it is sunnah, but the aspect of it being a muthlah (mutilation) opposes it, so we said it is hasan. Abu Hanifa's proof is that it is a muthlah and that it is prohibited. And when there is a conflict, preference is given to the prohibitor. And the Prophet's ish'ar was for the protection of the hadi, because the polytheists would not refrain from molesting it except by it. And it is said that Abu Hanifa disliked ish'ar for the people of his time because of their excess in it in a way that caused fear of infection. And it is said that he disliked preferring ish'ar over taqlid. Translation: Al-Quduri said: According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, one should make ish'ar to the badanah, and according to Abu Hanifa, one should not make ish'ar and it is makruh. Ish'ar lexically means causing blood to flow by wounding. The method of ish'ar is to split the hump of the badanah, meaning to stab in the lower part of the hump from the right side. Our later scholars said that the more similar is the left side, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) intentionally stabbed the left side and accidentally the right side. And to inform that it is a sacrificial animal, he smears its hump with blood. This act is makruh according to Abu Hanifa, good according to the Sahibayn, and sunnah according to Imam al-Shafi'i, because ish'ar is reported from the Prophet and the rightly-guided caliphs. The proof of the Sahibayn is that the purpose of taqlid is that the hadi should not be driven away when it goes to water or grass, or that it should be returned if lost, and this meaning is more perfect in ish'ar because ish'ar is more binding. So from this aspect it is sunnah, but because it is opposed by the aspect of being a muthlah, we said it is hasan. Abu Hanifa's proof is that it is a muthlah and that it is prohibited. And when there is conflict, preference is given to the prohibitor. The Prophet's ish'ar was for the protection of the hadi, because the polytheists would not refrain from interfering with it except by that. And it is said that Abu Hanifa disliked ish'ar for the people of his time because of their excess in it in a way that caused fear of infection. And it is said that he disliked preferring ish'ar over taqlid. Explanation: The issue is that if the sacrificial animal is a goat or sheep, by consensus ish'ar is not done. If it is a badanah (camel or cow), according to the Sahibayn ish'ar will be done, and according to Imam Abu Hanifa ish'ar is makruh. Lexically, ish'ar means causing blood to flow by wounding. The method is to stab the right side of the hump at its base and split it. The later scholars say that the more correct side is the left, i.e., ish'ar on the left side is better. The proof is that ish'ar on both sides is reported from the Prophet, but he intentionally stabbed the left side and accidentally the right side. And it is clear that the action done intentionally by the Prophet is the one to be followed by the ummah. The author of Hidayah says that when doing ish'ar, one should smear the hump with blood so that people understand that
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf Al-Hidayah addresses the controversial practice of ish'ar for the sacrificial camel (badanah). Ish'ar is the act of making an incision on the hump of the camel to draw blood, which serves as a distinctive mark. The passage begins by quoting the matn of Al-Hidayah: 'He said: And one should make ish'ar to the badanah according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, but according to Abu Hanifa he should not make ish'ar, and it is makruh.' The commentary then defines ish'ar linguistically and describes the procedure. A key intra-madhhab ikhtilaf (dispute) is presented: Imam Abu Hanifa considers ish'ar makruh (disliked) due to its resemblance to muthlah (mutilation), which is prohibited in Islam. In contrast, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) consider it hasan (good) because it achieves the purpose of marking the animal more effectively than taqlid (garlanding). The Shafi'i school, represented by Imam al-Shafi'i, goes further, considering it sunnah based on the practice of the Prophet and the caliphs. The commentary provides the reasoning for each position. The Sahibayn argue that ish'ar is more binding and thus more effective for the intended purpose: preventing the animal from being disturbed and ensuring it can be identified if lost. However, they concede that the concern regarding muthlah leads them to rate it as hasan rather than sunnah. Abu Hanifa's argument rests on the prohibition of muthlah, and that any conflict between a recommended act and a prohibition must be resolved in favor of the prohibition. The Prophet's own ish'ar is explained as a special measure needed because polytheists would otherwise interfere with the animals. Later scholars offered two reconciliations: Abu Hanifa's dislike may have been specific to the people of his time who overdid ish'ar, risking infection, or he disliked preferring ish'ar over taqlid, not ish'ar itself. The passage concludes with a consensus that ish'ar is not done for sheep or goats; for camels, the Sahibayn permit it, and the later scholars recommend the left side as the more precise following of the Prophet's intentional action.

Key Terms
اشعار (ish'ar): The act of making an incision on the hump of a camel to draw blood, used as a distinctive mark for the sacrificial animal.
مثلہ (muthlah): Mutilation or disfigurement of a living animal, which is prohibited in Islamic law.
بدنہ (badanah): A camel (and by extension a cow) used as a sacrificial animal, typically for pilgrimage.
تقلید (taqlid): Placing a garland around the animal's neck; an alternative method of marking the sacrificial animal that is not considered muthlah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason Imam Abu Hanifa considers ish'ar makruh?
A) It is not mentioned in the Quran
B) It is a form of muthlah (mutilation), which is prohibited
C) It was not practiced by the Prophet
D) It causes the animal to become invalid for sacrifice

Key Takeaway
Ish'ar on a sacrificial camel is an intra-Hanafi dispute where Abu Hanifa rules it makruh due to muthlah, while the Sahibayn rule it hasan; the mufta bihi follows the Sahibayn.

The Hanafi Dispute on Ish'ar (Marking the Sacrificial Animal)
Inter-madhhab dispute on ish'ar among Hanafi imams and Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on ish'ar (cutting the hump of a camel/cow) and explain the reasoning behind Abu Hanifa's ruling of makruh and the Sahibayn's ruling of hasan.

Core Idea
Ish'ar is makruh due to mutilation; Sahibayn allow it as hasan for stronger identification.

In this lesson, we examine the disagreement among Hanafi imams on the ruling of ish'ar—cutting the hump of a sacrificial camel or cow and smearing blood to mark it. While al-Shafi'i considers it a sunnah, the Hanafi school has internal divergence. You will see how Abu Hanifa prioritizes the prohibition of mutilation (muthla) over the prophetic example, while the Sahibayn reconcile both aspects by classifying it as hasan. This passage from al-Hidayah illustrates the Islamic legal methodology of weighing conflicting proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed act
Understand what ish'ar means: cutting the hump of a camel or cow (badanah) and smearing blood to mark it as a sacrificial animal (hadi). Note that it applies only to camels/cows, not sheep/goats.
2
State the three positions
Abu Hanifa: makruh; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn): hasan (jai'z, permissible); al-Shafi'i: sunnah. Also note that the majority (Malik, Ahmad) side with Shafi'i.
3
Examine the proofs
Al-Shafi'i relies on reports from the Prophet (ﷺ) and the Rightly Guided Caliphs. The Sahibayn argue that ish'ar fulfills the purpose of identification more effectively than taqlid (garlanding). Abu Hanifa counters that ish'ar is a form of mutilation (muthla), which is prohibited, and that the Prophet's practice was a specific measure against polytheists.
Note the principle: when proofs conflict, prohibition takes precedence.
4
Analyse the Hanafi internal critique
The Sahibayn concede that ish'ar has an element of mutilation, so they downgrade it from sunnah to hasan. Abu Hanifa insists on makruh because the prohibition is stronger. Also, later scholars note that Abu Hanifa's dislike was partly due to contemporary exaggeration harming the animal.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical consequence: a Hanafi following Abu Hanifa should avoid ish'ar and use taqlid; one following the Sahibayn may perform ish'ar but taqlid is superior. Shafi'is consider it sunnah. The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is makruh, following Abu Hanifa.

قَالَ وَأَشْعَرَ الْبُدْنَةَ عِنْدَ أَبِى يُوْسَفَ وَ مُحَمَّدٍ وَلَا يُشْعِرُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَيَكْرَهُ وَالْإِشْعَارُ هُوَ الْإِدْمَاء بِالْجَرْحِ لُغَةً وَ صِفَتهُ أنْ يَشُقَ سِنَامُهَا بِأنْ يَطْعَنَ فِي أَسْفَلِ السَّامِ مِنَ الْجَانِبِ الْأَيْمَنِ قَالُوا وَالأشْبَهُ هُوَ الْأَيْسَرُ لأنَّ النبى عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ طَعَنَ فِي جَانِبِ الْيَسَارِ مَقْصُودَ اوَ فِي جَانِبِ الْأَيْمَنِ إِتِّفَاقًا وَيَلْطَحُ سِنَامَهَا بِالدَّمِ إِعْلَامًا وَهَذَا الصُّنَعُ مَكْرُوهُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَعِندَهُمَا حَسَنُ وَعِندَ الشَّافِعِي سُنة لأنَّهُ مَرْوِيٌّ عَنِ النَّبِي عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ وَعَن الْحُلَفَاءِ وَلَهُمَا إِنَّ الْمَقْصُودَ مِنَ التَّقْلِيدِ أنْ لَايُهَاجَ إِذَا وَرَدَمَاء أَوْ كَلَا اَوْيُرَدُّ إِذَا ضَلَّ وَإِنَّهُ فِي الْإِشْعَارِ اتَهُ لِأَنَّهُ الرمُ فَمِنْ هَذَا الْوَجْهِ يَكُونُ سُنَّةً إِلَّا إِنَّهُ عَارَضَتْهُ جِهَهُ كُونِهِ مُثْلَةَ فَقُلْنَا بِحُسْنِهِ وَلا بِي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّهُ مُثْلَةٌ وَأَنَّهُ مَنْهِى عَنْهُ وَلَوْ وَقَعَ التَّعَارُضُ فَالتَّرْجِيحُ لِلْمُحَرِمِ وَإِشْعَارُ النَّى عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لِصَيَانَةِ الْهَدَى لِأَنَّ الْمُشْرِكِيْنَ لَا يَمْنَعُونَ عَنْ تَعَرُّضِهِ إِلَّا بِهِ وَقِيلَ إِنَّ أَبَا حَنِيفَةَ كَرَة إِشْعَارَ أَهْلِ زَمَانِهِ لِمُبَا لَغَتِهِمْ فِيهِ عَلَى وَجهِ يُخَافُ مِنْهُ السّرَايَةُ وَقِيلَ إِنَّمَا كَرِهَ أَبْنَارَهُ عَلَى التَّقْلِيدِ

مروی ہے جیسا کہ امام ترمندی نے ذکر کیا ہے۔ اور جو عمل پیغمبر اور خلفاء راشدین سے مروی ہو اس کے مسنون ہونے میں کیا شبہ ہو سکتا ہے۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ہدی کو قلادہ پہنانے سے مقصود یہ ہے کہ ہدی کا جانور اگر کسی پانی پر جائے یا گھاس پر تو اس کو کوئی دھتکار کر نہ نکالے۔ یا اگر وہ گم ہو جائے تو اس کو واپس کر دیا جائے اور یہ بات اشعار میں پورے طور پر پائی جاتی ہے اور الزم بھی ہے، کیونکہ اس طرح کا زخم بہت جلد مندمل نہیں ہو سکتا۔ ہر شخص اس کو دیکھ کر پہچان جائے گا کہ یہ بدی کا جانور ہے۔ بہر حال اس اعتبار سے اشعار سنت ہونا چاہئے ۔ مگر چونکہ اشعار میں مثلہ کرنا بھی پایا جاتا ہے اور مثلہ کرنا ممنوع ہے۔ اس لئے ہم نے درمیان کی راہ نکال کر کہا کہ اشعار نہ سنت ہے اور نہ مکروہ بلکہ حسن یعنی جائز ہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اشعار کرنا بالیقین جانور کو مثلہ کرنا ہے اور مثلہ کرنے سے احادیث میں ممانعت کی گئی ہے اس لئے اشعار کم از کم مکروہ ضرور ہو گا۔ اور اگر آپ کہیں کہ احادیث سے مسنون ہونا بھی ثابت ہے تو اس کا جواب یہ ہوگا کہ روایات دونوں طرح کی موجود ہیں محرم بھی اور میسج بھی۔ اور قاعدہ آپ کو معلوم ہے کہ محرم اور مسیح میں تعارض کے وقت محرم کو ترجیح ہوتی ہے نہ کہ میسج کو ۔ پس محرم کو ترجیح دے کر اشعار کو مکروہ قرار دیا گیا ہے۔ واشعار النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَام سے امام شافعی کی دلیل کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا اشعار کرنا یہ ہدی کے جانور کی حفاظت کے لئے تھا۔ کیونکہ مشرکین ہدی کے جانور کو پکڑ کر ذبح کرنے سے اسی وقت باز آتے تھے جبکہ اس کو اشعار کر دیا گیا ہوتا اور چونکہ ہمارے زمانہ میں یہ بات نہیں ہے اس لئے اشعار کی چنداں ضرورت نہیں رہی۔ حضرت امام طحاوی نے فرمایا ہے کہ حضرت امام اعظم نے اپنے زمانہ کے لوگوں کے اشعار کومکروہ کہا ہے۔ کیونکہ اس زمانہ کے لوگ اشعار میں اس قدر شدت اور مبالغہ سے کام لیتے تھے کہ بسا اوقات زخم سرایت کرنے کی وجہ سے ہدی کے ہلاک ہو جانے کا اندیشہ پیدا ہو جاتا تھا نفس اشعار حضرت امام صاحب کے نزدیک بھی مکروہ نہیں ہے۔ اور بعض حضرات نے فرمایا ہے کہ اشعار مکروہ نہیں ہے بلکہ اشعار کو قلادہ ڈالنے پر ترجیح دینا مکروہ ہے یعنی قلادہ ڈالنا اولیٰ ہے اگر چہ اشعار بھی سنت ہے۔
He said: And he makes ish'ar on the badanah according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and he does not make ish'ar according to Abu Hanifa, and he dislikes it. Ish'ar linguistically is causing blood to flow by wounding. Its description is that he splits its hump by stabbing in the lower part of the hump from the right side. They said: the more similar is the left side because the Prophet (peace be upon him) stabbed the left side intentionally and the right side incidentally. And he smears its hump with blood as a sign. This act is disliked according to Abu Hanifa, and according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is good, and according to al-Shafi'i it is sunnah because it is reported from the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the caliphs. And for them (the two) is that the purpose of taqlid (garlanding) is that it not be repelled when it comes to water or pasture, or that it be returned if it is lost, and this meaning is more complete in ish'ar because it is more binding. So from this aspect it would be sunnah, except that it is opposed by the aspect of it being mutilation (muthla), so we said it is good. And Abu Hanifa's proof is that it is mutilation and it is prohibited. If there is a conflict, the preference is given to the prohibited. And the Prophet's ish'ar was for protecting the hadi, because the polytheists would not refrain from interfering with it except by that. And it was said that Abu Hanifa disliked the ish'ar of the people of his time due to their exaggeration in it in a way that caused fear of infection. And it was said that he disliked preferring ish'ar over taqlid. ..., the Prophet's ish'ar was to protect the hadi, because the polytheists would only stop interfering with it when ish'ar was done. And since this reason is absent in our time, ish'ar is not needed. Imam Tahawi said that Imam Abu Hanifa disliked the ish'ar of the people of his time because they exaggerated in ish'ar to the extent that sometimes the wound would become infected and the hadi would die; the act of ish'ar per se is not disliked according to him. And some said that ish'ar is not disliked, but preferring ish'ar over taqlid is disliked, meaning taqlid is superior even if ish'ar is sunnah.
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the ruling on ish'ar (marking the sacrificial animal by cutting its hump and smearing blood) for the badanah (camel or cow). The author presents the positions of the major Hanafi imams and Imam al-Shafi'i. The passage opens by stating that according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), ish'ar is performed, while according to Abu Hanifa it is not performed and is makruh. The definition of ish'ar is given: linguistically, it means causing blood to flow by wounding; practically, it involves cutting the hump from the lower right side, though the later scholars prefer the left side because the Prophet (ﷺ) intentionally stabbed the left side. The blood is then smeared as a sign. The ruling: Abu Hanifa considers it makruh, the Sahibayn consider it hasan (good), and al-Shafi'i considers it sunnah. The proof for al-Shafi'i is that it is reported from the Prophet and the Rightly Guided Caliphs. The Sahibayn argue that the purpose of taqlid (garlanding) is to prevent the animal from being chased away or to help it be returned if lost, and ish'ar achieves this more strongly (being more binding), so it is sunnah; however, due to the element of mutilation, they downgrade it to hasan. Abu Hanifa holds that ish'ar is mutilation (muthla), which is prohibited, and when conflicting evidences occur, the prohibition is given precedence. He also explains that the Prophet's ish'ar was specific to his time to protect the hadi from the polytheists, so it is not a general sunnah. Additionally, it is said that Abu Hanifa's dislike was due to the excessive practices of his people that risked the animal's life, and that the dislike is actually for preferring ish'ar over taqlid, not for ish'ar itself. The passage concludes that for small animals like goats/sheep, ish'ar is not done by consensus; for camels/cows, the Sahibayn permit it while Abu Hanifa dislikes it.

Key Terms
الإشعار (al-ish‘ār): Making a cut on the hump of the sacrificial animal (badanah) to cause bleeding, as a mark that it is a hadi (sacrificial animal).
التقليد (al-taqlīd): Placing a garland (qilada) around the neck of the hadi to mark it as a sacrificial animal.
المثلة (al-muthla): Mutilation of an animal's body, which is prohibited in Islam.
البدنة (al-badanah): A camel or cow brought as a sacrificial animal (hadi) for Hajj or Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is ish'ar (cutting the hump of the sacrificial animal) considered makruh?
A) Because it is not established from the Prophet
B) Because it involves mutilation (muthla) which is prohibited, and the Prophet's practice was specific to his time
C) Because it is a Bid'ah (innovation) in the religion
D) Because it harms the owner of the animal

Key Takeaway
Ish'ar on a camel or cow is makruh in the Hanafi school (mufta bihi) due to its mutilation aspect, though the Sahibayn permit it as hasan; taqlid (garlanding) remains the preferred method.
