Mutamatti' with Hadi Does Not Become Halal After Umrah
Ruling with proof: Mutamatti' with hadi stays in ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a mutamatti' who brings a hadi and explain the proof from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Driving the hadi prevents tahlil: the mutamatti' remains in ihram until Hajj.

In Hajj al-Tamattu', the pilgrim performs Umrah first and then Hajj. A key distinction exists between those who bring a sacrificial animal (hadi) and those who do not. This lesson clarifies that the mutamatti' with hadi does not become halal after Umrah, based on the Prophet's practice in the Farewell Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of mutamatti'
Distinguish between a mutamatti' who brings a hadi (sa'iq al-hadi) and one who does not (ghayr sa'iq). Each has a different ruling regarding tahlil after Umrah.
The source text begins by stating the exception.
2
State the ruling for each type
Ghayr sa'iq becomes halal after Umrah; sa'iq does not. The sa'iq remains in ihram until the day of Tarwiyah (8th Dhul Hijjah), when he enters ihram for Hajj.
The ruling is wajib for the sa'iq to remain in ihram.
3
Locate the proof (dalil)
The proof is the Prophet's hadith: 'If I had known what I now know, I would not have driven the hadi and would have made it Umrah and become halal.' This shows that driving hadi prevents tahlil.
The hadith is found in Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's statement implies that his action of driving the hadi was the reason he did not become halal. The negation of tahlil is directly linked to the presence of the hadi.
This is a clear implication (dalala zanniyya) that is relied upon in the Hanafi school.
5
Apply the ruling to a modern scenario
A pilgrim performing tamattu' who brings a sacrificial animal (or its value designated as hadi) must not remove ihram after Umrah. He remains in ihram until Hajj, even if the animal is not physically driven.
The hadi does not need to be physically driven; the ruling applies to anyone who has undertaken to bring a hadi (e.g., by pre-purchasing).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
متمتع غیر سائق المھدی عمرہ کرنے کے بعد حلال ہو جاتا ہے بخلاف متمتع سائق الھدی کے کہ وہ عمرہ کے بعد حلال نہیں ہوتا
قَالَ فَإِذَا دَخَلَ مَكَّةَ طَافَ وَ سَعَى وَهَذَا لِلْعُمْرَةِ عَلَى مَا بَيْنَاهُ فِي مُتَمَتَع لا يَسُوق الهدى إلَّا أنَّه لا يتحلل حتى يُحْرمَ بالحَج يَوْمُ التّرُويَةِ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ لَوْ اسْتَقْبَلْتُ مِنْ أَمْرِى مَا اسْتَدْبَرُتُ لما سُقْتُ الهدى ولَجَعَلْتُها عُمْرَةً وَتَحَلَّلَتْ مِنْهَا وَهَذَا يَنْفِي التَّحَلَّلَ عِندَ سَوْقَ الْهَدَى
ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا پھر جب متمتع مکہ میں داخل ہو تو طواف وسعی کرے اور یہ طواف وسعی عمرہ کے واسطے ہے جیسا کہ ہم اسے متمتع میں بیان کر چکے جس نے ہدی نہیں چلائی ہے۔ مگر یہ کہ وہ حلال نہیں ہو گا اس حالت تک کہ یوم ترویہ میں حج کا احرام باند ھے کیونکہ حضور نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر اپنے بارے میں مجھے پہلے سے اس بات کا خیال ظاہر ہوتا جو بعد میں ظاہر ہوا تو میں ہدی کو نہ چلاتا اور میں اسکو عمرہ
The mutamatti' who does not drive the hadi becomes halal after performing Umrah, unlike the mutamatti' who drives the hadi, for he does not become halal after Umrah. He said: Then when he enters Makkah, he performs tawaf and sa'y, and this is for Umrah, as we explained for the mutamatti' who does not drive the hadi, except that he does not become halal until he enters ihram for Hajj on the day of Tarwiyah, because of his (the Prophet's) saying: 'If I had known what I now know, I would not have driven the hadi, and I would have made it Umrah and then become halal.' And this negates becoming halal when driving the hadi.
Source pages p. 398

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the mutamatti' (one who performs Umrah first and then Hajj) who brings a sacrificial animal (hadi) with him. The author distinguishes between two types of mutamatti': one who does not bring a hadi (ghayr sa'iq al-hadi) becomes halal after completing Umrah and may enjoy normal life until the 8th of Dhul Hijjah. However, the mutamatti' who brings a hadi (sa'iq al-hadi) does not become halal after Umrah; he remains in the state of ihram and must enter ihram again for Hajj on the day of Tarwiyah (8th Dhul Hijjah). The proof is the hadith in which the Prophet (ﷺ) said that if he had known what he came to know later, he would not have driven the hadi and would have made it Umrah and then become halal. This indicates that driving the hadi prevents becoming halal after Umrah. The matn (al-Quduri) states that such a mutamatti' performs tawaf and sa'y for Umrah upon entering Makkah, but he does not shave or cut his hair until after Hajj. The commentary explains that this is based on the Prophet's practice during the Farewell Hajj when he performed Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah with one ihram) and drove the hadi; his companions who had not brought a hadi were ordered to exit ihram after Umrah, but those who had brought a hadi remained in ihram.

Key Terms
متمتع (mutamatti‘): One who performs Umrah during the months of Hajj and then performs Hajj in the same year, with a sacrifice (dam) required.
سائق الهدى (sā’iq al-hadī): The one who brings/drives a sacrificial animal (hadi) with him while in ihram.
يوم التروية (yawm al-tarwiyah): The 8th of Dhul Hijjah, when pilgrims begin the rites of Hajj and proceed to Mina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for a mutamatti' who drives a hadi (sacrificial animal) with him?
A) He becomes halal after completing Umrah, just like any mutamatti'
B) He remains in ihram until the day of Tarwiyah and then enters ihram for Hajj without becoming halal in between
C) He must sacrifice the hadi immediately after Umrah and then become halal
D) He is not allowed to perform tamattu' if he has a hadi

Key Takeaway
A mutamatti' who brings a hadi must remain in ihram after Umrah until Hajj, based on the Prophet's hadith that driving hadi prevents becoming halal.

Ishaar: Between Muthla and Purpose
Inter-madhhab dispute on ruling of Ishaar for Hadi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on Ishaar, distinguish the views of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the principle of preferring prohibitory narrations.

Core Idea
Ishaar involves muthla, but its purpose is valid; the Hanafi school takes a middle path: permissible, not sunnah.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute over the practice of Ishaar—marking the sacrificial animal (hadi) by making a small wound on its hump. The text lays out three positions: Imam Abu Hanifa considers it makruh (disliked), the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) consider it permissible without dislike, and Imam al-Shafi'i considers it sunnah (recommended). Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to weigh conflicting dalils and apply Hanafi usul principles to resolve them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
Note the ruling from each authority: Abu Hanifa (makruh), Sahibayn (ja'iz), Shafi'i (sunnah). Also note that Malik and Ahmad agree with Shafi'i.
This is an intra-Hanafi difference as well as inter-madhhab.
2
Analyze the Sahibayn's reasoning
The Sahibayn argue that Ishaar serves the same purpose as a garland (qilada) but more effectively because the wound is a lasting mark. However, because Ishaar involves muthla (disfigurement), they stop short of calling it sunnah and label it merely permissible (hasan/ja'iz).
This is the 'middle path' the author refers to.
3
Examine Abu Hanifa's stronger stance
Abu Hanifa focuses on the prohibition of muthla. Since Ishaar is a form of muthla, it must be at least makruh. He invokes the usul principle: when conflicting narrations exist, the one imposing a prohibition is given precedence over the one allowing an action.
This principle is key to Hanafi istidlal.
4
Evaluate the Shafi'i proof and Hanafi response
Shafi'i relies on reports of the Prophet and Caliphs practicing Ishaar. The Hanafi response is two-fold: (a) the Prophet's action was for a specific context (protection from polytheists) and is not a general sunnah; (b) even if there are conflicting narrations, the prohibitory ones are preferred. Additionally, Imam Tahawi notes that Abu Hanifa's dislike was specific to the excessive practice of his time.
This shows how context and usul principles can restrict a seemingly general practice.
5
Identify the mufta bihi and practical takeaway
The Hanafi school's relied-upon position is the Sahibayn's view: Ishaar is permissible but not recommended. It is better to use a garland (qilada) instead. This is the ruling applied in fatwa today.
This reflects the later Hanafi preference for the less disputed view.

Source Text

صاحب ہدایہ نے مذاہب ائمہ بیان کرتے ہوئے فرمایا ہے کہ اشعار یعنی نیزہ مار کر کو ہان پھاڑنے کا عمل امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک مکروہ ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک بلا کراہت جائز ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک مسنون ہے۔ یہی قول امام مالک، امام احمد اور جمہور علماء کا ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اشعار کا عمل رسول خدا صلى الله عليه وسلم اور خلفاء راشدین سے مروی ہے جیسا کہ امام ترمندی نے ذکر کیا ہے۔ اور جو عمل پیغمبر اور خلفاء راشدین سے مروی ہو اس کے مسنون ہونے میں کیا شبہ ہو سکتا ہے۔
صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ہدی کو قلادہ پہنانے سے مقصود یہ ہے کہ ہدی کا جانور اگر کسی پانی پر جائے یا گھاس پر تو اس کو کوئی دھتکار کر نہ نکالے۔ یا اگر وہ گم ہو جائے تو اس کو واپس کر دیا جائے اور یہ بات اشعار میں پورے طور پر پائی جاتی ہے اور الزم بھی ہے، کیونکہ اس طرح کا زخم بہت جلد مندمل نہیں ہو سکتا۔ ہر شخص اس کو دیکھ کر پہچان جائے گا کہ یہ بدی کا جانور ہے۔ بہر حال اس اعتبار سے اشعار سنت ہونا چاہئے ۔ مگر چونکہ اشعار میں مثلہ کرنا بھی پایا جاتا ہے اور مثلہ کرنا ممنوع ہے۔ اس لئے ہم نے درمیان کی راہ نکال کر کہا کہ اشعار نہ سنت ہے اور نہ مکروہ بلکہ حسن یعنی جائز ہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اشعار کرنا بالیقین جانور کو مثلہ کرنا ہے اور مثلہ کرنے سے احادیث میں ممانعت کی گئی ہے اس لئے اشعار کم از کم مکروہ ضرور ہو گا۔ اور اگر آپ کہیں کہ احادیث سے مسنون ہونا بھی ثابت ہے تو اس کا جواب یہ ہوگا کہ روایات دونوں طرح کی موجود ہیں محرم بھی اور میسج بھی۔ اور قاعدہ آپ کو معلوم ہے کہ محرم اور مسیح میں تعارض کے وقت محرم کو ترجیح ہوتی ہے نہ کہ میسج کو ۔ پس محرم کو ترجیح دے کر اشعار کو مکروہ قرار دیا گیا ہے۔ واشعار النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَام سے امام شافعی کی دلیل کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا اشعار کرنا یہ ہدی کے جانور کی حفاظت کے لئے تھا۔ کیونکہ مشرکین ہدی کے جانور کو پکڑ کر ذبح کرنے سے اسی وقت باز آتے تھے جبکہ اس کو اشعار کر دیا گیا ہوتا اور چونکہ ہمارے زمانہ میں یہ بات نہیں ہے اس لئے اشعار کی چنداں ضرورت نہیں رہی۔ حضرت امام طحاوی نے فرمایا ہے کہ حضرت امام اعظم نے اپنے زمانہ کے لوگوں کے اشعار کومکروہ کہا ہے۔ کیونکہ اس زمانہ کے لوگ اشعار میں اس قدر شدت اور مبالغہ سے کام لیتے تھے کہ بسا اوقات زخم سرایت کرنے کی وجہ سے ہدی کے ہلاک ہو جانے کا اندیشہ پیدا ہو جاتا تھا نفس اشعار حضرت امام صاحب کے نزدیک بھی مکروہ نہیں ہے۔ اور بعض حضرات نے فرمایا ہے کہ اشعار مکروہ نہیں ہے بلکہ اشعار کو قلادہ ڈالنے پر ترجیح دینا مکروہ ہے یعنی قلادہ ڈالنا اولیٰ ہے اگر چہ اشعار بھی سنت ہے۔
The author of Hidayah states while explaining the views of the Imams: Ishaar, i.e., the act of piercing the hump with a spear, is considered makruh (disliked) by Imam Abu Hanifa, permissible without dislike by the Sahibayn, and sunnah (recommended) by Imam Shafi'i. This is also the view of Imam Malik, Imam Ahmad, and the majority of scholars. Imam Shafi'i's proof is that the practice of Ishaar is transmitted from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and the Rightly Guided Caliphs, as narrated by Imam Tirmidhi. And what is transmitted from the Prophet and the Caliphs, how can there be any doubt about it being sunnah? The Sahibayn's proof is that the purpose of placing a garland (qilada) on the Hadi is that if the animal goes to water or grass, no one should drive it away, or if it is lost, it should be returned. And this purpose is fully achieved and more firmly established by Ishaar, because such a wound does not heal quickly. Everyone who sees it will recognize that it is a sacrificial animal. Therefore, from this perspective, Ishaar should be sunnah. However, because Ishaar involves muthla (disfigurement), and muthla is prohibited, we took a middle path and said Ishaar is neither sunnah nor makruh, but hasan (good), i.e., permissible. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that Ishaar definitely constitutes muthla, and muthla has been prohibited in hadiths; therefore, Ishaar is at least makruh. If you say that it is also proven to be sunnah from hadiths, the answer is that there are narrations on both sides—prohibiting and permissive. And you know the rule: when there is conflict between a prohibiting (muharram) and a permissive (musayyigh) narration, the prohibiting one is given precedence, not the permissive one. So, giving precedence to the prohibiting narration, Ishaar is declared makruh. As for the Prophet's (peace be upon him) practice of Ishaar, which is Imam Shafi'i's proof, the answer is that the Prophet's Ishaar was for the protection of the Hadi because the polytheists would only refrain from capturing and slaughtering the Hadi when it was marked with Ishaar. Since this situation no longer exists in our time, Ishaar is not needed. Imam Tahawi said that Imam Abu Hanifa considered the Ishaar of the people of his time as makruh because they would do it with such severity and exaggeration that often the wound would spread and risk killing the Hadi. The essence of Ishaar is not considered makruh by Imam Abu Hanifa himself. Some scholars have said that Ishaar is not makruh, but preferring Ishaar over placing a garland is makruh, i.e., placing a garland is better although Ishaar is also sunnah.
Source pages p. 398

Commentary
A teacher explains: This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute regarding the practice of Ishaar, marking the sacrificial animal by making a small wound on its hump. The text first states the positions: Imam Abu Hanifa rules it makruh, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold it permissible without dislike, and Imam Shafi'i considers it sunnah. The passage then lays out the proofs. Shafi'i relies on reports that the Prophet and Caliphs did it. The Sahibayn argue that Ishaar serves the same purpose as the garland but more effectively because the wound is a lasting mark; however, due to the prohibition of muthla, they stop short of calling it sunnah and consider it merely permissible. Abu Hanifa takes the strongest stance: Ishaar is muthla, which is explicitly prohibited, so it must be at least makruh. The Hanafi response to Shafi'i's proof is that the Prophet's action was for a specific reason (protection from polytheists) which no longer applies, so it is not a general sunnah. Also, Imam Tahawi restricts Abu Hanifa's dislike to the excessive practice of his time. The passage also notes the Hanafi legal principle: when conflicting narrations exist, the one imposing a prohibition is given precedence over the one allowing an action. This is a key usuli principle. The Hanafi school's relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the Sahibayn's view that Ishaar is permissible, though it is better to use a garland.

Key Terms
اشعار (ish'ār): Marking a sacrificial animal by making a small wound on its hump to identify it.
مثلہ (muthla): Disfigurement or mutilation of an animal's body.
قلادہ (qilāda): A garland or necklace placed on a sacrificial animal to mark it.
صاحبین (ṣāḥibayn): The two disciples of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
مکروہ (makrūh): Disliked; an action that is not sinful but should be avoided.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which statement correctly reflects the intra-Hanafi difference on Ishaar (wound-marking) of the sacrificial animal?
A) Abu Hanifa says sunnah, Sahibayn say makruh.
B) Abu Hanifa says makruh, Sahibayn say ja'iz.
C) All Hanafis agree it is sunnah.
D) Abu Hanifa says ja'iz, Sahibayn say makruh.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi on Ishaar is permissible (not sunnah and not makruh), with a recommendation to use a garland instead.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
8 min
Rulings for Mutamatti Who Drives a Hadi
Explanation of why a Mutamatti with Hadi does not become Halal after Umrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a Mutamatti with a Hadi, explain the prophetic proof, and apply it to determine the correct procedure.

Core Idea
Driving a Hadi prevents the Mutamatti from becoming halal after Umrah.

In Hajj Tamattu', the pilgrim performs Umrah then later Hajj. A key distinction is whether he brings a sacrificial animal (Hadi). This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that a Mutamatti with a Hadi must remain in Ihram after Umrah, based on the Prophet's own practice during the Farewell Pilgrimage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of Mutamatti
Note that the Mutamatti with a Hadi (sā’iq al-hadī) and the Mutamatti without a Hadi are treated differently after Umrah.
2
Contrast their rulings after Umrah
The Mutamatti without Hadi becomes halal; the one with Hadi does not – he remains in Ihram until Hajj.
This is the core ruling of the passage.
3
Examine the prophetic proof
The Prophet's statement in the Farewell Pilgrimage: 'If I had known what I later knew, I would not have driven the Hadi and would have become halal from Umrah.' This shows that driving the Hadi prevents becoming halal.
The hadith is found in Bukhari and Muslim.
4
Understand the analogy with Qiran
The Mutamatti with Hadi resembles a Qarin: both remain in Ihram between Umrah and Hajj. The difference is timing of ihram for Hajj.
5
Note additional rulings
The preferred time to assume ihram for Hajj is Yawm al-Tarwiyah (8th Dhul-Hijjah), but earlier is better. Shaving on Yawm al-Nahr removes both ihrams.
These apply to both types of Mutamatti.

متمتع غير سائق المھدی عمرہ کرنے کے بعد حلال ہو جاتا ہے بخلاف متمتع
سائق الھدی کے کہ وہ عمرہ کے بعد حلال نہیں ہوتا
قَالَ فَإِذَا دَخَلَ مَكَّةَ طَافَ وَ سَعَى وَهَذَا لِلْعُمْرَةِ عَلَى مَا بَيْنَاهُ فِي مُتَمَتَع لا يَسُوق الهدى إلَّا أنَّه لا يتحلل حتى يُحْرمَ بالحَج يَوْمُ التّرُويَةِ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ لَوْ اسْتَقْبَلْتُ مِنْ أَمْرِى مَا اسْتَدْبَرُتُ لما سُقْتُ الهدى ولَجَعَلْتُها عُمْرَةً وَتَحَلَّلَتْ مِنْهَا وَهَذَا يَنْفِي التَّحَلَّلَ عِندَ سَوْقَ الْهَدَى
ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا پھر جب متمتع مکہ میں داخل ہو تو طواف وسعی کرے اور یہ طواف وسعی عمرہ کے واسطے ہے جیسا کہ ہم اسے متمتع میں بیان کر چکے جس نے ہدی نہیں چلائی ہے۔ مگر یہ کہ وہ حلال نہیں ہو گا اس حالت تک کہ یوم ترویہ میں حج کا احرام باند ھے کیونکہ حضور نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر اپنے بارے میں مجھے پہلے سے اس بات کا خیال ظاہر ہوتا جو بعد میں ظاہر ہوا تو میں ہدی کو نہ چلاتا اور میں اسکو عمرہ کر دیتا اور اس سے حلال ہو جاتا۔ اور یہ حدیث سوق ہدی کے وقت حلال ہونے کی نفی کرتی ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ متمتع جو ہدی ساتھ لے کر چلا جب مکہ میں داخل ہو تو وہ عمرہ کے واسطے طواف اور سعی کرے ۔اور یہ طواف وسعی عمرہ کے واسطے ایسا ہے جیسا کہ ہم ایسے متمتع کی صورت میں جس نے ہدی نہیں چاہائی ، بیان کر چکے۔ ہاں اتنا فرق ہے کہ ہدی ساتھ لے کر جانے والا طواف و عمرہ کے بعد حلال نہیں ہو گا۔ یعنی ہدی لے جانے والے اور نہ لے جانے والے کے درمیان نفس طواف وسعی میں کوئی فرق نہیں ہے۔ ہاں اتنا فرق ہے کہ وہ متمتع جو ہدی کے ساتھ لے کر چلا ہے وہ عمرہ سے فراغت کے بعد حلال نہیں ہو گا حال بیہ کہ وہ یوم ترویہ کو حج کا احرام باندھ لیتا ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ ہدی ساتھ لے جانے والا استمتع اور قارن دونوں یکساں ہیں جس طرح قارن عمرہ اور حج کے درمیان حلال نہیں ہوتا اسی طرح یہ تمتع بھی حلال نہیں ہوگا۔ فرق اتنا ہے کہ قارن کا احرام حج پہلے سے موجود ہوتا ہے اور یہ تمتع حج کا احرام یوم تر و به کو باندھتا ہے۔ اس کے برخلاف وہ متمتع جو ہدی ساتھ نہیں لے جاتا وہ عمرہ سے فراغت کے بعد حلال ہو جاتا ہے۔ دلیل اس کی یہ ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم حجۃ الوداع کے موقعہ پر جب مکہ المکرمہ میں داخل ہوئے تو صحابہ کو حکم دیا کہ حج کا احرام نسخ کر کے عمرہ کا احرام باندھ لیں۔ صحابہ نے اس کی تعمیل کی اور عمرہ کے افعال ادا کئے اس کے بعد صحابہ انتظار کرنے لگے کہ اللہ کا رسول حلق کر کے حلال ہوتا ہے یا نہیں اس پر آپ نے فرمایا کہ اگر مجھے پہلے سے یہ بات معلوم ہوتی کہ سوق ہدی حلال ہونے سے مانع ہے تو میں ہدی ساتھ لے کر نہ چلتا لیکن چونکہ میں بدی ساتھ لے کر آیا ہوں۔ اس لئے حلال نہیں ہوگا۔ اس واقعہ سے معلوم ہو گیا کہ سوق بدی کی صورت میں متمتع افعال عمرہ ادا کرنے کے بعد حلال نہیں ہوتا۔
وَيُحْرِمُ بِالْحَةُ التَّرْوِيهِ كَمَا يُحْرُمُ أَهْلُ مَكَّةَ عَلَى مَابَيْتًا وَإِنْ قَدَّمَ الْإِحْرَامَ قَبْلَهُ جَازَ وَمَا عَجَلَ الْمُتَمَتَعُ مِنَ الْإِحْرَامِ بِالْحَجِّ فَهُوَ أَفْضَلُ لِمَا فِيهِ مِنَ الْمُسَارَعَةِ وَ زِيَادَةِ الْمُشَقَّةِ وَهَذِهِ الْأَفْضَلِيَّةِ فِي حَقِّ مَنْ سَاقَ الْهَدْيَ وَ فِي حَقِّ مَنْ لَمْ يَسُقُ وَعَلَيْهِ دَمْ وَهُوَ دَمُ التَّمتَّع عَلَى مَا بَيَنَا وَإِذَا حَلَقَ يَوْمَ النَّحْرِ فَقَدْ حَلَّ مِنَ الْإِحْرَامَيْنِ لِأَنَّ الْحَلْقَ مُحَلّل فِي الْحَجِّ كَالسَّلَامِ فِي الصَّلوةِ فَيَتَحَلَّلُ بِهِ عَنْهُمَا
ترجمہ اور ترویہ کے دن حج کا احرام باندھے جیسے اہل مکہ باندھتے ہیں اس بنا پر جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے۔ اور اگر یوم ترویہ سے پہلے احرام باندھ لیا تو جائز ہے۔ اور متمتع جس قدر ج کا احرام جلدی باند ھے وہی افضل ہے کیونکہ اس میں مسارعت اور زیادت مشقت ہے۔ اور یہ افضل ہونا اس متمتع کے حق میں ہے جس نے ہدی چلائی ہو اور اس کے حق میں بھی جس نے ہدی نہیں چلائی اور اس متمتع پر بھی قربانی ہے اور یہ قربانی تمتع کی ہے جیسا کہ ہم بیان کر چکے۔ اور جب یوم نحر کو حلق کرے تو دونوں احراموں سے حلال ہو گیا کیونکہ حلق کرنا حج میں حلال کرنے والا ہے جیسے نماز میں سلام ہے۔ پس اس حلق کے ذریعہ حج اور عمرہ دونوں کے احرام سے حلال ہو جائے گا۔ تشریح . صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ متمتع ارکان عمرہ ادا کرنے کے بعد آٹھویں ذی الحجہ کو حج کا احرام باندھے جیسا کہ مکی آٹھویں ذی الحجہ کو احرام باندھتا ہے کیونکہ یہ بھی مکی کے حکم میں ہے۔ لیکن اگر یوم ترویہ سے پہلے احرام باندھ لیا تو بھی جائز ہے بلکہ افضل ہے اس لئے کہ متمتع حج کا احرام جس قدر جلدی باند ھے گا اسی قدر افضل ہوگا اور دلیل یہ ہے کہ جلدی احرام باندھنے میں مسارعت الی الخیر اور زیادتی
The Mutamatti who does not drive a Hadi becomes halal after performing Umrah, unlike the Mutamatti who drives a Hadi, for he does not become halal after Umrah. Al-Quduri said: 'When he enters Mecca, he performs Tawaf and Sa'i, and this is for the Umrah, as we explained in the case of a Mutamatti who does not drive a Hadi, except that he does not become halal until he assumes Ihram for Hajj on Yawm al-Tarwiyah, due to the Prophet's (peace be upon him) statement: "If I had known what I came to know later, I would not have driven the Hadi and I would have made it an Umrah and become halal from it." And this negates becoming halal when driving the Hadi.' Translation: Al-Quduri said: Then when the Mutamatti enters Mecca, he performs Tawaf and Sa'i, and this Tawaf and Sa'i are for Umrah, as we have explained in the case of a Mutamatti who did not drive a Hadi. However, he will not become halal until he assumes Ihram for Hajj on Yawm al-Tarwiyah, because the Prophet said: 'If I had known beforehand about this matter what became apparent afterward, I would not have driven the Hadi, and I would have made it an Umrah and become halal from it.' And this hadith negates becoming halal when driving the Hadi. Explanation: The Mutamatti who drives a Hadi, when he enters Mecca, performs Tawaf and Sa'i for Umrah, and this Tawaf and Sa'i are similar to what we explained for the Mutamatti who does not drive a Hadi. The only difference is that the one who drives a Hadi does not become halal after Tawaf and Umrah, but remains in ihram until he assumes Ihram for Hajj on Yawm al-Tarwiyah. In summary, the one who drives a Hadi is like a Qarin (one performing Qiran): just as a Qarin does not become halal between Umrah and Hajj, so too this Mutamatti will not become halal. The difference is that the Qarin's Ihram for Hajj was already present, while this Mutamatti assumes Ihram for Hajj on Yawm al-Tarwiyah. In contrast, the Mutamatti who does not drive a Hadi becomes halal after completing Umrah. The proof for this is that when the Messenger of Allah entered Mecca during the Farewell Pilgrimage, he ordered the Companions to annul the Ihram for Hajj and assume Ihram for Umrah. The Companions complied and performed the acts of Umrah. Then the Companions waited to see if the Messenger would shave and become halal. The Prophet said: 'If I had known beforehand that driving the Hadi prevents becoming halal, I would not have driven the Hadi, but since I have brought the Hadi, I will not become halal.' From this incident, it is understood that in the case of driving the Hadi, the Mutamatti does not become halal after performing the acts of Umrah. And he assumes Ihram for Hajj on Yawm al-Tarwiyah just as the people of Mecca assume Ihram, as we have explained. If he assumes Ihram before that, it is permissible. And the sooner the Mutamatti assumes Ihram for Hajj, the better, because it involves hastening and increased hardship. This preference applies both to the one who drives a Hadi and the one who does not. And upon him is a dam (sacrifice), which is the dam of Tamattu', as we have explained. And when he shaves (halq) on Yawm al-Nahr, he becomes halal from both Ihrams, because shaving is what makes one halal in Hajj, just as the Salam (greeting) makes one halal in prayer. So through shaving, he becomes halal from both (Hajj and Umrah). Translation: And he should assume Ihram on Yawm al-Tarwiyah just as the people of Mecca assume Ihram, based on what we have explained. And if he assumes Ihram before it, it is permissible. And the sooner the Mutamatti assumes Ihram for Hajj, the better, because it involves hastening and increased hardship. This preference applies to the Mutamatti who drove a Hadi and also to the one who did not. And upon this Mutamatti is a sacrifice, which is the sacrifice of Tamattu', as we have explained. And when he shaves on Yawm al-Nahr, he becomes halal from both Ihrams, because shaving is what makes halal in Hajj, just as the Salam in prayer. So by this shaving, he becomes halal from both Ihrams. Explanation: Al-Quduri says: The Mutamatti, after performing the pillars of Umrah, should assume Ihram for Hajj on the 8th of Dhul-Hijjah, just as a Meccan assumes Ihram on the 8th, because he is considered like a Meccan. But if he assumes Ihram before Yawm al-Tarwiyah, it is permissible, indeed better, because the sooner he assumes Ihram for Hajj, the more excellent it is, and the proof is that hastening to do good and increasing... (end of page 399)
Source pages p. 398

Commentary
A teacher explains: This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah explains the rulings specific to a Mutamatti (one performing Tamattu' Hajj) who brings a sacrificial animal (Hadi). The central point is that driving a Hadi prevents the Mutamatti from becoming halal after completing Umrah, unlike the Mutamatti without a Hadi. This is based on the Prophet's (peace be upon him) statement during the Farewell Pilgrimage: if he had known beforehand, he would not have driven the Hadi and would have become halal. The Companions were ordered to change their Ihram to Umrah, and they did so, but the Prophet remained in Ihram because he had the Hadi. Thus, the one with Hadi remains in Ihram until Hajj, similar to a Qarin. The passage then discusses the best time to assume Ihram for Hajj: Yawm al-Tarwiyah (8th Dhul-Hijjah), but earlier is better because of hastening to good and increasing hardship. This preference applies whether one has a Hadi or not. The passage also mentions that the Mutamatti owes a Dam (sacrifice) for Tamattu'. Finally, it explains that shaving (halq) on Yawm al-Nahr (10th Dhul-Hijjah) removes both the Ihram of Umrah and Hajj, analogous to the Salam in prayer which ends the prayer. This is an important principle: the Halq is the halal-maker in Hajj.

Key Terms
متمتع (mutamatti‘): One who performs Tamattu' Hajj: performs Umrah in the Hajj months and then Hajj in the same year with a break in between.
سائق الھدی (sā’iq al-hadī): A pilgrim who drives a sacrificial animal (Hadi) along with himself.
یوم الترویہ (yawm al-tarwiya): The 8th of Dhul-Hijjah, the day before Arafah, when pilgrims traditionally go to Mina.
یوم النحر (yawm al-nahr): The 10th of Dhul-Hijjah, the day of sacrifice (Eid al-Adha).
حلق (halq): Shaving the head; the act that makes one halal from Ihram in Hajj.
دم تمتع (dam al-tamattu‘): The sacrifice (a sheep or goat) required of a Mutamatti as compensation for the Tamattu' concession.

A Mutamatti who drives a Hadi remains in Ihram after Umrah until Hajj, based on the Prophet's practice and hadith.

intermediate

The Mutamatti' with Hadi Remains in Ihram
Explains that a Mutamatti' bringing Hadi does not become halal after Umrah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a Mutamatti' who brings a Hadi and explain the dalil from the Sunnah that prevents him from becoming halal after Umrah.

Core Idea
Bringing a sacrificial animal prevents a Mutamatti' from becoming halal after Umrah.

In this passage from Al-Hidayah, we learn a key distinction in the rulings of Tamattu' Hajj. While a Mutamatti' who does not bring a Hadi becomes halal after completing Umrah, the one who brings a Hadi must remain in Ihram until the Day of Nahr. This ruling is derived from the Prophet's own practice during the Farewell Pilgrimage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is a Mutamatti' (one performing Tamattu') who brings a sacrificial animal (Hadi) when entering Makkah. The Hanafi ruling is that such a person does not become halal after completing Umrah; he remains in Ihram until the Day of Nahr.
Contrast with a Mutamatti' without Hadi, who becomes halal after Umrah.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is from the incident of Hajjat al-Wada' (the Farewell Pilgrimage). When the Prophet commanded the Companions to change their Ihram to Umrah, he himself did not become halal because he had brought the Hadi.
The specific evidence is the Prophet's statement: 'If I had known that bringing the Hadi prevents becoming halal, I would not have brought it. But since I have brought it, I will not become halal.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The operative phrase is 'إذا كنت سقت الهدي لم أحل' (if I have brought the Hadi, I do not become halal). This establishes that bringing the Hadi is a preventer (mani') of becoming halal after Umrah. The Prophet's action confirms this ruling.
In Hanafi usul, this hadith is a hadith ahad (zanni al-thubut) but is accepted in practice.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that even a Mutamatti' with Hadi becomes halal after Umrah, and the Hadi is simply an additional offering. The Hanafi school disagrees based on the apparent meaning of the hadith.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both schools have their proofs.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) and is from the Zahir al-Riwayah. It is based on the clear practice of the Prophet and is followed in Hanafi fatwa.
The practical consequence is that a Mutamatti' with Hadi must remain in Ihram, cannot have marital relations, and must sacrifice on the Day of Nahr.

He makes [halal] and becomes halal from it. And this hadith negates becoming halal at the time of bringing the Hadi. Explanation: The issue is that the Mutamatti' who brings Hadi, when he enters Makkah, he should perform Tawaf and Sa'i for Umrah. And this Tawaf and Sa'i for Umrah is just as we have explained for the case of a Mutamatti' who did not bring Hadi. However, there is one difference: the one who brings Hadi will not become halal after Tawaf and Umrah. That is, there is no difference in the Tawaf and Sa'i itself between the one who brings Hadi and the one who does not. The only difference is that the Mutamatti' who brought Hadi will not become halal after completing Umrah, even though he ties the Ihram for Hajj on the Day of Tarwiyah. In short, the Mutamatti' who brings Hadi and the Qarin are the same: just as a Qarin does not become halal between Umrah and Hajj, similarly this Mutamatti' will not become halal. The difference is that the Qarin's Ihram for Hajj was present from before, while this Mutamatti' ties the Ihram for Hajj on the Day of Tarwiyah. In contrast, the Mutamatti' who does not bring Hadi becomes halal after completing Umrah. The proof for this is that when the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, entered Makkah during the Farewell Pilgrimage, he commanded the Companions to abrogate the Ihram for Hajj and tie the Ihram for Umrah. The Companions complied and performed the actions of Umrah. After that, the Companions waited to see whether the Messenger of Allah would shave and become halal. At that, he said: 'If I had known beforehand that bringing the Hadi prevents becoming halal, I would not have brought the Hadi. But since I have brought the Hadi, I will not become halal.' From this incident it is understood that when bringing the Hadi, a Mutamatti' does not become halal after performing the actions of Umrah.
Source pages p. 399

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Sunnah. It explains the difference between two types of Mutamatti': one who brings a sacrificial animal (Hadi) and one who does not. Both perform the same Tawaf and Sa'i for Umrah, but the former remains in Ihram after completing Umrah, while the latter becomes Halal (releases from Ihram). The Mutamatti' with Hadi is like a Qarin (one performing Qiran) in that he does not become Halal between the two rites. The proof is the incident of Hajjat al-Wada' where the Prophet (PBUH) did not become Halal after Umrah because he had brought the Hadi, and he stated that had he known, he would not have brought it. This shows that bringing the Hadi prevents becoming Halal after Umrah for a Mutamatti'. The Hanafi ruling is that such a person remains in Ihram until the Day of Nahr when he sacrifices the animal and shaves or trims his hair.

Key Terms
سوق هدي (sawq al-hady): Bringing a sacrificial animal (Hadi) with oneself when entering Makkah for Hajj or Umrah.
متمتع (mutamatti'): One who performs Tamattu' Hajj: performs Umrah first, then Hajj within the same journey.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Ruling on Timing of Hajj Ihram for Mutamatti' and Superiority of Early Ihram
States the ruling on timing of Hajj Ihram for Mutamatti'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended time for a Mutamatti' to enter Ihram for Hajj, explain the permissibility and virtue of earlier Ihram, and identify the act that releases from both Ihrams.

Core Idea
Early Ihram for Hajj after Umrah is permissible and more virtuous due to hastening and increased hardship.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses the timing of the Hajj Ihram for someone performing Tamattu'. It establishes that while the ideal time is the Day of Tarwiyah, entering Ihram earlier is not only permissible but considered better (afḍal). The commentary explains that this virtue applies to all, whether or not they have brought a sacrificial animal (hady).

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and its context
The ruling concerns a Mutamatti' who has completed the pillars (arkan) of Umrah and now intends to perform Hajj. Recognize that he is in a state of partial release (tahlul) from Umrah but still in Ihram for the combined ritual.
The Mutamatti' has already performed Umrah and is waiting for the Hajj days.
2
Determine the ideal time for Hajj Ihram
The ideal time is the Day of Tarwiyah (8th Dhu al-Hijjah), following the practice of the people of Makkah. Note that this is the sunnah method.
Day of Tarwiyah is the 8th of Dhu al-Hijjah.
3
Recognize the permissibility and virtue of earlier Ihram
Entering Ihram before the Day of Tarwiyah is permissible (ja'iz) and is actually better (afḍal) because it involves hastening towards good (al-musara'ah ila al-khayr) and extra hardship (mashaqqah), which increases reward.
The commentary cites the hadith: 'The most excellent acts of worship are the most strenuous.'
4
Understand the scope of the virtue
The virtue of early Ihram applies to all Mutamatti' pilgrims, whether or not they have brought a Hadi (sacrificial animal). The dam of Tamattu' is obligatory on all.
This clarifies that the superiority is not conditional on bringing a Hadi.
5
Identify the release from both Ihrams
Shaving the head (halq) or trimming the hair (qasr) on the Day of Nahr (10th Dhu al-Hijjah) releases the Mutamatti' from both the Ihram of Umrah and Hajj. This is analogous to the final salam in prayer, which ends the prayer.
Halq is the primary means; qasr suffices but halq is more virtuous.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
متمتع ارکان عمرہ کے بعد ایام حج میں احرام باندھے
وَيُحْرِمُ بِالْحَجِّ يَوْمَ التَّرْوِيهِ كَمَا يُحْرِمُ أَهْلُ مَكَّةَ عَلَى مَا بَيَّنَا وَإِنْ قَدَّمَ الْإِحْرَامَ قَبْلَهُ جَازَ وَمَا عَجَّلَ الْمُتَمَتِّعُ مِنَ الْإِحْرَامِ بِالْحَجِّ فَهُوَ أَفْضَلُ لِمَا فِيهِ مِنَ الْمُسَارَعَةِ وَ زِيَادَةِ الْمُشَقَّةِ وَهَذِهِ الْأَفْضَلِيَّةِ فِي حَقِّ مَنْ سَاقَ الْهَدْيَ وَ فِي حَقِّ مَنْ لَمْ يَسُقُ وَعَلَيْهِ دَمْ وَهُوَ دَمُ التَّمتَّع عَلَى مَا بَيَّنَا وَإِذَا حَلَقَ يَوْمَ النَّحْرِ فَقَدْ حَلَّ مِنَ الْإِحْرَامَيْنِ لِأَنَّ الْحَلْقَ مُحَلّل فِي الْحَجِّ كَالسَّلَامِ فِي الصَّلوةِ فَيَتَحَلَّلُ بِهِ عَنْهُمَا
ترجمہ اور ترویہ کے دن حج کا احرام باندھے جیسے اہل مکہ باندھتے ہیں اس بنا پر جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے۔ اور اگر یوم ترویہ سے پہلے احرام باندھ لیا تو جائز ہے۔ اور متمتع جس قدر ج کا احرام جلدی باندھے وہی افضل ہے کیونکہ اس میں مسارعت اور زیادت مشقت ہے۔ اور یہ افضل ہونا اس متمتع کے حق میں ہے جس نے ہدی چلائی ہو اور اس کے حق میں بھی جس نے ہدی نہیں چلائی اور اس متمتع پر قربانی ہے اور یہ قربانی تمتع کی ہے جیسا کہ ہم بیان کر چکے۔ اور جب یوم نحر کو حلق کرے تو دونوں احراموں سے حلال ہو گیا کیونکہ حلق کرنا حج میں حلال کرنے والا ہے جیسے نماز میں سلام ہے۔ پس اس حلق کے ذریعہ حج اور عمرہ دونوں کے احرام سے حلال ہو جائے گا۔
تشریح . صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ متمتع ارکان عمرہ ادا کرنے کے بعد آٹھویں ذی الحجہ کو حج کا احرام باندھے جیسا کہ مکی آٹھویں ذی الحجہ کو احرام باندھتا ہے کیونکہ یہ بھی مکی کے حکم میں ہے۔ لیکن اگر یوم ترویہ سے پہلے احرام باندھ لیا تو بھی جائز ہے بلکہ افضل ہے اس لئے کہ متمتع حج کا احرام جس قدر جلدی باندھے گا اسی قدر افضل ہوگا اور دلیل یہ ہے کہ جلدی احرام باندھنے میں مسارعت الی الخیر اور زیادتی مشقت ہے۔ عبادت باعتبار زیادتی مشقت کے افضل ہے چنانچہ حدیث میں ہے اَفضَلَ الْعِبَادَاتِ أَحْمَضُهَا - صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اس افضلیت میں ہدی ساتھ لے جانے والا اور نہ لے جانے والا دونوں برابر ہیں یعنی دونوں کے لئے احرام حج میں جلدی کرنا افضل ہے۔ صاحب قدوری نے کہا ہے کہ حج تمتع کرنے والے پر دم تمتع واجب ہے۔ جیسا کہ سابق میں بیان ہو چکا۔ مستمتع نے جب یوم نحر میں حلق یا قصر کیا تو وہ حج اور عمرہ کے دونوں احراموں سے حلال ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ حلق کرنا حج میں حلال کرنے والا ہے۔ جیسے نماز میں سلام ملل ہے۔ پس حلق سے عمرہ اور حج دونوں کے احرام سے نکل جائے گا۔
The Mutamatti' ties Ihram for Hajj after performing the pillars of Umrah.
And he ties Ihram for Hajj on the day of Tarwiyah just as the people of Makkah tie Ihram, according to what we have explained. And if he advances the Ihram before that, it is permissible. And whatever hastening the Mutamatti' does in tying Ihram for Hajj, it is better because of the haste and increased hardship involved. And this superiority is for the one who brought the Hadi and for the one who did not bring it. And upon him is a sacrifice (dam), and it is the dam of Tamattu' as we have explained. And when he shaves his head on the day of Nahr, he has become halal from both Ihrams because shaving is a cause of halal in Hajj like the salam in prayer, so by it he becomes halal from both.
[Translation of the commentary follows similarly...]
Source pages p. 399

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of Al-Hidayah, with accompanying translation and commentary. The ruling covers three main points: (1) The Mutamatti' should enter Ihram for Hajj on the Day of Tarwiyah (8th Dhu al-Hijjah), following the practice of the people of Makkah. (2) It is permissible and even better to enter Ihram earlier than that, as it involves hastening towards good and extra hardship in worship, which increases reward. This is supported by the hadith that the most excellent acts of worship are the most strenuous. (3) Shaving the head or trimming the hair on the Day of Nahr (10th Dhu al-Hijjah) releases the Mutamatti' from both the Ihram of Umrah and Hajj, analogous to the final salam in prayer. The commentary emphasizes that the virtue of early Ihram applies equally to those who have brought a Hadi and those who have not, and reiterates the obligation of the dam of Tamattu'.

Key Terms
متمتع (mutamatti'): A pilgrim who performs Umrah first, then after a break enters Ihram for Hajj within the same journey.
يَوْمَ التَّرْوِيهِ (yawm al-tarwiyah): The 8th day of Dhu al-Hijjah, the day when pilgrims traditionally go to Mina and prepare for Arafah.
يَوْمَ النَّحْرِ (yawm al-nahr): The 10th day of Dhu al-Hijjah, the day of sacrifice and shaving/trimming.
حلق (halq): Shaving the head completely, which is one of the actions that releases one from Ihram.
قصر (qasr): Trimming the hair, an alternative to shaving for releasing from Ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) On the Day of Tarwiyah (8th Dhu al-Hijjah)
B) On the Day of Arafah (9th Dhu al-Hijjah)
C) Immediately after Umrah, regardless of the date
D) On the Day of Nahr (10th Dhu al-Hijjah)

Key Takeaway
The Mutamatti' is encouraged to hasten in entering Ihram for Hajj after Umrah, as it brings greater reward due to hastening towards good and extra hardship.

Ruling on Tamattu' and Qiran for Residents of Makkah
Inter-madhhab dispute with proof and response

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on Tamattu' and Qiran for Makkans, explain the dalil from Quran 2:196, and compare it with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Makkans may only perform Ifrad; the ease of Tamattu' is for those coming from afar.

This passage addresses an important inter-madhhab dispute: can the people of Makkah and those residing within the Miqat perform Hajj al-Tamattu' or al-Qiran? The Hanafi school holds that they cannot, while Imam al-Shafi'i permits it for all. We will unpack the Hanafi proofs—both textual and rational—and understand the practical consequences of the difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify who is excluded from Tamattu' and Qiran according to the Hanafis: residents of Makkah and anyone living within the Miqat boundaries. They may only perform Ifrad (Hajj without Umrah).
2
Identify the opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that Tamattu' and Qiran are permissible for everyone, including Makkans, and that the obligation of dam applies equally to all.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i school relies on the general command in Quran 2:196: 'And whoever performs Tamattu'... then [offer] whatever is easy of the Hadi.' They argue the text is absolute and does not distinguish between Makkan and Afaqi.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds by citing the very same verse: 'That is for him whose family is not present at al-Masjid al-Haram' (2:196), interpreting 'dhalika' as referring to Tamattu', thus specifying it for non-residents. Additionally, the rationale of eliminating one of two journeys applies only to those coming from a distance.
5
Determine the practical consequence
According to Hanafis, if a Makkan performs Tamattu', the Hajj is valid but sinful, and a compensatory dam is required. Shafi'is hold it is valid without sin or dam obligation.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference).

وَلَيْسَ لِأهْلِ مَكَّةَ تَمَتُّعٌ وَلَا قِرَانَ وَإِنَّمَا لَهُمُ الافْرَادُ خَاصَّةً خِلَافًا لِلشَّافِعِي وَ الْحُجَّةُ عَلَيْهِ قُوْلُهُ تَعَالَى ذَلِكَ لِمَن لَّمْ يَكُنْ أهْلُهُ حَاضِرِى الْمَسْجِدِ الْحَرَامِ وَلأنَّ شَرعَهُمَا لِلتَرَفَه بِاسْقَاطِ إِحْدَى السَّفَرَتَيْنِ وَهَذَا فِي حَقِّ الْآفَاقِي وَمَنْ كَانَ دَاخِلَ الْمَوَاقِيتِ فَهُوَ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الْمَكَى حَتَّى لَا يَكُونُ لَهُ مُتْعَةٌ وَلَا قِرَانٌ بِخِلَافِ الْمَكَّيَ إِذَا خَرَجَ إِلَى الْكُوفَةِ وَقَرَنَ حَيْثُ يَصِحُ لِأَنَّ عُمْرَتَهُ وَحَجَّتُهُ مِيقَاتَانِ فَصَارَ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الْآفَاقِى
ترجمہ اور باشندگانِ مکہ کے لئے نہ حج تمتع ہے اور نہ حج قران ، ان کے لئے خاص طور پر حج افراد ہے۔ امام شافعی کا اختلاف ہے اور ان کے خلاف باری تعالیٰ کا قول ذلِكَ لِمَنْ لَّمْ يَكُنُ أَهْلُهُ حَاضِرِى الْمَسْجِدِ الْحَرَامِ حجت ہے اور اس لئے کہ تمتع اور قارن کو دوسفروں میں سے ایک کو ساقط کر کے راحت دینے کے لئے مشروع کیا ہے اور یہ راحت آفاقی کے حق میں ہے۔ اور جوشخص میقات کے اندر رہتا ہے وہ بھی مکی کے مرتبہ میں ہے حتی کہ اس کے واسطے تمتع اور قران نہیں ہے برخلاف مکی کے جب وہ کوفہ کی طرف نکلا اور قرآن کیا تو صحیح ہے اس لئے کہ اس کا عمرہ اور حج دونوں میقاتی ہیں۔ پس آفاقی کے مرتبہ میں ہو گیا۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مکی اور میقاتی کے لئے احناف کے نزدیک نہ تمتع ہے اور نہ قرآن ہے بلکہ ان کے لئے فقط حج افراد ہے اس کے باوجود اگر مکی یا میقات کے اندر رہنے والے نے تمتع یا قرآن کیا تو جائز ہو تو جائے گا مگر گنہ گار ہوگا۔ اور اس کی وجہ سے اس پر دم جبر لازم ہوگا۔ امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ مکی اور میقاتی کے لئے تمتع اور قران تو جائز ہے لیکن ان پر تمتع اور قران کا دم واجب نہیں ہوتا جیسا کہ آفاقی پر واجب ہوتا ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ باری تعالیٰ کا قول فَمَن تَمَتَّعَ بِالْعُمْرَةِ إِلَى الْحَقِّ فَمَا اسْتَيْسَرَ مِنَ الْهَدْي (البقرة: ۱۹۶) مطلق ہے آفاقی اور کی کی اس میں کوئی تفصیل نہیں ہے اس لئے تمتع اور قران آفاقی دونوں کے لئے مشروع ہوگا۔ ہماری دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا یہ قول ہے ذَالِكَ لِمَن لَّمْ يَكُنُ الآية یعنی يتمتع اس کے لئے ہے جس کے گھر والے مسجد حرام کے پاس نہ رہتے ہوں یعنی حج تمتع غیر کی یعنی آفاقی کے لئے ہے۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ مکی کے لئے تمتع نہیں ہے۔ اس آیت میں ذلک کا مشار الیہ ہمارے نزدیک تمتع ہے۔ اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک وجوب ہدی کا حکم ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ حج تمتع اور حج قران کو اس لئے مشروع کیا گیا ہے تا کہ عمرہ اور حج کے دوسفروں میں سے ایک کو ساقط کر کے آرام دیا جا سکے اور یہ راحت آفاقی کے حق میں ہے یعنی ان لوگوں کے حق میں ہے جو میقات سے باہر رہتے ہیں۔ صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا ہے کہ میقات کے اندر رہنے والے تمام لوگ مکی کے حکم میں ہیں چنانچہ مکی کی طرح میقاتی کے لئے بھی تمتع اور قران نہ ہو گا۔ ہاں اگر کوئی مکی اشہر حج سے پہلے کوفہ چلا گیا اور وہاں سے قران کیا تو بلا کراہت جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کا عمرہ اور حج دونوں میقاتی ہیں اس لئے یہ
For the people of Makkah, there is no Tamattu' and no Qiran; rather they have only Ifrad specifically, contrary to al-Shafi'i. The proof against him is the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'That is for him whose family is not present at al-Masjid al-Haram.' And because the legislation of these two is for comfort by dropping one of the two journeys, and this is for the Afaqi (one from distant regions). And whoever is within the Miqat, he is in the same status as a Makkan, so Tamattu' and Qiran are not for him. Contrary to the Makkan if he goes out to Kufah and performs Qiran, it is valid because his Umrah and Hajj are both from the Miqat, so he becomes like an Afaqi.
[Translation of the rest follows...]
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the permissibility of Tamattu' and Qiran for the people of Makkah and those within the Miqat. The Hanafi position is that Makkans and residents within the Miqat may only perform Ifrad (Hajj without Umrah); Tamattu' and Qiran are not prescribed for them. If they do perform them, it is valid but sinful, and they owe a compensatory dam. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that Tamattu' and Qiran are permissible for everyone, including Makkans, and that the obligation of dam for Tamattu' and Qiran applies to all alike. The Hanafi proof is the verse 'That is for him whose family is not present at al-Masjid al-Haram' (Surah al-Baqarah, 2:196), interpreting 'that' as referring to Tamattu'. The second proof is that Tamattu' and Qiran were legislated to provide ease by eliminating one of the two journeys, which is only needed by those who come from far away (Afaqi). The commentary also explains that if a Makkan travels outside the Miqat (e.g., to Kufah) and then returns with the intention of Qiran, it becomes valid because his journeys now originate from a distance. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the Hanafi view.

Key Terms
آفاقي (afaqi): A person whose home is outside the Miqat, i.e., from distant regions.
ميقات (miqat): The designated boundary for entering Ihram; those living within the Miqat are considered like Makkans.
إفراد (ifrad): Performing Hajj only without Umrah in the same journey.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person living in Makkah performs Hajj al-Tamattu', what is the ruling?
A) It is invalid and must be repeated as Ifrad.
B) It is valid but sinful, and a dam is required.
C) It is completely valid without any sin or dam.
D) It is permissible only if the person leaves Makkah before Ihram.

Key Takeaway
Makkans and those within the Miqat may only perform Ifrad; Tamattu' and Qiran are reserved for those coming from beyond the Miqat (afaqi).

Returning Home Without Hadi Voids Tamattu'
Ruling that returning home without Hadi voids Tamattu'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a Mutamatti' who returns home without Hadi and explain the evidence from Tabi'i practice.

Core Idea
Returning home between 'Umrah and Hajj without a sacrificial animal voids the Tamattu' arrangement.

This passage addresses a specific scenario in Hajj Tamattu': what happens if a pilgrim performs 'Umrah in the months of Hajj, returns to his hometown, and then comes back for Hajj without having brought a sacrificial animal (Hadi)? The passage delivers a clear ruling that his Tamattu' becomes void by consensus of the Hanafi school, based on the practice of the righteous predecessors (Tabi'in). Understanding this helps avoid common mistakes in performing Hajj with the correct intention and ritual status.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Identify that the person is a Mutamatti' who has completed 'Umrah and intends to perform Hajj in the same year.
2
Check the condition of Hadi
Determine whether he drove a sacrificial animal (Hadi) with him when he returned home. This is the key factor.
3
State the ruling
If he returned home without Hadi, his Tamattu' becomes void (batil). If he had Hadi, the ruling is different (deferred to next passage).
4
Explain the 'illa
The effective cause (al-Imam) is that he alighted at his home between the two rituals, breaking the required continuity.
Al-Imam means returning to one's residence and settling there.
5
Note the evidence
The ruling is supported by the practice of a group of Tabi'in, as narrated by Imam al-Tahawi from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib, 'Ata', Mujahid, and Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا عَادَ الْمُتَمَعُ إِلى بَلَدِهِ بَعْدَ فَرَاغِهِ مِنَ الْعُمْرَةِ وَلَمْ يَكُنْ سَاقَ الْهَدْيَ بَطَلَ تَمَتَّعُهُ لِأَنَّهُ أَلَمْ بِأَهْلِهِ فِيْمَا بَينَ نُسُكَيْن المَامًا صَحِيعًا وَبِذَلِكَ يَبْطُلُ التَّمَتَّعُ كَذَا رُوِيَ عَنْ عِدَةٍ مِّنَ التَّابِعِين

ترجمہ: اور اگر متمع عمرہ سے فارغ ہو کر اپنے وطن لوٹ آیا اور اس نے سوق بدی بھی نہیں کی تھی تو اس کا تمتع باطل ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ اس نے دونوں نسک یعنی حج و عمرہ کے درمیان المام صحیح کر لیا۔ اور ایسا کرنے سے تمتع باطل ہو جاتا ہے یونہی تابعین کی ایک جماعت سے روایت کیا گیا ہے۔

تشریح: آفاقی جو اشہر حج میں عمرہ کرنے والا ہے افعال عمرہ ادا کر کے اپنے وطن لوٹ آیا پھر ای سال حج کیا تو بشخص متمتع ہوگا یا نہیں۔ اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں ایک تو یہ کہ وہ شخص ہدی کا جانور ساتھ لے کر گیا تھا، دوم یہ کہ بدی کا جانور ساتھ نہیں لے گیا تھا۔ پہلی صورت کا حکم اگلی عبارت میں آرہا ہے اور دوسری صورت میں باتفاق احناف اس کا تمتع باطل ہو جائے گا۔ اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حج اور عمرہ کے درمیان اس شخص کا اپنے وطن میں المام صحیح کرنا پایا گیا۔ اور امام صحیح کرنے سے تمتع باطل ہو جاتا ہے اس لئے اس کا تمتع باطل ہو گیا۔ اسی طرح تابعین کی ایک جماعت سے روایت کیا گیا ہے۔ چنانچہ امام طحاوی نے اس کو سعید بن المسیب ، عطاء بن ابی رباح مجاہد اور ابراہیم مخفی سے روایت کیا ہے۔
And when the Mutamatti' returns to his city after finishing the 'Umrah and he had not driven the Hadi, his Tamattu' becomes void because he performed a valid al-Imam (alighting) with his family between the two rituals. And by that, Tamattu' becomes void. Thus it is narrated from a group of the Tabi'in. Translation: And if the Mutamatti' after finishing 'Umrah returns to his homeland and he had not driven the Hadi, then his Tamattu' becomes void. Because he performed a valid al-Imam between the two rituals (i.e., Hajj and 'Umrah). And by doing so, Tamattu' becomes void. Similarly, it is narrated from a group of the Tabi'in. Explanation: The Afaqi who performs 'Umrah in the months of Hajj, after performing the actions of 'Umrah returns to his homeland, then in the same year performs Hajj—will he be considered a Mutamatti' or not? There are two scenarios: first, he had taken the sacrificial animal (Hadi) with him; second, he had not taken the Hadi with him. The ruling of the first scenario is coming in the next sentence. In the second scenario, by consensus of the Hanafis, his Tamattu' becomes void. The proof is that between Hajj and 'Umrah, this person performed a valid al-Imam in his homeland. And by performing al-Imam, Tamattu' becomes void. Similarly, it is narrated from a group of the Tabi'in. Thus, Imam al-Tahawi narrated it from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib, 'Ata' ibn Abi Rabah, Mujahid, and Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.
Source pages p. 401

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling with proof regarding a Mutamatti' (one performing Hajj Tamattu') who returns to his hometown after completing 'Umrah but before performing Hajj. The key condition is whether he drove a sacrificial animal (Hadi) with him. If he did not bring the Hadi, then his Tamattu' becomes void by consensus of the Hanafis. The reason ('illa) is that he alighted (al-Imam) at his home between the two rituals (Hajj and 'Umrah) in a valid manner. This al-Imam breaks the continuity required for Tamattu'. The passage supports this ruling by citing the practice of a group of Tabi'in, including Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib, 'Ata', Mujahid, and Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, as narrated by Imam al-Tahawi. The second scenario, where he did drive the Hadi, is deferred to the next passage. Thus, the rule serves as a clear statement: returning home between 'Umrah and Hajj without having the Hadi invalidates the Tamattu' arrangement. The underlying rationale is that Tamattu' is a concession meant to combine two journeys; once one returns home, the need for the concession dissolves.

Key Terms
المام (al-Imam): To alight or stay at home, meaning to return to one's residence and settle there between the two rituals.
متمتع (Mutamatti'): One who performs Hajj Tamattu', i.e., performs 'Umrah then Hajj in the same year with a break.
ھدی (Hadi): A sacrificial animal (usually a camel, cow, or goat) brought for the ritual.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to a Mutamatti' who completes 'Umrah, returns to his home city without having driven any Hadi, and then performs Hajj in the same year?
A) His Tamattu' remains valid and no dam is required.
B) His Tamattu' becomes void by consensus of Hanafis.
C) His Hajj becomes invalid (batil).
D) He must repeat the 'Umrah.

Key Takeaway
A Mutamatti' who returns home between 'Umrah and Hajj without a sacrificial animal voids his Tamattu' arrangement by Hanafi consensus.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Mutamatti' Returning with Hadi
Intra-Hanafi dispute on driving Hadi and returning home

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the positions of the Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad on the effect of driving Hadi on a Mutamatti' returning home, and apply the Shaykhayn's reasoning to determine the validity of Tamattu'.

Core Idea
Driving Hadi restrains a Mutamatti' from exiting ihram, so returning home does not void Tamattu' per Shaykhayn.

This passage addresses a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the status of a Mutamatti' who drives a sacrificial animal (Hadi) and returns home after 'Umrah before Hajj. According to the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), the Tamattu' remains intact because the Hadi prevents him from becoming halal, making his return a non-event. However, Imam Muhammad argues that the return breaks the continuity, voiding the Tamattu'. Understanding this nuance is crucial for correctly managing the Hajj rituals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the two Hanafi positions
The issue is whether returning home after 'Umrah voids Tamattu' when Hadi is driven. Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf: Tamattu' does not become void. Muhammad: Tamattu' becomes void.
Both sides agree on the factual scenario: the Mutamatti' drove Hadi and returned home.
2
Examine the key factor: driving Hadi
The dispute hinges on the legal effect of driving Hadi on the state of ihram. Does it prevent tahallul (exiting ihram)?
Driving Hadi is a sign of persistence in ihram.
3
Analyze the Shaykhayn's proof
They argue that driving Hadi prevents tahallul, so the Mutamatti' remains in a continuous state of ihram for Tamattu'. Hence, returning home is not a valid break; he is still bound to perform Hajj as a Mutamatti'.
The key phrase: 'al-sawqu yamna'uhu min al-tahallul'.
4
Analyze Imam Muhammad's proof
He argues that the return home shows the two rituals ('Umrah and Hajj) were performed in separate journeys, which negates the continuity required for Tamattu'.
Muhammad's proof: 'annahu adahuma bi safaratayn'.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
Practical consequence: according to Shaykhayn, he performs Hajj as a Mutamatti' and must offer dam; according to Muhammad, Tamattu' is void. The mufta bihi is the Shaykhayn's position.
The tarjih is based on the principle that driving Hadi imposes an additional restriction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا سَاقَ الْهَدْىَ فَالْمَا مُدَّ لَا يَكُونُ صَحِيحًا وَلَا يَبْطُلُ تَمَتَّعُهُ عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَأَبِي يُوسُفَ وَ قَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ يَبْطُلُ لأنَّه أَذًا هُمَا بِسَفَرَتَيْنِ وَلُهُمَا أنَّ الْعُوْدَ مُسْتَحَقِّ عَلَيْهِ مَا دَامَ عَلى نِيَّةِ التَّمَتُّع لأنَّ السَّوقَ يَمْنَعُهُ مِنَ التَّحلل فَلَا يَصِحُ المَامُهُ بِخِلَافِ الْمَكِّى إِذَا خَرَجَ إِلَى الْكُوفَةِ وَ أَخَرَ مَ لِعُمْرَةٍ وَسَاقَ الْهَدَى حَيْثُ لَمْ يَكُنْ مُتَمَتِّعَا لأنَّ الْعُوْدَ هُنَالِكَ غَيْرُ مُسْتَحَق عَلَيْهِ فَصَحُ الْمَامُهُ بِأَهْلِهِ

ترجمہ: اور اگر اس نے ہدی کا جانور چلایا تو اس کا المام صیح نہ ہوگا۔ اور ابوحنیفہ اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک تمتع باطل نہ ہوگا اور امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ تمتع باطل ہو جائے گا کیونکہ اس نے عمرہ اور حج کو دو سفروں میں ادا کیا ہے۔ شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب تک و تمتع کی نیت پر ہے اس پر لوٹنا واجب ہے کیونکہ سوق بدی اس کو حلال ہونے سے مانع ہے۔ تو اس کا المام صحیح نہ ہو گا۔ برخلاف مکی کے جب وہ کوفہ کی طرف نکلا اور عمرہ کا احرام باندھا اور بدی کو چلایا تو وہ متمتع نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس پر یہاں لوٹنا واجب نہیں ہے تو اس کا المام اس کے وطن میں صحیح ہو گیا۔
And if he drove the Hadi, then his al-Imam is not valid, and his Tamattu' does not become void according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. And Muhammad said it becomes void because he performed them (Hajj and 'Umrah) in two journeys. And their (Shaykhayn) proof is that as long as he is on the intention of Tamattu', returning (al-'Awf) is required (mustahaqq) upon him, because driving the Hadi prevents him from becoming halal (by exiting ihram). So his al-Imam is not valid. Contrary to the Makkan if he goes out to Kufa and enters ihram for 'Umrah and drives the Hadi, he is not a Mutamatti' because there, returning is not required upon him, so his al-Imam with his family is valid. Translation: And if he drove the Hadi, then his al-Imam is not valid, and his Tamattu' does not become void according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. And Imam Muhammad said that it becomes void because he performed Hajj and 'Umrah in two journeys. The proof of the two Shaykh (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that as long as he is upon the intention of Tamattu', it is obligatory upon him to return (to Makkah for Hajj) because driving the Hadi prevents him from becoming halal (by exiting ihram). So his al-Imam is not valid. Contrary to the Makkan who goes to Kufa and enters ihram for 'Umrah and drives the Hadi, he is not a Mutamatti' because there, returning is not required, so his al-Imam with his family is valid.
Source pages p. 401

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute. The issue is: a Mutamatti' who drove a sacrificial animal (Hadi) and, after completing 'Umrah, returns to his hometown before performing Hajj — does the Tamattu' remain valid? According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the Shaykhayn), his Tamattu' does not become void because his al-Imam (alighting at home) is not considered valid. The reason is that driving the Hadi indicates he remains in a continuous state of ihram; he cannot remove it until after the Hajj. Therefore, returning home is not a true break from the rituals. In contrast, Imam Muhammad argues that Tamattu' becomes void because the person has effectively performed the two journeys separately (clearly going home in between). The passage concludes by contrasting the case of a Makkan who goes to Kufa, assumes ihram for 'Umrah with a Hadi, but is not a Mutamatti' — for him, al-Imam at home is valid because he is not in the state of Tamattu'. This highlights that the ruling hinges on the special status of a Mutamatti' who is in a continuous state. The mufta bihi position is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: Tamattu' is preserved if Hadi was driven.

Key Terms
سوق الھدی (Sawq al-Hadi): Driving or bringing along a sacrificial animal intended for the ritual.
المام (al-Imam): Alighting at home, breaking the journey.
تحلل (Tahallul): To exit the state of ihram, becoming permissible (halal) to do normal activities.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, if a Mutamatti' drives Hadi and returns home after 'Umrah, what is the status of his Tamattu'?
A) It becomes void because he returned home.
B) It remains valid because driving Hadi prevents him from exiting ihram.
C) He must repeat the 'Umrah.
D) He must perform Hajj as Qiran instead.

Key Takeaway
The Shaykhayn's position that driving Hadi prevents tahallul, thereby preserving Tamattu' despite returning home, is the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school.

Returning Home After Umrah in Tamattu' – Effect of Hady
Intra-Hanafi dispute on effect of hady on tamattu'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a mutamatti' returning home after Umrah with and without hady, and explain the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf regarding the validity of tamattu'.

Core Idea
A valid al-mam (returning home) between Umrah and Hajj invalidates tamattu'; bringing a hady prevents a valid al-mam, preserving tamattu'.

This lesson explores a key intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the tamattu' form of Hajj. When a mutamatti' (one performing Hajj with Umrah in the same journey) returns to his hometown after completing Umrah, does his tamattu' remain valid? The answer depends on whether he has brought a sacrificial animal (hady). We will unpack the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, focusing on the concept of al-mam (returning home) and its legal effect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The source text presents two cases: a mutamatti' returning home after Umrah without hady, and one returning with hady. Identify the ruling for each case as presented.
The scenario without hady is unanimous; the scenario with hady involves a dispute.
2
State the consensus on the no-hady scenario
According to the text, if the mutamatti' returns home without hady, his tamattu' becomes invalid (batil) by consensus of the Hanafi school. Understand why: he performed a valid al-mam (returning to his family) between the two rites.
This ruling is supported by narrations from the Tabi'un.
3
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on the hady scenario
If the mutamatti' brought a hady, there is disagreement. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold tamattu' remains valid; Imam Muhammad holds it becomes invalid. Note the basis of each view.
The two shaykhs' view is the mufta bihi (relied-upon position).
4
Examine the proofs of each side
Muhammad argues that the person performed Hajj and Umrah in two separate journeys, contradicting tamattu' which requires a single journey. The two shaykhs argue that the hady prevents tahallul after Umrah, so returning home is not a valid al-mam; it is fasid (defective), and a fasid al-mam does not invalidate tamattu'.
This is a rational proof based on the legal effect of bringing a hady.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its practical consequence
The relied-upon position is that of the two shaykhs: tamattu' is not invalidated by returning with hady. The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is that according to this view, the person remains a mutamatti' and must sacrifice a hady; according to Muhammad, he is no longer a mutamatti' and has no such obligation.
This affects whether the pilgrim owes a dam (penalty) for missing the wajib of tamattu'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب الحج
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد
س آفاقی کے مرتبہ میں ہو گیا۔ اور آفاقی چونکہ قران کر سکتا ہے اس لئے اس شخص کے لئے بھی قرآن کی اجازت ہوگی ۔ یہ خیال رہے کہ اگر کوئی مکی اشہر حج شروع ہونے کے بعد کوفہ گیا تو اس کے لئے قران ممنوع ہوگا۔
متمتع عمرہ کے بعد اپنے شہر لوٹ آئے متمتع شمار ہوگا یا نہیں
وَإِذَا عَادَ الْمُتَمَعُ إِلى بَلَدِهِ بَعْدَ فَرَاغِهِ مِنَ الْعُمْرَةِ وَلَمْ يَكُنْ سَاقَ الْهَدْيَ بَطَلَ تَمَتَّعُهُ لِأَنَّهُ أَلَمْ بِأَهْلِهِ فِيْمَا بَينَ نُسُكَيْن المَامًا صَحِيعًا وَبِذَلِكَ يَبْطُلُ التَّمَتَّعُ كَذَا رُوِيَ عَنْ عِدَةٍ مِّنَ التَّابِعِين

تشریح آفاقی جو اشہر حج میں عمرہ کرنے والا ہے افعال عمرہ ادا کر کے اپنے وطن لوٹ آیا پھر ای سال حج کیا تو بشخص متمتع ہوگا یا نہیں۔ اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں ایک تو یہ کہ وہ شخص ہدی کا جانور ساتھ لے کر گیا تھا، دوم یہ کہ بدی کا جانور ساتھ نہیں لے گیا تھا۔ پہلی صورت کا حکم اگلی عبارت میں آرہا ہے اور دوسری صورت میں باتفاق احناف اس کا تمتع باطل ہو جائے گا۔ اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حج اور عمرہ کے درمیان اس شخص کا اپنے وطن میں المام صحیح کرنا پایا گیا۔ اور امام صحیح کرنے سے تمتع باطل ہو جاتا ہے اس لئے اس کا تمتع باطل ہو گیا۔ اسی طرح تابعین کی ایک جماعت سے روایت کیا گیا ہے۔ چنانچہ امام طحاوی نے اس کو سعید بن المسیب ، عطاء بن ابی رباح مجاہد اور ابراہیم مخفی سے روایت کیا ہے۔
اگر سائق الھدی تھا تو اس کے لوٹنے سے تمتع پر فرق پڑے گا یا نہیں، اقوال فقہاء وَإِذَا سَاقَ الْهَدْىَ فَالْمَا مُدَّ لَا يَكُونُ صَحِيحًا وَلَا يَبْطُلُ تَمَتَّعُهُ عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَأَبِي يُوسُفَ وَ قَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ يَبْطُلُ لأنَّه أَذًا هُمَا بِسَفَرَتَيْنِ وَلُهُمَا أنَّ الْعُوْدَ مُسْتَحَقِّ عَلَيْهِ مَا دَامَ عَلى نِيَّةِ التَّمَتُّع لأنَّ السَّوقَ يَمْنَعُهُ مِنَ التَّحلل فَلَا يَصِحُ المَامُهُ بِخِلَافِ الْمَكِّى إِذَا خَرَجَ إِلَى الْكُوفَةِ وَ أَخَرَ مَ لِعُمْرَةٍ وَسَاقَ الْهَدَى حَيْثُ لَمْ يَكُنْ مُتَمَتِّعَا لأنَّ الْعُوْدَ هُنَالِكَ غَيْرُ مُسْتَحَق عَلَيْهِ فَصَحُ الْمَامُهُ بِأَهْلِهِ
ترجمہ اور اگر اس نے ہدی کا جانور چلایا تو اس کا المام صیح نہ ہوگا۔ اور ابوحنیفہ اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک تمتع باطل نہ ہوگا اور امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ تمتع باطل ہو جائے گا کیونکہ اس نے عمرہ اور حج کو دو سفروں میں ادا کیا ہے۔ شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب تک و تمتع کی نیت پر ہے اس پر لوٹنا واجب ہے کیونکہ سوق بدی اس کو حلال ہونے سے مانع ہے۔ تو اس کا المام صحیح نہ ہو گا۔ برخلاف مکی کے جب وہ کوفہ کی طرف نکلا اور عمرہ کا احرام باندھا اور بدی کو چلایا تو وہ متمتع نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس پر یہاں لوٹنا واجب نہیں ہے تو اس کا المام اس کے وطن میں صحیح ہو گیا۔ تشریح اس عبارت میں پہلی صورت کا بیان ہے۔ حاصل اس کا یہ ہے کہ تمتع جو ہدی کا جانور ساتھ لے کر گیا۔ افعال عمرہ ادا کر کے اپے والٹن واپس چلا گیا پھر اسی سال حج کیا تو شیخین کے نزدیک اس کا تمتع باطل نہ ہوگا ۔ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک باطل ہو جائے گا۔ امام محمد
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم
۴۰۱
کتاب الحج کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس شخص نے حج اور عمرہ کو دوسفروں میں ادا کیا ہے حالانکہ متمتع دونوں کو ایک سفر میں ادا کرتا ہے اس لئے شخص متمتع نہ گا۔ شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب تک یہ شخص نیست تمتع پر ہے اس پر وطن سے لوٹ کر مکتہ المکرمہ واپس آنا لازم ہے۔ کیونکہ ہدی کا چلانا اس کے لئے حلال ہونے سے مانع ہے۔ پس اس کا یہ المام صیح نہ ہوا بلکہ فاسد ہوا۔ اور المام فاسد ہے تمتع باطل نہیں ہوتا اس لئے اس کا تمتع باطل نہ ہو گا۔ برخلاف مکی کے کیونکہ مکی جب کوفہ گیا اور عمرہ کا احرام باندھا اور بدی کا جانور چلایا تو وہ تمع نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس میں وطن چونکہ عین مکہ ہے اس لئے اس پر عود واجب نہیں ہے۔ عود سے مراد یہ ہے کہ وطن سے مکہ چلا جائے اور یہ شخص چونکہ مکی ہے اس لئے اس کے حق میں وطن سے مکہ کی طرف واپس آنا ممکن نہیں بہر حال اس کا الہام صحیح ہو گا اور جب المهام صحیح ہو گیا تو تمتع باطل ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ المام صحیح سے تمتع باطل ہو جاتا ہے۔ المسام کی تعریف اور تقسیم ابتدائے باب میں گذر چکی ہے وہاں ملاحظہ کر لیا جائے ۔
When a mutamatti' returns to his country after completing his Umrah and he did not bring the hady (sacrificial animal), his tamattu' is invalidated because he performed a valid al-mam (returning to his family) between the two rites, and by that tamattu' is invalidated. Thus it is narrated from a group of the Tabi'un. Translation: If a mutamatti' returns home after Umrah and did not bring the hady, his tamattu' becomes invalid because he performed a valid al-mam between the two rites. This invalidates tamattu', as narrated from a group of Tabi'un. Commentary: An afaqi (one from outside Mecca) who performed Umrah in the months of Hajj, returned home, then performed Hajj the same year, is he considered a mutamatti'? Two cases: (1) He took the hady animal, (2) He did not take it. The first case's ruling comes later; in the second, by consensus of the Hanafis, his tamattu' is invalidated because a valid al-mam occurred between Hajj and Umrah. Al-mam invalidates tamattu'. This is narrated from Tabi'un like Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib, 'Ata', Mujahid, and Ibrahim al-Nakha'i. If he was saq al-hady (bringing the hady), his al-mam is not valid, and according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf his tamattu' is not invalidated, but Muhammad says it is invalidated because he performed the two rites in two journeys. The two shaykhs argue that as long as he is on the intention of tamattu', returning is obligatory upon him because bringing the hady prevents him from tahallul, so his al-mam is not valid. Unlike the Meccan who left for Kufa and performed Umrah with hady; he is not a mutamatti' because returning is not obligatory on him, so his al-mam is valid. Translation: If he brought the hady, his al-mam is not correct; according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf his tamattu' is not invalid, but Muhammad says it is invalid because he performed the two rites in two journeys. The two shaykhs argue: as long as he is on the intention of tamattu', returning is obligatory because the hady prevents tahallul, so his al-mam is not valid. Unlike a Meccan who goes to Kufa, enters ihram for Umrah, and brings hady; he is not a mutamatti' because returning is not obligatory on him. Commentary continues: Explaining the first case, the one who brought hady and returned home, then performed Hajj the same year: according to the two shaykhs his tamattu' is not invalid, but according to Muhammad it is invalid. Imam Muhammad's proof: he performed Hajj and Umrah in two journeys, while a mutamatti' performs both in one journey. The two shaykhs' proof: as long as he is on the intention of tamattu', returning from his hometown to Mecca is obligatory because the hady prevents tahallul. So his al-mam is invalid (fasid), and a fasid al-mam does not invalidate tamattu'. Unlike a Meccan, because his homeland is 'ayn Makkah, so returning is not possible; thus his al-mam is valid, and a valid al-mam invalidates tamattu'. The definition and division of al-mam has already passed at the beginning of the chapter.
Source pages p. 401

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on a mutamatti' who performs Umrah during the months of Hajj, then returns to his hometown before performing Hajj. The text presents two scenarios: without hady and with hady. In the first scenario (without hady), there is consensus among Hanafis that his tamattu' is invalidated because he has performed a valid al-mam (returning to his family) between the two rites. This is supported by narrations from several Tabi'un. In the second scenario (with hady), there is an intra-Hanafi dispute. Imam Muhammad argues that tamattu' is invalid because the person performed the two rites in two separate journeys, which contradicts the nature of tamattu'. However, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two shaykhs) argue that as long as the person intends tamattu', returning is obligatory because the hady prevents him from making tahallul (becoming halal). Therefore, his al-mam is not valid (it is fasid), and a fasid al-mam does not invalidate tamattu'. The passage contrasts this with a Meccan who leaves Mecca for Kufa, performs Umrah with hady, and then returns; he is not a mutamatti' because returning is not obligatory on him, so his al-mam is valid and he does not become a mutamatti'. The key concept here is al-mam, which means returning home between the two rites. If it is valid (sahih), it invalidates tamattu'; if it is fasid (invalid but not nullifying), tamattu' remains valid. The madhhab distinction is important: the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is the view of the two shaykhs that tamattu' is not invalidated by returning home with hady.

Key Terms
المام (al-mam): Returning to one's hometown and family between the two rites (Umrah and Hajj) in tamattu'.
سوق الهدي (sawq al-hady): Bringing a sacrificial animal (hady) while in ihram, which prevents the pilgrim from making tahallul (becoming halal) until the animal is sacrificed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on a mutamatti' who returns to his hometown after Umrah without bringing a hady?
A) His tamattu' remains valid.
B) His tamattu' becomes invalid.
C) This depends on whether he is a Meccan.
D) He must repeat the Umrah.

Key Takeaway
A valid al-mam (returning home) between Umrah and Hajj invalidates tamattu'; however, bringing a hady renders the al-mam fasid, preserving tamattu' according to the mufta bihi.
