Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
10 min
Determining Tamattu': The Majority of Tawaf in Hajj Months
Determines tamattu' status when Umrah ihram begins before Hajj months

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tamattu' status when the majority of tawaf circuits are performed in the months of Hajj, and distinguish it from the Shafi'i and Maliki positions.

Core Idea
Majority of tawaf in Hajj months determines tamattu', not the start of ihram.

When does a person who begins Umrah before the Hajj months become a mutamatti'? The Hanafi school answers with a precise rule: it depends on where most of the tawaf occurs. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning and contrasts it with the views of Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik, grounding the discussion in the source text from Al-Hidayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
The passage describes a person who enters ihram for Umrah before Shawwal, performs less than four circuits, then the months of Hajj begin, and he completes the tawaf and enters ihram for Hajj.
2
State the Hanafi Ruling
According to the Hanafi school, such a person is a mutamatti'. The key is that the majority of the tawaf (four or more circuits) was performed in the months.
If four or more circuits were done before the months, he is not a mutamatti'.
3
Understand the Legal Principle
The Hanafi proof rests on two points: ihram is a condition, not the determinant of time; the effective criterion is the performance of the acts. The maxim 'al-akthar hukm al-kull' (the majority has the ruling of the whole) applies.
This usul principle is widely used in Hanafi jurisprudence.
4
Contrast with Shafi'i and Maliki Positions
Imam Shafi'i considers the start of ihram decisive: if ihram is before the months, it cannot be tamattu' regardless of when acts are done. Imam Malik considers the completion (tahallul) in the months as decisive, even if acts are before.
The passage mentions that Shafi'i's proof is given but cuts off.
5
Apply to Given Cases
Using the Hanafi rule, determine the status in two cases: (a) 3 circuits before months, 4 after → mutamatti'. (b) 4 circuits before, 3 after → not mutamatti'.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is whether a hady is required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جس نے اشہر حج سے پہلے عمرہ کا احرام باندھا پھر چار سے کم طواف کے چکر کاٹے پھر اشہر حج داخل ہو گئے ان چکروں کو مکمل کیا اور حج کا احرام باندھا متمتع شمار ہوگا
وَمَنْ أَحْرَمَ بِعُمَرَةٍ قَبْلَ أَشْهُرٍ الْحَجِّ فَطَافَ لَهَا أَقلَ أَربَعَةِ أَشْوَاطِ ثُمَّ دَخَلَتْ أشهر الْحَجِّ فَتَمَّمَهَا وَأَحْرَمَ بِالْحَجِّ كَانَ مُتَمَتِّعَا لِأَنَّ الْإِحْرَامَ عِندَنَا شَرَطُ فَيَصِحُ تَقْدِيمُهُ عَلَى أَشْهُرِ الْحَجِّ وَإِنَّمَا يُعْتَبَرُ أَدَاء الْأَفْعَالِ فِيهَا وَقَدْ وُجِدَ الأكْثَرُ وَلِلأكثَرِ حُكْمُ الكُلّ وَإِنْ طَافَ لِعُمَرَتِهِ قَبْلَ أَشْهُرِ الْحَجَ أَرْبَعَةَ أَشْوَاطٍ فَصَاعِدَ اثُمَّ حَجَّ مِنْ عَامِهِ ذَلِكَ لَمْ يَكُنْ مُتَمَةٍ تَمَتِّعًا لأنه أدى الأكْثَرَ قَبْلَ أَشْهْرِ الْحَجّ وَهَذَا لِأَنَّهُ صَارَ بِحَالٍ لَا يُفْسِدُ نُسُكَهُ بِالْجَمَاعَ فَصَارَ كَمَا اذَا تَحَلَّلَ مِنْهَا قَبْلَ أَشْهُرِ الْحَقِّ وَمَالِكَ يَعْتَبِرُ الْإِنْمَامَ فِي أَشْهُرِ الْحَج وَالْحُجَّةُ عَلَيْهِ مَا ذَكَرَنَا وَلِأَنَّ التَرَفَقَ بِأَدَاءِ الأفْعَالِ وَالسَّمَعُ الْمُتَرَقِّقُ بِأدَاءِ التَسْكَيْنِ فِي سَفَرِةِ وَاحِدَةٍ فِي اَشْهُرِ الْحَجِّ
ترجمہ اور جس نے حج کے مہینوں سے پہلے عمرہ کا احرام باندھا اور عمرہ کے لئے چار شوط سے کم طواف کیا پھر حج کے مہینے آ گئے اور اس نے عمرہ پورا کیا اور حج کا احرام باندھا تو یہ شخص متمتع ہو گا۔ کیونکہ ہمارے نزدیک احرام شرط ہے اس لئے حج کے مہینوں پر اس کو مقدم کرنا صحیح ہے اور معتبر حج کے ایام میں افعال عمرہ کا ادا کرنا ہے اور حال یہ کہ اکثر کی ادائیگی پائی گئی اور اکثر کے واسطے کل کا حکم ہے۔ اور اگر حج کے مہینوں سے پہلے اکثر کو ادا کیا ہے اور یہ ایسے حال پر ہو گیا کہ اب جماع کرنے سے اس کا عمرہ باطل نہ ہوگا۔ پس یہ ایسا ہو گیا گویا ایام حج سے پہلے عمرہ سے حلال ہو گیا اور امام مالک ایام حج میں عمرہ کے پورا کرنے کا اعتبار کرتے ہیں۔ اور امام مالک کے خلاف وہ حجت ہے جس کو ہم ذکر کر چکے۔ اور اس لئے کہ ترفق ( فائدہ اٹھانا) افعال ادا کرنے کے ساتھ ہے اور مستمع وہ ہے جو ایام حج میں ایک سفر میں دونسک ادا کر کے فائدہ اٹھائے۔
تشریح اگر کسی نے اشہر حج سے پہلے عمرہ کا احرام باندھا تو اس میں تین مذہب ہیں۔ امام شافعی کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ اگر عمرہ کا احرام اشہر حج سے پہلے باندھا تو وہ تمتع نہ ہوگا۔ اگر چہ افعال عمرہ اشہر حج میں ادا کئے ہوں۔ اور امام مالک نے فرمایا ہے کہ یہ شخص متمتع ہے اگر چہ افعال عمرہ بھی اشہر حج میں ادا نہ کئے ہوں۔ بشرطیکہ عمرہ کے احترام سے حلال ہونا اشہر حج میں پایا جائے ۔ اور ہمارا مذ ہب یہ ہے کہ اگر چار شوط اشہر حج میں کئے اور تین اس سے پہلے کر چکا تو ی شخص متمتع ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر بر عکس ہے تو متمتع نہیں ہوگا۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے
One who enters ihram for Umrah before the months of Hajj, performs less than four circuits of tawaf, then the months of Hajj enter, and he completes the tawaf and enters ihram for Hajj, he is a mutamatti'. Because according to us, ihram is a condition, so advancing it before the months of Hajj is valid; what matters is the performance of the acts in the months, and the majority (of the tawaf) was performed in them, and the majority has the ruling of the whole. If he performed four or more circuits of tawaf for his Umrah before the months of Hajj, then performed Hajj in the same year, he is not a mutamatti' because he performed the majority before the months of Hajj, and he reached a state where intercourse does not invalidate his rite, so it is as if he had made tahallul from it before the months of Hajj. Malik considers completing the Umrah in the months of Hajj; the proof against him is what we mentioned. The benefit is achieved by performing the acts, and the mutamatti is one who benefits by performing both rites in one journey in the months of Hajj. Translation: One who enters ihram for Umrah before the months of Hajj, performs less than four circuits of tawaf, then the months enter, completes it, and enters ihram for Hajj, he is a mutamatti'. Because according to us, ihram is a condition, so advancing it is valid; what matters is performing the acts in the months, and the majority was performed in them, and the majority has the ruling of the whole. If he performed four or more circuits before the months, then performed Hajj the same year, he is not a mutamatti' because he performed the majority before the months, and he reached a state where intercourse does not invalidate his rite, so it is as if he had made tahallul before the months. Malik considers completing the Umrah in the months; the proof against him is what we mentioned. Benefit is achieved by performing the acts, and the mutamatti is the one who benefits by performing both rites in one journey in the months of Hajj. Commentary: There are three schools on this. Shafi'i: if ihram for Umrah is before the months, it is not tamattu', even if acts are in the months. Maliki: he is a mutamatti' even if acts are not in the months, provided tahallul occurs in the months. Our madhhab: if four circuits are in the months and three before, he is mutamatti'; if the reverse, he is not. Shafi'i's proof is... (cut off).
Source pages p. 402

Commentary
This passage deals with the scenario where a person enters ihram for Umrah before the months of Hajj (Shawwal, Dhul Qa'dah, first ten days of Dhul Hijjah) but performs only a few circuits of tawaf before the months begin. The Hanafi ruling is that such a person is a mutamatti' if most of the tawaf (at least half, i.e., four or more circuits out of seven) is performed during the months. The reasoning is that ihram is merely a condition, and the actual performance of the acts is what matters. Since the majority of the tawaf occurs in the months, it is as if the entire Umrah was performed in the months. If, however, the person performs four or more circuits before the months, then completing the rest during the months does not make him a mutamatti', because he has effectively completed most of the Umrah before the months, and he has reached a state where sexual intercourse does not invalidate his rite (since he has performed most of the tawaf), as if he had made tahallul. The passage contrasts the Hanafi position with Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik. Shafi'i holds that if ihram itself is before the months, it cannot be tamattu', regardless of when the acts are performed. Malik holds that the person is a mutamatti' as long as tahallul (completion of Umrah) occurs in the months, even if all acts are done before. The Hanafi school takes a middle position, focusing on the location of the majority of the actions. The passage also mentions that the benefit of tamattu' is achieved by performing both rites in one journey during the months of Hajj. This lesson is incomplete as the text cuts off during the explanation of Imam Shafi'i's proof.

Key Terms
أشهر الحج (ashhur al-hajj): The months of Hajj: Shawwal, Dhul Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhul Hijjah.
الأكثر حكم الكل (al-akthar hukm al-kull): A legal maxim meaning 'the majority has the ruling of the whole,' used here to determine that if most tawaf circuits are in the months, it is as if all are in the months.
متمتع (mutamatti'): A person who performs Umrah and then Hajj in the same journey during the months of Hajj, and is obligated to offer a hady.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does a person who enters ihram for Umrah before the months of Hajj become a mutamatti'?
A) If he completes the entire Umrah in the months.
B) If he performs most of the tawaf (four or more circuits) in the months.
C) If he performs most of the tawaf before the months.
D) If he delays tahallul until the months.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school determines tamattu' by where the majority of tawaf circuits are performed, not by the start of ihram.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Tamattu' with Umrah Begun Before Ashhur al-Hajj
Explains Hanafi ruling on tamattu' with three madhhab positions and proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on tamattu' when Umrah ihram precedes the months of Hajj, explain the proof based on the majority of tawaf, and distinguish the Shafi'i and Maliki positions and their practical consequences.

Core Idea
The majority of tawaf within ashhur al-Hajj suffices for tamattu'; ihram can precede the time.

This passage addresses a classic inter-madhhab dispute: what happens if a person begins Umrah before the months of Hajj (Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah, first 10 days of Dhul-Hijjah) and then completes the tawaf within those months? The Hanafi school holds that if the majority of tawaf (four out of seven circuits) is performed in the months, the person is a mutamatti'. This ruling hinges on a fundamental legal maxim: al-akthar lahu hukm al-kull (the majority has the ruling of the whole). We will analyse the proofs of the three schools and understand the practical difference in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Read the initial scenario: a person enters ihram for Umrah before Shawwal, performs less than four tawaf circuits, then the months of Hajj enter, completes the circuits, and then performs Hajj. This is the core case that triggers the dispute.
2
State the Hanafi position
According to the Hanafi school, this person is a mutamatti'. The key principle is that ihram is a condition (shart) that can validly precede the time, but the performance of the acts (af'al) is what matters. Since the majority of the tawaf (four circuits) was done in the months, it is as if all tawaf was done there.
Maxim: al-akthar lahu hukm al-kull.
3
Analyse the Shafi'i counter-argument
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that tamattu' requires both ihram and the acts to be within the months. Since ihram preceded, the combination is not achieved, so the person is not a mutamatti'. Identify the rukn vs. shart distinction.
Hanafis respond: ihram is a condition, not a pillar.
4
Analyse the Maliki position
Imam Malik focuses on the tahlul (becoming halal) occurring within the months. Even if the acts were outside, as long as the Umrah ends (tahlul) in the months, tamattu' is valid. The Hanafi rebuttal: ease (taraffuq) is by performing the acts, not merely the tahlul.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Work through the example: if three circuits in Ramadan and four in Shawwal → Hanafi says mutamatti', Shafi'i says not. If four in Ramadan and three in Shawwal → Hanafi says not, Shafi'i says not, Maliki says yes if tahlul in months. Understanding this helps in applying the ruling to real cases.

And whoever enters ihram for Umrah before the months of Hajj and performs less than four circuits of tawaf for it, then the months of Hajj enter and he completes them (the circuits) and enters ihram for Hajj, he is a mutamatti' because according to us ihram is a condition, so its precedence over the months of Hajj is valid. Rather, the performance of the acts within them is considered, and the majority has been found, and the majority has the ruling of the whole. And if he performed for his Umrah before the months of Hajj four circuits or more, then performed Hajj in that same year, he is not a mutamatti' because he performed the majority before the months of Hajj. This is because he reached a state where intercourse does not invalidate his rite, so he became like one who had become halal from it before the months of Hajj. And Malik considers completion within the months of Hajj, and the proof against him is what we mentioned, and because ease is achieved by performing the acts, and the mutamatti' is one who achieves ease by performing the two rites in one journey during the months of Hajj. Translation: And whoever entered ihram for Umrah before the months of Hajj and performed less than four circuits of tawaf for Umrah, then the months of Hajj came and he completed the Umrah and entered ihram for Hajj, then this person is a mutamatti'. Because according to us, ihram is a condition, so it is valid to give it precedence over the months of Hajj, and what is considered is performing the acts of Umrah in the days of Hajj, and the majority has been performed, and the majority has the ruling of the whole. And if he performed the majority before the months of Hajj, and he reached such a state that intercourse would not invalidate his Umrah, then he became like one who became halal from Umrah before the days of Hajj, and Imam Malik considers completing Umrah within the days of Hajj. And against Imam Malik the proof we have mentioned. And because ease is by performing the acts, and the mutamatti' is one who gains ease by performing both rites in one journey during the days of Hajj. Explanation: If someone entered ihram for Umrah before the months of Hajj, there are three madhhabs. The madhhab of Imam al-Shafi'i is that if he entered ihram for Umrah before the months of Hajj, he is not a mutamatti', even if he performed the acts of Umrah in the months of Hajj. And Imam Malik said that this person is a mutamatti' even if he did not perform the acts of Umrah in the months of Hajj, provided that becoming halal from the ihram of Umrah occurs in the months of Hajj. And our madhhab is that if he performed four circuits in the months of Hajj and three before that, then this person becomes a mutamatti'. And if the opposite, then he is not a mutamatti'. The proof of Imam al-Shafi'i is that for tamattu' it is necessary to combine both acts of worship, Umrah and Hajj, in the months of Hajj. And this is not found here because the rukn of Umrah, i.e., ihram, preceded the months of Hajj, so due to the absence of combining Umrah and Hajj in the months of Hajj, he is not a mutamatti'. The proof of Imam Malik is that in the mentioned case, the combining of both Umrah and Hajj is present, in that he became halal from the ihram of Umrah in the months of Hajj and also entered ihram for Hajj in the months of Hajj, i.e., in terms of becoming halal, both are found in the months of Hajj. So due to this combination, this person is called a mutamatti'. Our proof is that according to us, ihram is a condition, so giving precedence to ihram over the months of Hajj is permissible just as purification is permissible before the time of prayer. However, the performance of acts in the months of Hajj is considered. So when four circuits are found in the months of Hajj, it is as if the majority is found in the months of Hajj, and since the majority has the ruling of the whole, it will be said that the entire tawaf of Umrah is found in the months of Hajj. And when the entire tawaf is in the months of Hajj, then combining Umrah and Hajj in the months of Hajj is found, and since this combination is called tamattu', this person is a mutamatti'. And if he performed four circuits of tawaf before the months of Hajj and then performed Hajj in that same year, he is not a mutamatti' because he performed the majority before the months of Hajj. And since the majority has the ruling of the whole, it is as if he performed the entire tawaf before the months of Hajj, and a person in this case is not a mutamatti' because after performing four circuits, Umrah is not invalidated by intercourse. So this person became like one who became halal before the months of Hajj, and no one is a mutamatti' in the case of becoming halal from the ihram of Umrah before the months of Hajj. Therefore, he is also not a mutamatti'. Our second proof is that ease (comfort) is achieved by performing the acts, and the mutamatti' also gains ease by performing the two acts of worship, Hajj and Umrah, in one journey during the months of Hajj. Therefore, for being a mutamatti', it is necessary that all acts of Umrah or the majority occur in the months of Hajj.
Source pages p. 402

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute explaining the Hanafi ruling on tamattu' when Umrah is begun before the months of Hajj. The text first presents the matn: a person who enters ihram for Umrah before Shawwal, performs less than four circuits of tawaf, then the months of Hajj begin, completes the tawaf (now making four or more circuits within the months), and then enters ihram for Hajj—such a person is a mutamatti' according to the Hanafi school. The key principle is that ihram is a condition (shart) that can precede the time, but the actual performance of the acts (af'al) is what matters, and the majority of the acts must occur within the months of Hajj. The legal maxim 'al-akthar lahu hukm al-kull' (the majority has the ruling of the whole) is applied: four circuits out of seven is the majority, so it is as if all tawaf was done in the months. Conversely, if four circuits are done before the months, the majority is already completed before the months, so the person is not a mutamatti'. The text then outlines the three madhhabs: Imam Shafi'i requires both ihram and acts within the months; Imam Malik only requires becoming halal (tahlul) within the months, regardless of acts; the Hanafi school follows the principle of majority of acts. The Hanafi proofs include analogy to purification before prayer, the maxim of the majority, and the concept that ease (taraffuq) is attained by performing the acts within one journey during the months. This passage guards against the misunderstanding that tamattu' requires all Umrah acts to be in the months of Hajj, clarifying that the majority suffices.

Key Terms
تمتع (tamattu'): Performing Umrah and Hajj in one journey during the months of Hajj, with a break in between (tahlul).
أشهر الحج (ashhur al-Hajj): The months of Hajj: Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhul-Hijjah.
الأكثر له حكم الكل (al-akthar lahu hukm al-kull): A legal maxim stating that when the majority of an act is performed, it takes the ruling of the entire act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person enters ihram for Umrah in Ramadan, performs three circuits of tawaf, then in Shawwal completes the remaining four circuits, and then performs Hajj in the same journey, is he a mutamatti'?
A) Yes, because the majority of tawaf (four circuits) was performed in the months of Hajj.
B) No, because the ihram was before the months of Hajj.
C) Yes, because he completed the Umrah in the months of Hajj.
D) No, because he performed three circuits before the months.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, tamattu' is valid when the majority of the Umrah tawaf (four of seven circuits) is performed within the months of Hajj, even if ihram and the remaining circuits occur before the months.

Definition of the Months of Hajj (Ashhur al-Hajj)
Defines the months of Hajj with proof from Companions and rational argument

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of the months of Hajj and explain the proof from the Companions and the rational argument that defines them.

Core Idea
The months of Hajj are Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhul-Hijjah.

This lesson explores the precise definition of the months of Hajj, a key time frame for the pilgrimage. Al-Quduri presents the Hanafi view based on the authority of the three 'Abdullahs and a logical argument about the loss of Hajj after the tenth of Dhul-Hijjah. Understanding this definition affects the validity of the ihram for Hajj and the timing of its rites.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its definition
Recognise that the passage defines the 'months of Hajj' as a time limit for the pilgrimage rites, not as a ruling of obligation.
2
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school, following al-Quduri, holds that the months are Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhul-Hijjah.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
Examine the two proofs
The first proof is the narration from the three 'Abdullahs and Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr. The second proof is rational: the essential act of Hajj (wuquf at Arafah) occurs on the 9th, and after the 10th, Hajj is lost; thus the time ends after the 10th.
The narration is zanni al-thubut but qati al-dalala according to the Hanafis.
4
Compare with the opposing school
Imam Malik argues that the plural 'ashhur' in the Quran requires three full months, so all of Dhul-Hijjah is included. The Hanafi response is that the Companions' practice clarifies the Quranic expression.
Shafi'is and Hanbalis agree with the Hanafis on this point.
5
Recognise the practical consequence
If someone enters ihram for Hajj on the 15th of Dhul-Hijjah, it is invalid according to Hanafis (outside the months), but valid according to Malikis. This is the thamarah al-khilaf.

قَالَ وَأَشْهُرُ الْحَجِّ شَوَّالٌ وَ ذُو الْقعْدَةِ وَعَشَرٌ مِنْ ذِى الْحَجَّةِ كَذَا رُوى عَنِ الْعِبَادِلَةِ الثَّلَثَةِ وَعَبْدِ الله بن الزبير أَجْمَعِينَ وَلانَّ الْحَجَّ يَفُوتُ بمضى عَشْرِ ذِي الْحَجَّةِ وَمَعَ بَقَاءِ الْوَقْتِ لا يتحقَّقُ الْفَوَاتُ وَهَذَا يَدُلُّ عَلَى أَنَّ الْمُرَادَ مِنْ قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى الْحَجُ اَشْهُرٌ مَعْلُومَاتٌ به شهران وَبَعْضُ الثالث لا كله

The months of Hajj: He (al-Quduri) said: The months of Hajj are Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah, and ten days from Dhul-Hijjah. Thus it is narrated from the three 'Abdullahs and Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr, all of them. And because Hajj is missed with the passing of the ten days of Dhul-Hijjah, and with the remaining of the time, the loss does not realize, and this indicates that the meaning of the statement of Allah Almighty 'Al-Hajj ashhurun ma'lamat' is two months and part of the third, not all of it. Translation: Al-Quduri said that the months of Hajj are Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah, and ten days of Dhul-Hijjah. Thus it is narrated from the three 'Abdullahs and Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr. And because with the passing of ten days of Dhul-Hijjah, Hajj is missed, while with the remaining of the time, the loss does not realize, and this indicates that what is meant by the statement of Allah Almighty 'al-Hajj ashhurun ma'lamat' is two months and part of the third, not the entire third. Explanation: Sheikh Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri said that the months of Hajj are Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah, and ten days of Dhul-Hijjah. Imam Malik said that Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah, and the entire Dhul-Hijjah are the months of Hajj. The proof of Imam Malik is that Allah Almighty said 'al-Hajj ashhurun ma'lamat' and 'ashhur' is plural, and the minimum of plurality is three. So the full three months are the months of Hajj. Our proof is that it is narrated from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, Abdullah ibn Umar, Abdullah ibn Abbas, and Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr that the months of Hajj are Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah, and ten days of Dhul-Hijjah. The second proof is that with the passing of ten days of Dhul-Hijjah, Hajj is missed, meaning if someone does not perform the waqoof of Arafah and the Day of Sacrifice arrives, his Hajj is missed.
Source pages p. 403

Commentary
This passage defines the months of Hajj (ashhur al-Hajj) and presents the Hanafi ruling with proofs. The matn states that the months are Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhul-Hijjah, as narrated from the three 'Abdullahs (Ibn Mas'ud, Ibn Umar, Ibn Abbas) and Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr (may Allah be pleased with them). The rational proof is that the essential act of Hajj, the standing at Arafah, occurs on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah, and if it is missed, Hajj is lost after the 10th; thus the time for Hajj ends after the 10th, so only the first ten days are included. The Quranic phrase 'al-Hajju ashhurun ma'lamat' (Hajj is [in] known months) thus refers to two full months and part of the third. The text then mentions the disagreement of Imam Malik, who considers all of Dhul-Hijjah as part of the months based on the plural 'ashhur' implying three full months. The Hanafi response is that the practice of the noble Companions (the 'Abdullahs) confirms the first ten days, and the rational proof about the expiration of Hajj time supports this. This definition has practical implications: the time for entering ihram for Hajj begins from the first day of Shawwal, and the last time for the sacrifice (hadī) and other rites is the 13th of Dhul-Hijjah after the days of tashriq. Students should note that the Hanafi definition is based on transmitted proof (naql) from the Companions and rational proof (aql) about the loss of Hajj after the 10th.

Key Terms
أشهر الحج (ashhur al-Hajj): The months of Hajj: Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhul-Hijjah.
العبادلة الثلاثة (al-'Ibadilah al-thalathah): The three 'Abdullahs among the Companions: Ibn Mas'ud, Ibn Umar, and Ibn Abbas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhul-Hijjah
D) Only the ten days of Dhul-Hijjah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school, following the Companions, defines the months of Hajj as Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhul-Hijjah, concluding that the Quranic 'ashhur' refers to two months and part of the third.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate

Conditions for Tamattu': Hanafi View vs. Imam Malik
Explains when a person becomes Mutamatti' and refutes Imam Malik's alternative view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for becoming a Mutamatti' and contrast it with Imam Malik's position, applying the principle that the majority (akthar) takes the ruling of the whole.

Core Idea
For tamattu', the majority of Umrah acts must fall within the months of Hajj – akthar takes the ruling of the whole.

This lesson examines an inter-madhhab dispute about when a person becomes a Mutamatti' in Hajj. The Hanafi school insists that the performance of Umrah acts within the months of Hajj is critical, while Imam Malik focuses on the timing of becoming halal. Understanding this difference clarifies when tamattu' is valid and reveals the Hanafi jurisprudential method of treating the majority as the whole.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: a person becomes a Mutamatti' if the majority of Umrah acts (at least four circuits of tawaf) are performed within the months of Hajj. Note the principle that 'akthar yunazzalu manzilat al-kull' (the majority is treated as the whole) is applied here.
The Hanafi position is based on the performance of acts, not ihram or halal alone.
2
Identify the opposing school and its view
State that Imam Malik considers a person a Mutamatti' simply because the halal from both Umrah and Hajj occurs within the months of Hajj. For Malik, the combination (jam') is achieved through halal, not the timing of acts.
Malik focuses on the legal release (halal) rather than the physical performance of acts.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine Imam Malik's dalil: the person becomes halal from Umrah within the months (since the Hajj ihram is there) and also becomes halal from Hajj within the months, so both are present in the months. Thus, he becomes Mutamatti'.
Malik's reasoning is that halal is the key moment for combination.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school rebuts by clarifying that ihram is a condition (shart), not a pillar (rukn), so it can precede its time—like purification before prayer. What matters is the performance of acts within the months. The majority principle then completes the argument: if at least four circuits occur in the months, the entire tawaf is considered within the months, fulfilling the condition of tamattu'.
Second proof: ease (tarfuq) is only realized by performing acts within the months, not by ihram or halal timing.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if someone performs Umrah before Shawwal (e.g., in Ramadan) and then Hajj in the same year, according to Hanafis he is a Mutamatti' only if he performed at least four circuits of tawaf after Shawwal. According to Malik, he is always a Mutamatti' because his halal from Umrah occurs within the months of Hajj.
This difference affects whether the person must offer a hady (sacrifice) for tamattu'.

کتاب الحج ۴۰۲ اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم کر تمتع کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ عمرہ اور حج کی دونوں عبادتوں کو اشہر حج میں جمع کرے۔ اور یہاں یہ بات پائی نہیں گئی کیونکہ عمرہ کا رکن یعنی احرام اشہر حج پر مقدم ہو گیا ہے پس اشہر حج میں عمرہ اور حج کے جمع نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے متمتع نہیں ہوگا ۔ امام مالک کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مذکورہ صورت میں عمرہ اور حج دونوں کا جمع کرنا موجود ہے بایں طور کہ عمرہ کے احترام سے بھی اشہر حج میں حلال ہوا ہے اور حج کے احرام سے بھی اشہر حج میں حلال ہوا ہے یعنی با عتبار حلال ہونے کے دونوں اشہر حج میں پائے گئے ۔ پس اس اجتماع کی وجہ سے یہ شخص متمتع کہلائے گا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ہمارے نزدیک اجرام شرط ہے پس احترام کا اشہر حج پر مقدم کرنا اسی طرح جائز ہے جس طرح طہارت کا وقت صلوۃ پر مقدم کرنا جائز ہے۔ البتہ اشہر حج میں افعال کا ادا کرنا معتبر ہے پس جب چار شوط اشہر حج میں پائے گئے تو گویا اکثر اشہر حج میں پائے گئے اور اکثر کو چونکہ کل کا حکم حاصل ہے اس لئے کہا جائے گا کہ گویا پورا طواف عمرہ اشہر حج میں پایا گیا۔ اور جب پورا طواف اشہر حج میں ہے تو عمرہ و حج کو شہر حج میں جمع کر نا پایا گیا اور چونکہ اس جمع کا نام ہی تمتع ہے اس لئے یہ شخص متمتع ہو گا۔ اور اگر اشہر حج سے پہلے چارشو ط طواف کیا اور پھر اسی سال حج کیا تو متمتع نہیں۔ وگا کیونکہ اس نے اشہر حج سے پہلے اکثر کو ادا کیا ہے۔ اور اکثر کو چونکہ کل کا حکم حاصل ہے اس لیئے گویا اس نے پورا طواف اشہر حج سے پہلے کیا اور شخص اس صورت میں متمتع اس لئے نہیں ہوگا کہ چارشو طواف کرنے کے بعد عمرہ جماع کی وجہ سے فاسد نہیں ہوتا۔ پس یہ شخص ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ اشہر حج سے پہلے حلال ہو گیا ہو اور اشہر حج سے پہلے عمرہ کے احرام سے حلال ہونے کی صورت میں کوئی شخص متمتع نہیں ہوتا۔ اس لئے یہ بھی متمتع نہ ہوگا۔ ہماری دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ترفق یعنی راحت اٹھانا افعال کی ادائیگی سے ہوگا اور متمتع بھی اشہر حج میں ایک سفر میں حج اور عمرہ کی دو عبادتوں کو ادا کر کے راحت اٹھاتا ہے پس متمتع ہونے کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ اشہر حج میں تمام افعال عمرہ پائے جائیں یا اکثر پائے جائیں۔
The book of Hajj. 402. Ashraf al-Hidayah, an Urdu commentary on al-Hidayah, volume three. For tamattu', it is necessary that he combines both the acts of worship of 'Umrah and Hajj within the months of Hajj. And here this condition is not found because the pillar of 'Umrah, i.e. ihram, preceded the months of Hajj. Therefore, due to the lack of combining 'Umrah and Hajj within the months of Hajj, he will not become a Mutamatti'. The proof of Imam Malik is that in the mentioned situation, combining both 'Umrah and Hajj is present in that he became halal (discharged) from the ihram of 'Umrah within the months of Hajj and also became halal from the ihram of Hajj within the months of Hajj, i.e., in terms of becoming halal, both are found within the months of Hajj. Therefore, due to this combination, this person will be called Mutamatti'. Our proof is that in our view, ihram is a condition. Therefore, advancing ihram before the months of Hajj is permissible just as it is permissible to perform purification before the time of prayer. However, the performance of the acts within the months of Hajj is considered. So when four circuits [of tawaf] are found within the months of Hajj, then as if the majority is found within the months of Hajj, and since the majority takes the ruling of the whole, it will be said that as if the entire tawaf of 'Umrah was performed within the months of Hajj. And when the entire tawaf is within the months of Hajj, then combining 'Umrah and Hajj within the months of Hajj is found, and since the name of this combination is tamattu', this person will be a Mutamatti'. And if he performed four circuits of tawaf before the months of Hajj and then performed Hajj in the same year, he is not a Mutamatti'. Because he performed the majority before the months of Hajj, and since the majority takes the ruling of the whole, so it is as if he performed the entire tawaf before the months of Hajj. And this person in this case will not be Mutamatti' because after performing four circuits, the 'Umrah does not become invalid due to intercourse. So this person becomes like one who became halal before the months of Hajj, and no one becomes Mutamatti' in the case of becoming halal from the ihram of 'Umrah before the months of Hajj. Therefore, this person also will not be Mutamatti'. Our second proof is that 'tarfuq' (seeking ease) comes from performing the acts, and the Mutamatti' also gains ease by performing both acts of worship in a single journey within the months of Hajj. So for being Mutamatti', it is necessary that all the acts of 'Umrah are found within the months of Hajj, or the majority are found.
Source pages p. 403

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the conditions for becoming a Mutamatti' (one performing Tamattu' Hajj). Imam Malik argues that if a person performs Umrah before the months of Hajj and then Hajj in the same year, he becomes Mutamatti' because the halal (release from ihram) from both Umrah and Hajj occurs within the months of Hajj. The Hanafi school rebuts this by stating that ihram is a condition (shart), not a pillar (rukn), so it can precede its time, similar to purification for prayer. The key is the performance of acts within the months of Hajj. Using the Hanafi principle that the majority (akthar) takes the ruling of the whole, if at least four circuits of tawaf (the majority of the seven) occur in the months of Hajj, the entire tawaf is considered within the months, and thus tamattu' is achieved. If the majority occurs before the months, the person is not Mutamatti'. The second proof is based on the concept of ease (tarfuq): tamattu' is meant to combine two worships in one journey for ease, and this ease is only realized if the acts of Umrah are performed within the months of Hajj. Thus, the Hanafi position is that only if the majority of Umrah acts fall within the months of Hajj does one become a Mutamatti'.

Key Terms
تمتع (tamattu‘): A type of Hajj where one performs 'Umrah first and then Hajj in the same year, with a break in between, and enjoys the ease of combining both in one journey.
اشہر حج (ashhur al-hajj): The months of Hajj: Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhul-Hijjah.
اکثر (akthar): Majority; in this context, more than half (e.g., four out of seven circuits of tawaf) which takes the ruling of the whole in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) If he performs the entire Umrah after Shawwal.
B) If he performs at least four circuits of tawaf in the months of Hajj.
C) If he performs sa'y in the months of Hajj.
D) If he does not have intercourse between Umrah and Hajj.

Key Takeaway
For tamattu' in the Hanafi school, the majority of Umrah acts (tawaf circuits) must occur within the months of Hajj, applying the principle that the majority takes the ruling of the whole.

The Months of Hajj: Hanafi Definition and Proofs
Defines the months of Hajj with Companion and rational evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of the months of Hajj, explain the evidence from the Companions and rational proof, and evaluate the objection of Imam Malik.

Core Idea
The months of Hajj are Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah, and ten days of Dhul-Hijjah – based on Companions' reports and the logical end of time.

In this passage, Imam al-Quduri defines the months of Hajj. The Hanafi school relies on the authority of the three 'Abdullahs and the concept of fawat (missing Hajj) to restrict the phrase 'ashhurun ma'lumat' to two months and part of the third. Imam Malik's counterargument from the plural form is addressed through Quranic usage. This lesson unpacks the proofs and the dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
State the three months as per al-Quduri: Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah, and ten days of Dhul-Hijjah.
2
Examine the naqli dalil
Recall the reports from the four Companions named 'Abdullah (Ibn Mas'ud, Ibn 'Umar, Ibn 'Abbas, and Ibn al-Zubayr) that support this definition.
These are considered qawl sahabi, authoritative in Hanafi usul.
3
Understand the aqli dalil
Realize that Hajj is missed (fawat) after the 10th of Dhul-Hijjah; if the whole month were included, the time would still remain and fawat would not be actualized.
This logical argument shows the time ends at ten days.
4
Analyze Malik's objection and the Hanafi response
Malik argues from the Quranic plural 'ashhur' that three full months are meant. The Hanafi response uses the Quran's own use of 'qulub' for two hearts to show plural can mean more than one, not necessarily three.
This is a linguistic argument (dalalah) about the scope of the plural.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
State the practical difference: if someone performs Hajj after the 10th of Dhul-Hijjah, it is invalid according to the Hanafis but valid according to Malikis.
This shows the real-world impact of the dispute.

اشہر حج قَالَ وَأَشْهُرُ الْحَجِّ شَوَّالٌ وَ ذُو الْقعْدَةِ وَعَشَرٌ مِنْ ذِى الْحَجَّةِ كَذَا رُوى عَنِ الْعِبَادِلَةِ الثَّلَثَةِ وَعَبْدِ الله بن الزبير أَجْمَعِينَ وَلانَّ الْحَجَّ يَفُوتُ بمضى عَشْرِ ذِي الْحَجَّةِ وَمَعَ بَقَاءِ الْوَقْتِ لا يتحقَّقُ الْفَوَاتُ وَهَذَا يَدُلُّ عَلَى أَنَّ الْمُرَادَ مِنْ قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى الْحَجُ اَشْهُرٌ تَعْلُومَات به شهران وَبَعْضُ الثالث لا كله ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا کہ حج کے مہینے شوال، ذوالقعدہ اور ذوالحجہ کے دس دن ہیں ایسا ہی عبادلہ ثلاثہ اور عبد اللہ بن زبیر سے مروی ہے۔ اور اس لئے کہ ذوالحجہ کے دس روز گزرنے سے حج فوت ہو جاتا ہے حالانکہ بقائے وقت کے ساتھ فوت ہونا متحقق نہیں ہوتا اور یہ دلالت کرتا ہے کہ باری تعالیٰ کے قول الحج اشهر معلومات سے دو ماہ اور تیسرے کا کچھ مراد ہے تیسرا پورا مراد نہیں ہے۔ تشریح شیخ ابو الحسن قدوری نے فرمایا ہے کہ حج کے مہینے شوال، ذوالقعدہ اور ذوالحجہ کے دس روز ہیں ۔ امام مالک نے فرمایا کہ شوال، ذوالقعدہ، ذوالحجہ پورے تین ماہ حج کے مہینے ہیں۔ امام مالک کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے الْحَجُّ اشْهُرٌ مَعْلُومَات اور اشهر جمع ہے اور جمع کا اقل مصداق تین ہے۔ پس پورے تین ماہ حج کے مہینے ہوں گے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ عبداللہ بن مسعود، عبد اللہ بن عمرؓ اور عبد اللہ بن عباس او عبد اللہ بن زبیر سے یہی مروی ہے کہ حج کے مہینے شوال، ذوالقعدہ اور ذوالحجہ کے دس روز ہیں۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ذوالحجہ کے دس روز گذر جانے سے حج فوت من جاتا ہے یعنی اگر کسی نے وقوف عرفہ نہیں کیا اور یوم نحر آگیا تو اس کا حج فوت ہو گیا اگر ذوالحجہ کے آخر تک حج کا وقت ہوتا تو ذوالحجہ کے دس یوم گذرنے سے حج فوت نہ ہوتا کیونکہ وقت باقی رہتے ہوئے فوت ہونا محقق نہیں ہوتا۔ حضرت امام مالک کی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ آیت میں اشہر سے مراد دو ماہ اور تیسرے کا بعض ہے تیسرا ماہ پور امراد نہیں ہے کیونکہ جمع کا اطلاق ایک سے زیادہ پر ہوتا ہے۔ جیسے باری تعالیٰ کے قول فَقَدْ صَغَتْ قُلُوبُكُمَا میں دو قلب مراد ہیں حالانکہ قلوب بصیغہ جمع ذکر کیا گیا ہے۔
The months of Hajj. He said: The months of Hajj are Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah, and ten days of Dhul-Hijjah. Thus it is narrated from the three 'Abdullahs (Ibn Mas'ud, Ibn 'Umar, Ibn 'Abbas) and 'Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr, all of them. And because Hajj is missed (fawat) by the passing of the ten days of Dhul-Hijjah, and with the remaining time, the fawat is not actualized. This indicates that the meaning of the saying of Allah Most High 'The Hajj is in months well-known' is two months and part of the third, not all of it. Translation: Al-Quduri said: The months of Hajj are Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah, and ten days of Dhul-Hijjah. Thus it is narrated from the three 'Abdullahs and 'Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr. And because by the passing of ten days of Dhul-Hijjah, Hajj is missed, while with the remaining time, being missed is not verified. And this indicates that from the saying of Allah Most High 'The Hajj is in months well-known', two months and something of the third is meant, not the entire third. Explanation: Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri said: The months of Hajj are Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah, and ten days of Dhul-Hijjah. Imam Malik said: Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah, and the whole of Dhul-Hijjah are the months of Hajj. The proof of Imam Malik is that Allah Most High said 'The Hajj is in months well-known' and 'months' is plural, and the minimum of plural is three. So the full three months would be the months of Hajj. Our proof is that it is narrated from 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar, 'Abdullah ibn 'Abbas, and 'Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr that the months of Hajj are Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah, and ten days of Dhul-Hijjah. The second proof is that by the passing of ten days of Dhul-Hijjah, Hajj is missed, meaning if someone did not do the standing at 'Arafah and the Day of Sacrifice came, his Hajj is missed. If the time for Hajj extended to the end of Dhul-Hijjah, then by the passing of ten days Hajj would not be missed, because with time remaining, being missed is not actualized. The answer to Imam Malik's proof is that in the verse, 'months' refer to two months and part of the third, not the whole third month, because the application of the plural is to more than one. As in the saying of Allah Most High 'Then your hearts became inclined' (fqad saghat qulubukuma) where two hearts are meant, even though 'qulub' is in the plural form.
Source pages p. 403

Commentary
This passage defines the months of Hajj (ashhur al-hajj) according to the Hanafi school, with evidence from the noble Companions (the 'three Abdullahs' and Ibn al-Zubayr) and a rational proof based on the concept of fawat (missing Hajj). The matn of al-Quduri states that the months are Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhul-Hijjah. Imam Malik argued that the three full months are meant based on the Quranic plural 'ashhur'. The Hanafi response uses two proofs: first, the explicit narrations from the Companions; second, the logical argument that if the entire month of Dhul-Hijjah were included, Hajj would not be missed at the end of ten days, since the time would still be remaining. The Hanafis also reply to Malik's plural argument by giving an example from the Quran where a plural (qulub) refers to only two. Thus, the relied-upon Hanafi position is that the months of Hajj are as stated by al-Quduri.

Key Terms
اشہر حج (ashhur al-hajj): The specific months during which the rituals of Hajj must be performed: Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhul-Hijjah.
عبادلہ ثلاثہ (al-‘abādilah al-thalāthah): The three Companions named 'Abdullah: Ibn Mas'ud, Ibn 'Umar, and Ibn 'Abbas (and sometimes also Ibn al-Zubayr).

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The 8th day of Dhul-Hijjah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines the months of Hajj as Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhul-Hijjah, based on Companion reports and the logic that Hajj is missed after the tenth day.

Ihram for Hajj Before Its Months: Hanafi Validity and Shafi'i Dispute
Ruling on the validity of ihram for Hajj before its time, with a refutation of Imam al-Shafi'i's view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school validates ihram for Hajj before Shawwal and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Ihram for Hajj can precede its months because it is a condition, not a pillar.

This passage addresses a classic inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Imam al-Shafi'i. The key question: if a person performs ihram for Hajj before the months of Hajj (Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah, first 10 days of Dhul-Hijjah), is it valid and for which act does it count? The Hanafi ruling is that it is valid for Hajj. Understanding the reasoning requires grasping the fundamental difference between a condition (shart) and a pillar (rukn) in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The source opens with 'jaaza ihramuhu wa al-'aqadu hajjan' – the ihram is valid and contracted for Hajj. Write down the ruling in your own words.
The Urdu commentary elaborates that this is for Hajj, not 'Umrah.
2
Identify the opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that such ihram becomes for 'Umrah, not Hajj. Locate the phrase 'khilafan li al-Shafi'i' and understand why he reclassifies it.
His reasoning is that ihram is a rukn, which cannot precede its time.
3
Examine the Shafi'i proof
The Shafi'i proof is based on analogy to other pillars: just as you cannot perform tawaf or sa'y before their time, you cannot perform the pillar of ihram early. Also, to avoid futility, it is counted as 'Umrah.
The text gives an example of a missed fast becoming voluntary – this is the Shafi'i analogy.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response has three parts: (1) Ihram is a shart (condition), not a rukn – like purification for prayer. (2) Ihram's effects (prohibitions and obligations) are valid at any time. (3) Analogy to advancing ihram before the place (miqat) – agreed upon by all.
The condition can be advanced because it merely prepares for the act, while a rukn is part of the act.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: A Hanafi who performs ihram before Shawwal remains in ihram for Hajj and continues at the proper time. A Shafi'i must exit ihram as 'Umrah and later re-enter ihram for Hajj.
This has real implications for travel and planning Hajj.

اشہر حج سے پہلے حج کا احرام باندھنے کا حکم فَإِن قَدَّمَ الْإِحْرَامَ بِالْحَجِّ عَلَيْهَا جَازَ إِحْرَامُهُ وَالْعَقَد حَبًّا خِلَاقًا للشَّافِعِى فَإِنَّ عِندَهُ يَصِيرُ مُحْرمًا بِالْعُمْرَةِ لأَنَّهُ رُكَنَّ عِنْدَهُ وَهُوَ شَرَطَ عِندَنَا فَاشْبَهَ الطَّهَارَةَ فِي جَوَازِ التَّقْدِيمِ عَلَى الْوَقْتِ وَلِأَنَّ الْإِحْرَامَ تَحْرِيمُ أَشْيَاءِ وَإِيْجَابُ أَشْيَاءَ وَذَلِكَ يَصِحُ فِى كُلِّ زَمَانٍ وَصَارَ كَالتَّقْدِيم عَلَى الْمَكَانِ ترجمہ اگر حج کا احرام ان مہینوں پر مقدم کیا تو اس کا احترام جائز اور حج کے لئے منعقد ہوگا ۔ امام شافعی کا اختلاف ہے اس لئے کہ ان کے نزدیک عمرہ کے ساتھ محرم ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک احترام ایک رکن ہے اور ہمارے نزدیک وہ شرط ہے ۔ پس احرام، وقت پر مقدم کرنے کے جواز میں طہارت کے مشابہ ہو گیا ہے اور اس لئے کہ احرام چند چیزوں کو حرام کرنے اور چند چیزوں کو واجب کرنے کا نام ہے اور یہ ہر زمانہ میں صحیح ہے اور یہ مکان پر مقدم کرنے کے مانند ہو گیا۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے حج کا احرام شوال سے پہلے باندھا تو ہمارے نزدیک یہ احرام جائز ہے۔ اور یہ احرام حج ہی کے لئے منعقد ہوگا ۔ اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک یہ احرام عمرہ کے لئے معتبر ہوگا۔ حج کے لئے معتبر نہ ہوگا ۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ احترام ان کے نزدیک رکن ہے پس جس طرح دوسرے ارکان کو وقت پر مقدم کرنا جائز نہیں ہے اسی طرح احرام کو بھی مقدم کرنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔ لیکن سوال یہ ہے کہ یہ احرام جب حج کے لئے معتبر نہیں تو عمرہ کے لئے کیونکر معتبر ہو گا۔ جواب یہاں احرام تو پایا گیا مگر وقت حج سے پہلے باندھنے کی وجہ سے حج کا احرام ہونے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا۔ پس اس احرام کو لغو ہونے سے بچانے کے لئے عمرہ کے لئے معتبر مان لیا گیا ہے۔ جیسے اگر کوئی شخص دن میں قضاء روزے کی نیت کرے تو وہ نفل کا روزہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ قضاء روزہ کی نیت اول وقت صبح میں کرنا ضروری ہے۔ لہذا اس نیت کو لغو ہونے سے بچانے کے لئے نفل کے روزے کی نیت شمار کر لیا جائے گا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ احترام ہمارے نزدیک حج کے کلئے شرط ہے جیسے نماز کے لئے طہارت شرط ہے۔ پس جس طرح طہارت کو وقت نماز پر مقدم کرنا جائز ہے اسی طرح احرام کو وقت حج پر مقدم کرنا جائز ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے احرام سے چند چیزیں تو حرام ہو جاتی ہیں جیسے سلا ہوا کپڑا پہنا، شکار کرنا وغیرہ۔ اور چند چیزیں واجب ہوتی ہیں جیسے سعی اور رمی وغیرہ۔ اور ایسا کرنا ہر زمانہ میں صحیح ہے خواہ ایام حج ہوں یا نہ ہوں اس لئے احرام ہر زمانہ میں باندھنا جائز ہے۔ تیسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ احرام کو جس طرح مکان یعنی میقات پر مقدم کرنا جائز ہے اسی طرح زمانہ یعنی اشہر حج پر بھی مقدم کرنا جائز
The ruling on performing ihram for Hajj before its months. If he advances the ihram for Hajj before them, his ihram is valid and it is contracted for Hajj, contrary to al-Shafi'i. For according to him, he becomes a muhrim for 'Umrah because for him ihram is a pillar, while for us it is a condition. So it resembles purification (taharah) in the permissibility of advancing it before the time. And because ihram is the prohibition of certain things and the obligation of certain things, and that is valid in every time, and it becomes like advancing it upon the place. Translation: If he advances the ihram for Hajj before these months, his ihram is valid and it is contracted for Hajj. Imam al-Shafi'i differs; according to him, he will become a muhrim for 'Umrah. Because according to Imam al-Shafi'i, ihram is a pillar, while according to us it is a condition. Thus, ihram, in permissibility of advancing it before the time, resembles purification. And because ihram is the prohibition of some things and the obligation of some things, and that is valid in every time, and it becomes like advancing it upon the place. Explanation: The issue is that if someone performs ihram for Hajj before Shawwal, according to us this ihram is valid, and it will be contracted for Hajj. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, this ihram will be considered for 'Umrah, not for Hajj. The proof of Imam al-Shafi'i is that ihram is a pillar in his view, so just as it is not permissible to advance other pillars before their time, similarly ihram cannot be advanced. But there is a question: if this ihram is not valid for Hajj, how can it be valid for 'Umrah? The answer is that ihram is found, but because it was performed before the time of Hajj, it does not have the capacity to be ihram for Hajj. So to prevent this ihram from being wasted, it is considered valid for 'Umrah. Like if someone makes the intention for a make-up fast during the day, it becomes a voluntary fast, because the intention for a make-up fast must be made at dawn. Therefore, to prevent the intention from being wasted, it is considered as the intention for a voluntary fast. Our proof is that ihram is a condition for Hajj in our view, just as purification is a condition for prayer. So just as it is permissible to advance purification before the time of prayer, similarly it is permissible to advance ihram before the time of Hajj. The second proof is that with ihram, some things become prohibited (e.g., wearing stitched clothing, hunting) and some things become obligatory (e.g., sa'y and rami). And doing this is valid in any time, whether it is the days of Hajj or not. Therefore, performing ihram at any time is permissible. The third proof is that just as it is permissible to perform ihram before the place (miqat), similarly it is permissible to perform it before the time (months of Hajj).
Source pages p. 404

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the validity of ihram for Hajj if performed before the months of Hajj. The Hanafi ruling is that such ihram is valid and counts for Hajj. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that it becomes an ihram for 'Umrah instead because he considers ihram a pillar of Hajj and 'Umrah, and pillars cannot precede their time. The Hanafi response is based on the classification of ihram as a condition (shart) similar to purification (taharah) for prayer, which can be performed before the prayer time. Additionally, the text provides two more proofs: first, the nature of ihram as a prohibition and obligation that can be applied at any time; second, the analogy to advancing ihram before the place (miqat), which is agreed upon. The Shafi'i counterargument that it becomes 'Umrah is refuted by the Hanafi principle that a condition can be advanced, and the analogy to make-up fasts turning into voluntary fasts is dismissed because a condition for a specific act can be valid even if advanced, as long as the act itself is performed later. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that ihram before the months is valid for Hajj.

Key Terms
احرام (ihrām): The state of consecration for Hajj or 'Umrah, involving intention and recitation of talbiyah, which prohibits certain actions and obligates others.
شرط (shart): A condition that must be fulfilled for an act to be valid, but can precede the act itself, like purification before prayer.
رکن (rukn): A pillar or integral part of an act of worship that must be performed within its time; if omitted, the act is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the status of ihram for Hajj if it is performed before the months of Hajj?
A) It is invalid and must be repeated.
B) It is considered as ihram for 'Umrah instead.
C) It is valid and counts for Hajj.
D) It is permissible but strongly disliked (makruh tahrimi).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates ihram for Hajj before its months on the grounds that ihram is a condition, not a pillar, and conditions can be advanced.

The Kufi Who Settles Between Umrah and Hajj: Tamattu' Dispute
Ruling on whether a Kufi becomes Mutamatti' after Umrah, settling, and Hajj in same year

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tamattu' for a person who performs Umrah, settles outside Makkah, then performs Hajj in the same year, and explain the intra-madhhab disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Tamattu' is defined by a continuous journey, not just the locations of ihram.

This lesson examines a specific scenario from al-Jami' al-Saghir of Imam Muhammad: a Kufi performs Umrah during the months of Hajj, then settles in Makkah or Basra, and later performs Hajj in the same year. The question is whether he becomes a Mutamatti', requiring the dam (sacrifice). While there is agreement on the first case, the second case (settling in Basra outside the Miqat) reveals an important intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn. Understanding this dispute clarifies the school's definition of tamattu'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Read the passage carefully and identify the two cases: (1) the Kufi settles in Makkah after Umrah, (2) the Kufi settles in Basra (outside Miqat) after Umrah. Both perform Hajj the same year.
2
Locate the positions
Find where the author states the ruling of Imam Muhammad (that he is Mutamatti' in both cases) and then the disagreement: Abu Hanifa agrees, while the Sahibayn say he is not Mutamatti' in the Basra case.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's reasoning
The Sahibayn define a Mutamatti' as one whose Umrah ihram is from the Miqat but Hajj ihram is from within the Haram (Makki). In the Basra case, both ihrams are from the Miqat, so it is not tamattu'.
See the translation literal: 'Umrah is Miqati and Hajj is Makki.'
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's reasoning
Abu Hanifa focuses on the continuity of the journey: as long as the Kufi does not return to his original homeland (Kufa), the first journey is ongoing. Since both rites occur within this one journey, it is tamattu'.
Abu Hanifa's dalil is that the journey remains (qa'imah) until return to the watan.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view: the person is Mutamatti' and must offer the dam. This is indicated by the structure of the passage and the commentator's emphasis.
The commentator says: 'wa wajaba alayhi dam al-tamattu'.'

کوفی نے اشہر حج میں عمرہ کیا اور عمرہ سے فارغ ہو کر حلق یا قصر کرالیا پھر مکہ یا بصرہ کو وطن اقامت بنالیا پھر اسی سال حج کا ارادہ کیا تو متمتع ہوگا
قَالَ وَإِذَا قَدِمَ الْكُوفِيُّ بِعُمَرَة فِي أَشْهُرِ الْحَجِّ وَ فَرَغَ مِنْهَا وَ حَلَقَ أَوْ قَصَرَ ثُمَّ اتَّخَذَ مَكَةَ أَوِ الْبَصَرِةَ دَارًا وَحَجَّ مِنْ عَامِهِ ذَلِكَ فَهُوَ مُتَمَتِّعُ أَمَّا الْأَوَّلَ فَلَأنَّهُ تَرَفَقَ بِنُسُكَيْن فِى سَفَرٍ وَاحِدٍ فِى اَشْهُرِ الْحَج وَأمَّا الثَّانِي فَقِيلَ هُوَ بالاتفاق وقيل هُوَ قَولُ أبي حَنِيفَةَ وَعِندَهُمَا لَا يَكُونُ مُتَمَتِّعًا لأنَّ المُتَمَتِّعَ مَنْ تَكُونُ عُمْرَتُهُ مِيقَاتِيَّة وَحَجَّتُهُ مَكَّيَّةً وَنُسُكَاهُ هذَانِ مِيقَاتِيَانِ وَلَهُ أنَّ السَّفَرة الأولى قَائِمَةُ مَالَمْ يُعد إلى وَطَيْهِ وَقَدْ اجْتَمَعَ لَهُ نُسُكَانِ فِيهِ فَوَجَبَ دَهُ التَّمَتُه
ترجمہ امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں کہا اور جب کوئی اشہر حج میں عمرہ کے لئے آیا اور عمرہ سے فارغ ہو گیا اور حلق کیا یا قصر کیا۔ پھر مکہ کو یا بصرہ کو اقامت کا گھر بنا لیا اور اسی سال میں حج ادا کیا تو وہ متمتع ہے بہر حال اول تو اس لئے کہ اس نے اشہر حج میں ایک سفر میں دو عبادتیں ادا کر کے نفع اٹھایا ہے۔ اور دوسری صورت کے بارے میں کہا گیا کہ وہ بالا تفاق ہے اور کہا گیا کہ وہ ابوحنیفہ کا قول ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک وہ تمتع نہ ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ متمتع مشخص ہے جس کا عمرہ میقاتی اور اس کا حج مکی ہو اور اس کے دونوں نسک میقاتی ہیں۔ اور ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ پہلا سفر موجود ہے جب تک کہ وہ اپنے وطن واپس نہ جائے اور حال یہ کہ اس کے لئے اسی سفر میں دونوں نسک جمع ہو گئے پس اس پر تمتع کی قربانی واجب ہے۔

A Kufi performed Umrah in the months of Hajj, completed it and shaved or clipped his hair, then made Makkah or Basra a place of residence, then intended Hajj in the same year: he is Mutamatti'.
He (Imam Muhammad) said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: And when a Kufi comes for Umrah in the months of Hajj, completes it, shaves or clips, then takes Makkah or Basra as a home, and performs Hajj in that same year, then he is Mutamatti'. As for the first case, because he benefited from two rites in one journey in the months of Hajj. As for the second case, it is said it is by agreement, and it is said it is the statement of Abu Hanifa, while according to them (the two Sahibayn) he is not Mutamatti', because the Mutamatti' is one whose Umrah is from the Miqat and his Hajj is from Makkah, but here both rites are from the Miqat. And Abu Hanifa's proof is that the first journey remains as long as he does not return to his homeland, and indeed two rites have combined for him in it, so the sacrifice of Tamattu' becomes obligatory upon him.

Explanation: The issue is that if a resident of Kufa comes for Umrah in the months of Hajj, completes Umrah and becomes halal (by shaving or clipping), then intends residence in Makkah or Basra and becomes a resident, then performs Hajj in the same year, then in both cases he is Mutamatti'. In the first case (staying in Makkah), he is Mutamatti' because he neither left Makkah nor returned to his homeland, so he benefited from two rites in one journey in the months of Hajj, and such a person is called Mutamatti', so he is Mutamatti'. In the second case (when he settled in Basra), some say that in this case too it is agreed (that he is Mutamatti'), and some say that the ruling of being Mutamatti' is the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa, while according to the two Sahibayn this person is not Mutamatti'. The Sahibayn's proof is that the Mutamatti''s Umrah is from the Miqat but his Hajj is from Makkah, i.e., the Mutamatti' performs ihram for Umrah from the Miqat but for Hajj from Makkah (the Haram). Here it is not so; rather both rites are from the Miqat, because when the Kufi left home for Umrah, he performed ihram from the Miqat, and after completing the rites of Umrah he settled in Basra, which is outside the Miqat, so when he returns for Hajj, he must perform ihram from the Miqat again. Thus both rites are from the Miqat, so it is not Tamattu'. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that the journey the Kufi made from Kufa to Makkah still exists as long as he does not return to his homeland. So this person becomes like one who did not leave the Miqat and returned to perform Hajj. The conclusion is that in one journey, his two rites (Umrah and Hajj) combined, and the one who combines two rites in one journey is called Mutamatti', so this person is Mutamatti' and the sacrifice of Tamattu' is obligatory upon him.
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning a specific case of tamattu'. The source text is from Imam Muhammad's al-Jami' al-Saghir, and the commentator (author of Ashraf al-Hidaya) expands on it. The scenario: a person from Kufa performs Umrah during the months of Hajj, completes it (shaves/clips), then settles in Makkah or Basra as a resident, and later performs Hajj in the same year. The question is whether he becomes a Mutamatti', thus requiring the dam (sacrifice) of tamattu'.

The passage begins with Imam Muhammad's statement that he is Mutamatti'. This is explained in two cases. In the first case (if he settles in Makkah), there is agreement that he is Mutamatti' because he performed both rites in one journey without returning to his homeland. In the second case (if he settles in Basra, which is outside the Miqat and outside the Haram), there is a difference: Abu Hanifa holds that he is still Mutamatti', while the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that he is not.

The Sahibayn's reasoning is based on the definition of Mutamatti': one whose Umrah is from the Miqat and whose Hajj is from within the Haram (i.e., from Makkah). In this case, the person performed ihram for Umrah from the Miqat (when leaving Kufa), but after Umrah, he settled in Basra, which is outside the Miqat. When he later intends Hajj, he must perform ihram again from the Miqat (since Basra is beyond the Miqat), so both his Umrah and Hajj have ihram from the Miqat. This contradicts the definition of tamattu', so no dam is required.

Abu Hanifa's proof is that the original journey from Kufa is still considered ongoing as long as the person has not returned to his original homeland (Kufa). Even if he settled in Basra temporarily, the journey is not terminated. Therefore, both rites are performed within this single continuous journey, which is the essence of tamattu'. Hence he is Mutamatti' and must offer the dam.

The commentator mentions that some early authorities considered the second case to be agreed upon (muttifaq 'alayh), but this is not the preferred view; rather the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn is the established position. The operative ruling (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa, as it prioritizes the unity of the journey over the physical location of ihram.

Key Terms
متمتع (mutamatti'): A person who performs Umrah and then Hajj in the same journey during the months of Hajj, enjoying the relaxation between rites, requiring a sacrifice (dam).
میقاتی (miqati): Relating to the Miqat; ihram performed from the appointed boundary (Miqat).
مکی (makki): Relating to Makkah; ihram performed from within the Haram (Makkah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why does the Kufi who settled in Basra after Umrah still become Mutamatti' when he performs Hajj the same year?
A) Because he performed Umrah and Hajj both from the Miqat.
B) Because he did not return to his original homeland (Kufa), so the journey is considered continuous.
C) Because Basra is inside the Haram area.
D) Because he performed Hajj immediately after Umrah without any gap.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi holds that a person who performs Umrah and Hajj in one continuous journey is a Mutamatti', even if he settles temporarily outside the Miqat between them.

Defining Tamattu': The Journey Continuity Principle
Intra-Hanafi ruling on tamattu' with intermediate residence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of tamattu' according to Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and apply the journey continuity principle to determine whether a person is mutamatti'.

Core Idea
The journey continues until return to homeland; temporary residence does not break it for tamattu'.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute about the conditions of tamattu'. When a pilgrim performs Umrah in the Hajj months, then settles in Mecca or Basra before performing Hajj in the same year, does he become a mutamatti' requiring a sacrifice? Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ based on how they define the continuity of the original journey. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply principles of intention and journey in Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario
The person is a Kufi who performs Umrah in Hajj months, shaves/trims, then takes Mecca or Basra as residence, and performs Hajj in the same year. Determine the ruling on tamattu'.
2
State the matn's ruling
Imam Muhammad's al-Jami' al-Saghir states: 'He is mutamatti'.' Note that this is the transmitted text (riwayah).
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's objection
The Sahibayn argue that tamattu' requires Umrah from miqat and Hajj from within Haram (Makki). Here both are from miqat, so not tamattu'.
Their condition: Umrah miqati, Hajj Makki.
4
Understand Abu Hanifa's counter-argument
Abu Hanifa holds that the original journey from Kufa continues until the person returns to his original homeland (watan). Temporary residence in Basra does not end the journey; since both rites occur in one journey, tamattu' applies.
Key principle: al-safar al-awwal qā'im mā lam ya'ud ilā watanihi.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
If mutamatti', a sacrifice (dam) is wajib. If not, no sacrifice. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view, making the sacrifice obligatory.

قَالَ وَإِذَا قَدِمَ الْكُوفِيُّ بِعُمَرَة فِي أَشْهُرِ الْحَجِّ وَ فَرَغَ مِنْهَا وَ حَلَقَ أَوْ قَصَرَ ثُمَّ اتَّخَذَ مَكَةَ أَوِ الْبَصَرِةَ دَارًا وَحَجَّ مِنْ عَامِهِ ذَلِكَ فَهُوَ مُتَمَتِّعُ أَمَّا الْأَوَّلَ فَلَأنَّهُ تَرَفَقَ بِنُسُكَيْن فِى سَفَرٍ وَاحِدٍ فِى اَشْهُرِ الْحَج وَأمَّا الثَّانِي فَقِيلَ هُوَ بالاتفاق وقيل هُوَ قَولُ أبي حَنِيفَةَ وَعِندَهُمَا لَا يَكُونُ مُتَمَتِّعًا لأنَّ المُتَمَتِّعَ مَنْ تَكُونُ عُمْرَتُهُ مِيقَاتِيَّة وَحَجَّتُهُ مَكَّيَّةً وَنُسُكَاهُ هذَانِ مِيقَاتِيَانِ وَلَهُ أنَّ السَّفَرة الأولى قَائِمَةُ مَالَمْ يُعد إلى وَطَيْهِ وَقَدْ اجْتَمَعَ لَهُ نُسُكَانِ فِيهِ فَوَجَبَ دَهُ التَّمَتُه
ترجمہ امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں کہا اور جب کوئی اشہر حج میں عمرہ کے لئے آیا اور عمرہ سے فارغ ہو گیا اور حلق کیا یا قصر کیا۔ پھر مکہ کو یا بصرہ کو اقامت کا گھر بنا لیا اور اسی سال میں حج ادا کیا تو وہ متمتع ہے بہر حال اول تو اس لئے کہ اس نے اشہر حج میں ایک سفر میں دو عبادتیں ادا کر کے نفع اٹھایا ہے۔ اور دوسری صورت کے بارے میں کہا گیا کہ وہ بالا تفاق ہے اور کہا گیا کہ وہ ابوحنیفہ کا قول ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک وہ تمتع نہ ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ متمتع مشخص ہے جس کا عمرہ میقاتی اور اس کا حج مکی ہو اور اس کے دونوں نسک میقاتی ہیں۔ اور ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ پہلا سفر موجود ہے جب تک کہ وہ اپنے وطن واپس نہ جائے اور حال یہ کہ اس کے لئے اسی سفر میں دونوں نسک جمع ہو گئے پس اس پر تمتع کی قربانی واجب ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کوفہ کا کوئی باشندہ اشہر حج میں عمرہ کے لئے آیا اور عمرہ سے فارغ ہو کر حلال ہو گیا یعنی حلق کیا یا قصر کیا پھر مکہ المکرمہ یا بصرہ میں اقامت کی نیت کر کے مقیم ہو گیا اور پھر اسی سال حج کیا تو مشخص دونوں صورتوں میں متمتع ہوگا۔ پہلی صورت میں تو اس لئے متمتع ہو گا کہ یہ شخص نہ تو مکہ سے نکلا اور نہ اپنے وطن گیا پس اس نے اشہر حج میں ایک سفر میں عمرہ اور حج دو عبادتیں ادا کر کے فائدہ اٹھایا ہے اور چونکہ ایسے ہی شخص کو متمتع کہتے ہیں اس لئے یہ شخص متمتع ہوگا۔ اور دوسری صورت یعنی جب بصرہ میں مقیم ہوا تو بعض حضرات نے فرمایا کہ اس صورت میں بھی متمتع ہونا متفق علیہ ہے۔ اور بعض نے کہا کہ متمتع ہونے کا قول امام ابوحنیفہ کا ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک ي شخص متمتع نہ ہو گا۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ متمتع کا عمرہ تو میقاتی ہوتا ہے مگر حج کی ہوتا ہے یعنی متمتع عمرہ کا احرام تو میقات سے باندھتا ہے مگرحج کا احرام مکہ یعنی حرم سے باندھتا ہے اور یہاں ایسا نہیں ہے بلکہ عمرہ اور حج دونوں کا احرام میقات سے باندھا گیا ہے بایں طور کہ کوفی جب عمرہ کے لئے گھر سے روانہ ہوا تو عمرہ کا احرام میقات سے باندھا اور ارکان عمرہ سے فراغت پاکر بصرہ میں مقیم ہوا تو وہ حلال ہو کر میقات سے تجاوز کر گیا یعنی بصرہ میقات سے باہر ایک شہر کا نام ہے پس جب یہ شخص حج کے لئے واپس ہو گا تو اس کو حج کا احرام بھی میقات سے باندھنا پڑے گا۔ پس جب اس نے عمرہ اور حج دونوں کا احرام میقات سے باندھا ہے تو یہ تمتع نہ ہو گا ۔ امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جو سفر کوفی نے کوفہ سے مکہ المکرمہ کی طرف کیا تھا بصرہ چلے جانے کے باوجود وہ سفرا بھی موجود ہے تا وقتیکہ اپنے وطن واپس نہ چلا جائے۔ پس یہ شخص اس کے مانند ہو گیا جو ابھی میقات سے نہیں نکلا اور واپس آکر حج کر لیا۔ حاصل یہ کہ ایک سفر میں اس کی دو عبادتیں عمرہ اور ج جمع ہو گئے اور ایک سفر میں ان دو عبادتوں کو جمع کرنے والا متمتع کہلاتا ہے اس لئے یہ شخص متمتع ہوگا اور اس پر دم تمتع واجب ہوگا۔
Book of Hajj. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary of Hidaya volume third. A Kufi performed Umrah in the months of Hajj, finished it, shaved or trimmed, then took Mecca or Basra as a residence, then intended Hajj in that same year, so he is mutamatti'. He (Imam Muhammad) said: When the Kufi comes with Umrah in the months of Hajj, finishes it, shaves or trims, then takes Mecca or Basra as a home, and performs Hajj in that same year, then he is mutamatti'. As for the first, because he benefited from two rites in one journey in the months of Hajj. As for the second, it is said it is by agreement, and it is said it is the view of Abu Hanifa, and according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) he is not mutamatti' because the mutamatti' is one whose Umrah is from the miqat and whose Hajj is from Mecca, and these two rites are both from the miqat. And his (Abu Hanifa's) proof is that the first journey remains as long as he has not returned to his home, and two rites have come together for him in it, so tamattu' sacrifice is obligatory upon him. Translation: Imam Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: And when someone comes for Umrah in the months of Hajj and finishes Umrah and does shaving or trimming, then takes Mecca or Basra as a residence, and performs Hajj in that same year, then he is mutamatti'. In any case, first because he benefited by performing two acts of worship in one journey in the months of Hajj. And regarding the second case, it is said that it is by agreement, and it is said that it is the saying of Abu Hanifa, and according to the two companions he is not mutamatti'. Because the mutamatti' is specified as one whose Umrah is from miqat and his Hajj is from Mecca, and his both rites are from miqat. And Abu Hanifa's proof is that the first journey exists as long as he does not return to his homeland, and the situation is that for him both rites have gathered in that same journey, so the sacrifice of tamattu' is obligatory upon him. Explanation: The issue is that if a resident of Kufa came for Umrah in the months of Hajj, finished Umrah and became halal, i.e., shaved or trimmed, then intended residence in Mecca or Basra and became a resident, then performed Hajj in that same year, then in both cases he is mutamatti'. In the first case he is mutamatti' because this person neither left Mecca nor went to his homeland, so he benefited by performing Umrah and Hajj in one journey in the months of Hajj, and since such a person is called mutamatti', he is mutamatti'. And in the second case, i.e., when he became resident in Basra, some scholars said that in this case also being mutamatti' is agreed upon. And some said that the saying of being mutamatti' is of Imam Abu Hanifa, and according to the two companions this person will not be mutamatti'. The proof of the two companions is that the Umrah of the mutamatti' is from miqat but his Hajj is from Mecca, i.e., the mutamatti' ties the ihram for Umrah from the miqat but ties the ihram for Hajj from Mecca, i.e., from the Haram. And here it is not so; rather, the ihram for both Umrah and Hajj is tied from the miqat. In such a manner that when the Kufi left home for Umrah, he tied the ihram for Umrah from the miqat, and after completing the pillars of Umrah he became resident in Basra, so he became halal and crossed beyond the miqat, i.e., Basra is a city outside the miqat. So when this person returns for Hajj, he will have to tie the ihram for Hajj also from the miqat. So when he has tied the ihram for both Umrah and Hajj from the miqat, then this is not tamattu'. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that the journey that the Kufi made from Kufa to Mecca, despite going to Basra, that journey still exists until he returns to his homeland. So this person became like one who has not left the miqat yet and returned and performed Hajj. The gist is that in one journey his two acts of worship, Umrah and Hajj, came together, and the one who combines these two acts of worship in one journey is called mutamatti', so this person is mutamatti' and the sacrifice of tamattu' is obligatory upon him.
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the definition of tamattu' when a person performs Umrah in the months of Hajj, then takes a new residence outside their original homeland (like Mecca or Basra) before performing Hajj in the same year. The matn from Imam Muhammad's al-Jami' al-Saghir states that such a person is mutamatti'. The commentary then explains that there are two opinions on the second case (where the person takes Basra as home). One view is that it is agreed upon (by all Hanafi imams) that he is mutamatti'. Another view says it is only Abu Hanifa's position, while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) disagree. The Sahibayn argue that for tamattu', the Umrah must be from the miqat and the Hajj must be from Mecca (the Haram). In this scenario, the person ties ihram for both from the miqat (since after staying in Basra, they return to the miqat for Hajj), so it is not tamattu'. Abu Hanifa's counter-argument is that the original journey from Kufa is still ongoing until the person returns to their original homeland (watan). Since they have not returned home, both Umrah and Hajj are performed within the same continuous journey, hence tamattu' applies and the sacrifice (dam) is due. The author (Ashraf al-Hidaya) concludes that in both cases (taking Mecca or Basra as residence), the preferred position is that he is mutamatti' and must offer the sacrifice.

Key Terms
متمتع (mutamatti‘): A person who performs Umrah in the months of Hajj and then performs Hajj in the same year without returning to their homeland between them, combining both rites in one journey, thereby benefiting (tamattu‘) by being in a state of ihram for a shorter period. Such a person must offer a sacrifice (dam).
میقاتی (mīqātī): Refers to an act of worship (Umrah or Hajj) whose ihram is initiated from the designated miqat (boundary). In this context, the Sahibayn argue that both rites being miqati prevents tamattu‘.
صاحبین (Sāhibayn): The two most prominent students of Abu Hanifa: Imam Abu Yusuf (Ya'qub ibn Ibrahim al-Ansari) and Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani. Their views are often contrasted with Abu Hanifa's in the Hidayah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why does a Kufi who performs Umrah, then resides in Basra, and then performs Hajj in the same year become a mutamatti'?
A) Because he performed Umrah and Hajj in different journeys.
B) Because the original journey from Kufa is still ongoing until he returns to Kufa.
C) Because he performed both rites from the miqat.
D) Because he shaved or trimmed his hair after Umrah.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi Hanafi position is that temporary residence outside the original homeland does not break the continuity of the journey for tamattu'; the sacrifice is wajib.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Invalidated Umrah and Tamattu' Status
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tamattu' with invalidated Umrah and residence change

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on tamattu' after an invalidated Umrah and explain the reasoning based on continuing vs. new journey.

Core Idea
Tamattu' after an invalidated Umrah hinges on journey continuity: Abu Hanifa says original journey continues, Sahibayn say new journey begins.

This passage presents a second intra-Hanafi dispute regarding tamattu' when the initial Umrah is invalidated. The key variable is whether the journey is considered continuous or newly initiated after a mid-journey residence. The scenario: a person comes for Umrah, invalidates it (e.g., by intercourse before completing rites), finishes the invalid Umrah, trims, takes Basra as a home, then returns to Mecca in the Hajj months for a compensatory Umrah and Hajj. Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Sahibayn) differ on whether this constitutes tamattu'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Restate the facts: the person invalidates his Umrah, completes its rites, trims, establishes residence in Basra, then in the months of Hajj performs a new Umrah (qada) and Hajj in that same year.
This is after the previous lesson's scenario where he invalidated Umrah and returned home.
2
State each position
Abu Hanifa: he is NOT mutamatti'. Sahibayn: he IS mutamatti'. Note the conditional: if departure to Basra was before Hajj months, it's agreed he is mutamatti'.
Remember the thamarah: if mutamatti', dam is wajib.
3
Analyze the proofs
Sahibayn argue that travel from Basra to Mecca is a new independent journey (insha safar), combining Umrah and Hajj. Abu Hanifa argues the original journey continues because he hasn't returned home; the first Umrah was fasid, so he didn't obtain two correct rites in one journey.
Focus on the concept of 'journey' as the decisive factor.
4
Determine the practical consequence
The difference affects whether dam is wajib. Also note the conditional: if departure was before Hajj months, the dispute disappears by agreement.
This shows the importance of timing in tamattu' rulings.
