فَإِنْ قَدِمَ بِعُمْرَةِ فَأَفْسَدَهَا وَفَرَغَ مِنْهَا وَقَصَرَ ثُمَّ اتَّخَذَ الْبَصَرَةَ دَارًا ثُمَّ اعْتَمَرَ فِي أَشْهُرِ الْحَقِّ وَحَجَّ مِنْ عَامِهِ لَمْ يَكُنْ مُتَمَتِّعَا عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَا هُوَ مُتَمَتِّعْ لِأَنَّهُ إِنْشَاءُ سَفَرٍ وَقَدْ تَرْفَقَ بِنُسُكَيْن وَلَهُ انَّهُ بَاقٍ عَلَى سَفَرِهِ مَالَمْ يَرْجِعُ إلى وطنه
ترجمہ اور اگر عمرہ کے لئے آیا ہیں اس کو فاسد کر دیا اور اس سے فارغ ہو گیا اور قصر کیا پھر بصرہ کو دارا قامت بنالیا پھر اشہر حج میں عمرہ کیا اور اسی سال حج کیا تو ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک متمتع نہ ہو گا۔ اور صاحبین نے فرمایا ہے کہ یہ تمتع ہے کیونکہ یہ ایجاد سفر ہے اور حال یہ کہ اس نے دو عبادتیں ادا کر کے نفع اٹھایا ہے اور ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ شخص اپنے سفر پر باقی ہے وقتیکہ اپنے وطن نہ لوٹ جائے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کوئی شخص عمرہ کا احرام باندھ کر مکہ آیا پھر اس کو فاسد کر دیا مثلا افعال عمرہ سے پہلے بیوی کے ساتھ جماع کر لیا اور پھر فاسد ہونے کے باوجود افعال عمرہ ادا کرکے قصر کر کے حلال ہو گیا پھر بصرہ میں اقامت اختیار کر لی پھر اشہر حج میں عمرہ قضاء کیا اور اسی سال حج کیا تو حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک یہ شخص متمتع نہیں ہوگا اور صاحبین کے نزدیک متمتع ہوگا۔ یہ خیال رہے کہ امام صاحب اور صاحبین کے درمیان اختلاف اس وقت ہے جبکہ بصرہ کی طرف خروج اشہر حج میں ہو اور اگر اشہر حج سے پہلے نکالا اور پھر اشہر حج میں عمرہ کیا اور اسی سال حج کیا تو بالا تفاق متمتع ہو گا۔ مسئلہ مختلف فیہ میں صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس کا بصرہ سے مکتہ المکرمہ آنا مستقل ایک سفر ہے اور اس سفر میں اس نے دو عبادتیں ادا کی ہیں ایک عمرہ دوسرے حج ۔ اور ایک سفر میں عمرہ اور حج کرنا تمتع کہلاتا ہے بشرطیکہ یہ سفر ا شہر حج میں ہو اس لئے یہ شخص متمتع کہلائے گا۔ اور امام صاحب کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس کا پہلا سفر باقی ہے جب تک یہ اپنے وطن نہ لوٹ جائے اور اس سفر میں اس کا پہلا عمرہ فاسد ہو گیا تو دونسک اس کو صحیح طور پر حاصل نہ ہوئے حالانکہ متمتع وہی ہے جو سفر واحد میں دونسک بطور صحیح حاصل کرے۔
Then if he comes for Umrah and invalidates it, and finishes it, and trims, then takes Basra as a home, then performs Umrah in the months of Hajj and performs Hajj in that same year, he is not mutamatti' according to Abu Hanifa, and they (Sahibayn) said he is mutamatti', because it is the initiation of a journey, and he has benefited from two rites. And his (Abu Hanifa's) proof is that he remains on his journey as long as he does not return to his homeland. Translation: And if he came for Umrah, invalidated it, finished it, and trimmed, then made Basra a residence, then performed Umrah in the months of Hajj and performed Hajj in that same year, then according to Abu Hanifa he is not mutamatti'. And the two companions said that this is tamattu', because it is the initiation of a journey, and he has benefited by performing two acts of worship. And Abu Hanifa's proof is that this person remains on his journey until he returns to his homeland. Explanation: The issue is that if a person ties ihram for Umrah and comes to Mecca, then invalidates it, e.g., he had intercourse with his wife before the acts of Umrah, then despite it being invalid, he performs the acts of Umrah, trims, and becomes halal, then adopts residence in Basra, then performs qada of Umrah in the months of Hajj and performs Hajj in that same year, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa this person is not mutamatti', and according to the two companions he is mutamatti'. Note that the difference between Imam Sahib and the two companions is when the departure to Basra occurs in the months of Hajj. And if he left before the months of Hajj and then performed Umrah in the months of Hajj and performed Hajj in that same year, then he is mutamatti' by agreement. In this disputed issue, the proof of the two companions is that his coming from Basra to Mecca is an independent journey, and in this journey he performed two acts of worship: one Umrah and the other Hajj. And performing Umrah and Hajj in one journey is called tamattu', provided that this journey is in the months of Hajj. Therefore this person is called mutamatti'. And Imam Sahib's proof is that his first journey remains until he returns to his homeland, and in that journey his first Umrah became invalid, so the two rites did not come to him correctly, whereas the mutamatti' is the one who obtains both rites correctly in a single journey.
Source pages p. 406

Commentary
This passage presents a second intra-Hanafi dispute regarding tamattu' when the initial Umrah is invalidated (fasid). The scenario: a person comes for Umrah, invalidates it (e.g., by sexual intercourse before completing the rites), then completes the invalid Umrah's acts (by performing them anyway), trims (qasr), then takes Basra as a residence, then performs a compensatory Umrah (qada) in the months of Hajj, and then performs Hajj in the same year. Abu Hanifa rules that he is NOT mutamatti', while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) say he IS mutamatti'. The Sahibayn argue that the person's travel from Basra to Mecca is a new, independent journey. In that new journey, he combines Umrah and Hajj, fulfilling the condition of tamattu'. Abu Hanifa argues that the original journey from his homeland is still ongoing because he has not returned home. Since the first Umrah was invalidated, he did not obtain two valid rites in that journey; rather, he only obtained one valid Umrah (the qada) and Hajj in the same journey? Wait, careful: Abu Hanifa's reasoning: the first journey remains, and in it the first Umrah was fasid, so he did not get both rites correctly in one journey. The mutamatti' is defined as one who obtains both rites correctly in a single journey. Therefore, he is not mutamatti'. The commentary also notes a condition: this dispute applies only if the departure to Basra occurs within the months of Hajj. If he left before the Hajj months, then by agreement he becomes mutamatti'.

Key Terms
عمرہ فاسد (‘umrah fāsid): An Umrah that is invalidated due to a violation (like sexual intercourse) before the completion of its pillars. The invalidated Umrah must be completed and then a qada (compensatory) Umrah is required.
ایجاد سفر (ījād safar): Initiating a new journey. The Sahibayn consider the travel from Basra to Mecca as a new, independent journey.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of the difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn in this scenario?
A) The person must perform a new Umrah only.
B) The person owes a dam if mutamatti', but not if not.
C) The person's original Umrah becomes valid.
D) The person must repeat both Umrah and Hajj.

Key Takeaway
The status of tamattu' after an invalidated Umrah depends on whether the journey is continuous (Abu Hanifa) or newly initiated (Sahibayn), with the conditional note that departure before Hajj months removes the dispute.

Returning to Watan and Tamattu' Consensus
Consensus ruling on tamattu' with watan return

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tamattu' when a person returns to their homeland before performing Umrah and Hajj in the same year and explain why this situation creates a new journey.

Core Idea
Returning to one's watan ends the first journey; a new journey from watan establishes tamattu'.

In this lesson, we examine a scenario where all Hanafi imams agree: the person who returns to his original homeland after a previous Umrah journey and then performs Umrah and Hajj in the same year is considered a mutamatti'. This consensus clarifies that the key factor is the termination of the previous journey by returning to the watan, not the validity of the first Umrah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Read the passage and note the conditions: the person returned to his family (watan) after a prior Umrah journey, then performed Umrah in the months of Hajj and Hajj in the same year.
The prior Umrah may have been valid or invalidated; the ruling is the same.
2
State the ruling
The ruling is that the person is mutamatti' (performing tamattu'). This is the unanimous position of Imam Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
Tamattu' means combining Umrah and Hajj with a break in ihram, requiring a dam.
3
Understand the rationale
The reason given is that returning to the homeland ends the first journey entirely. The subsequent travel for Umrah and Hajj is a completely new, independent journey. In this new journey, two correct rites come together, establishing tamattu'.
The first journey ends because the traveler has reached his permanent residence (watan).
4
Apply the condition
Note that the condition 'return to watan' is decisive. If the person had not returned to his watan but merely stayed in another city (e.g., Basra), the first journey would not end, and the earlier disputes would apply.
This scenario is the exception that resolves the previous disagreements.

Source Text

Then if he returned to his family, then performed Umrah in the months of Hajj and performed Hajj in that same year, he is mutamatti' in the saying of all of them, because this is the initiation of a journey due to the ending of the first journey, and two correct rites have come together for him in it. Translation: So if he returned to his homeland, then performed Umrah in the days of Hajj and performed Hajj in that same year, then by agreement of the Hanafis he is mutamatti', because it is a new initiation of a journey due to the first journey ending. And the situation is that in this second journey, both rites are available to him in a correct manner. Explanation: If a person came for Umrah and invalidated it, and performed the pillars of Umrah and became halal, then he returned to his homeland, then performed Umrah in the days of Hajj and performed Hajj in that same year, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions, that person is mutamatti'. Because due to returning to the homeland, the first journey ended, now this is an independent second journey, and in this second journey two correct rites gathered, and in the days of Hajj, the gathering of two rites in one journey...
Source pages p. 406

Commentary
This passage presents a scenario where there is no dispute: if a person returns to his original homeland (watan) after an invalidated Umrah (or any Umrah), and then from his homeland performs Umrah in the months of Hajj and Hajj in the same year, then all Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree that he is mutamatti'. The reason is that the first journey ended completely when he returned home. The new journey from his homeland is a fresh, independent journey. In this new journey, he combines Umrah and Hajj correctly, so tamattu' is established. This consensus resolves the previous disputes by clarifying that the key factor is whether the person has returned to his original watan. If he has, the journey is broken, and a new journey begins. If he has not, the journey continues, and the earlier rulings apply.

Key Terms
وطن (watan): One's original homeland or the place where the person's family resides. Returning to the watan ends the previous journey and initiates a new one.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the person must perform Hajj Ifrad instead.
D) Because they only agree if the Umrah was valid.

Key Takeaway
Returning to one's original homeland (watan) terminates the previous journey; thereafter, performing Umrah and Hajj in the same year forms a new journey establishing tamattu' with consensus.

Tamattu' After Invalid Umrah and New Residence: Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tamattu' after invalid Umrah and new residence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi dispute on tamattu' and identify the thamarah al-khilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
The journey is one until you return home; two sound rites in one journey define tamattu'.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about the definition of tamattu' (combining Umrah and Hajj) when a person's first Umrah was invalidated and he later takes up residence elsewhere before returning for Hajj. The ruling determines whether the dam (sacrificial animal) is wajib. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply the criteria of 'single journey' and 'sound rites'.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
Identify the sequence: invalidated Umrah, completed it with taqsir, took Basra as residence, then performed Umrah in Hajj months and Hajj in the same year.
The key is that he did not return to his original homeland (e.g., Kufa) before the second Umrah.
2
Identify the ruling of each imam
Abu Hanifa: not mutamatti'. Sahibayn: mutamatti'. Note the thamarah (practical difference): dam required or not.
The dam is a wajib for mutamatti'.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's evidence
They argue that the travel from Basra to Makkah is a new journey (insha al-safar), and in this journey he performed two sound rites, thus tamattu'.
They focus on the fact that he now resides in Basra, so his departure from Basra is a fresh journey.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's evidence
He argues that the original journey continues until the person returns to his original homeland (watan). Since he did not return, it is the same journey, and the first Umrah was invalid, so he did not complete two sound rites in one journey.
Abu Hanifa emphasizes the continuity of travel and the condition that both rites must be valid.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if Abu Hanifa's view is taken, no dam; if Sahibayn's view, dam is wajib. Later Hanafi practice may follow the Sahibayn.
This dispute does not affect the validity of the Hajj, only the obligation of dam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ قَدِمَ بِعُمْرَةِ فَأَفْسَدَهَا وَفَرَغَ مِنْهَا وَقَصَرَ ثُمَّ اتَّخَذَ الْبَصَرَةَ دَارًا ثُمَّ اعْتَمَرَ فِي أَشْهُرِ الْحَقِّ وَحَجَّ مِنْ عَامِهِ لَمْ يَكُنْ مُتَمَتِّعَا عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَا هُوَ مُتَمَتِّعْ لِأَنَّهُ إِنْشَاءُ سَفَرٍ وَقَدْ تَرْفَقَ بِنُسُكَيْن وَلَهُ انَّهُ بَاقٍ عَلَى سَفَرِهِ مَالَمْ يَرْجِعُ إلى وطنه ترجمہ اور اگر عمرہ کے لئے آیا ہیں اس کو فاسد کر دیا اور اس سے فارغ ہو گیا اور قصر کیا پھر بصرہ کو دارا قامت بنالیا پھر اشہر حج میں عمرہ کیا اور اسی سال حج کیا تو ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک متمتع نہ ہو گا۔ اور صاحبین نے فرمایا ہے کہ یہ تمتع ہے کیونکہ یہ ایجاد سفر ہے اور حال یہ کہ اس نے دو عبادتیں ادا کر کے نفع اٹھایا ہے اور ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ شخص اپنے سفر پر باقی ہے وقتیکہ اپنے وطن نہ لوٹ جائے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کوئی شخص عمرہ کا احرام باندھ کر مکہ آیا پھر اس کو فاسد کر دیا مثلا افعال عمرہ سے پہلے بیوی کے ساتھ جماع کر لیا اور پھر فاسد ہونے کے باوجود افعال عمرہ ادا کرکے قصر کر کے حلال ہو گیا پھر بصرہ میں اقامت اختیار کر لی پھر اشہر حج میں عمرہ قضاء کیا اور اسی سال حج کیا تو حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک یہ شخص متمتع نہیں ہوگا اور صاحبین کے نزدیک متمتع ہوگا۔ یہ خیال رہے کہ امام صاحب اور صاحبین کے درمیان اختلاف اس وقت ہے جبکہ بصرہ کی طرف خروج اشہر حج میں ہو اور اگر اشہر حج سے پہلے نکالا اور پھر اشہر حج میں عمرہ کیا اور اسی سال حج کیا تو بالا تفاق متمتع ہو گا۔ مسئلہ مختلف فیہ میں صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس کا بصرہ سے مکتہ المکرمہ آنا مستقل ایک سفر ہے اور اس سفر میں اس نے دو عبادتیں ادا کی ہیں ایک عمرہ دوسرے حج ۔ اور ایک سفر میں عمرہ اور حج کرنا تمتع کہلاتا ہے بشرطیکہ یہ سفر ا شہر حج میں ہو اس لئے یہ شخص متمتع کہلائے گا۔ اور امام صاحب کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس کا پہلا سفر باقی ہے جب تک یہ اپنے وطن نہ لوٹ جائے اور اس سفر میں اس کا پہلا عمرہ فاسد ہو گیا تو دونسک اس کو صحیح طور پر حاصل نہ ہوئے حالانکہ متمتع وہی ہے جو سفر واحد میں دونسک بطور صحیح حاصل کرے۔
If he came for Umrah and invalidated it, completed it and did taqsir, then took Basra as his residence, then performed Umrah in the months of Hajj and performed Hajj in the same year, he is not mutamatti' according to Abu Hanifa. They (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: he is mutamatti', because it is a new journey and he benefited from two rites. And his (Abu Hanifa's) evidence is that he remains on his journey as long as he does not return to his homeland.
Source pages p. 406

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling on tamattu' (combining Umrah and Hajj in one journey during Hajj months) when a person initially came for Umrah, invalidated it (e.g., by intercourse before completing Umrah), then completed the invalid Umrah, did taqsir, and subsequently made Basra his place of residence. Later, during the months of Hajj, he performed a compensatory Umrah and then Hajj in the same year. Imam Abu Hanifa rules that he is not a mutamatti' because his original journey is considered ongoing until he returns to his original homeland. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that he is a mutamatti' because his travel from Basra to Makkah constitutes a new journey, and in that journey he performed two sound rites. The dispute is conditional on his departure to Basra occurring during the Hajj months; if it was before, there is consensus that he is mutamatti'. The practical difference hinges on whether the journey is considered one continuous journey or two separate journeys.

Key Terms
تمتع (tamattu'): Combining Umrah and Hajj in one journey during the months of Hajj with a break in between, requiring a sacrificial animal (dam).
متمتع (mutamatti'): A person who performs tamattu', i.e., combines Umrah and Hajj in one journey during the Hajj months.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The dispute on tamattu' after an invalid Umrah and new residence highlights the importance of journey continuity and the condition of two sound rites in the Hanafi definition of tamattu'.

Consensus on Tamattu' After Returning to Homeland
Consensus ruling on tamattu' after returning to homeland.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tamattu' when a person returns home after an invalidated Umrah and then performs Umrah and Hajj in the same year, and explain why it is considered a new journey.

Core Idea
Returning home after an invalidated Umrah ends the first journey; a subsequent combination of Umrah and Hajj creates tamattu' by consensus.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario of tamattu' in Hajj, where the pilgrim first invalidates an Umrah, returns home, and then performs a valid Umrah during Hajj months followed by Hajj in the same year. The Hanafi school unanimously considers this a new journey, thereby making the person a mutamatti'. Understanding this ruling clarifies the boundaries of tamattu' and the effect of spatial separation on the journey.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the specific scenario described? The person returns home after an invalidated Umrah, then performs a new Umrah in Hajj months and Hajj in the same year. The ruling: he is mutamatti' by consensus.
The ruling is unanimous among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad.
2
Understand the key condition
Returning to one's original homeland ends the first journey. This is the critical condition that resets the travel.
Without returning home, the journey continues and the invalidated Umrah may affect tamattu'.
3
Apply the definition of tamattu'
Tamattu' is combining Umrah and Hajj in one journey during the months of Hajj, with both rites valid. Here, the two acts are performed in a new, independent journey, both valid, so tamattu' applies.
The dam (sacrifice) becomes wajib as a consequence.
4
Confirm the consensus
Note that all three Hanafi imams agree on this ruling. There is no ikhtilaf.
This strengthens the authority of the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

If he returned to his family, then performed Umrah in the months of Hajj and performed Hajj in the same year, he is mutamatti' in the saying of all of them, because this is a new journey due to the termination of the first journey, and he has combined two sound rites in it.
Source pages p. 406

Commentary
This passage states a consensus ruling among the Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad) that a person who returns to his original homeland after an invalidated Umrah, and then performs a new Umrah during the Hajj months and then Hajj in the same year, is considered a mutamatti'. The reason is that returning home ends the first journey, so the subsequent travel to Makkah is a new, independent journey. In this new journey, he successfully combines two sound rites (Umrah and Hajj), which is the definition of tamattu'. Therefore, the dam al-tamattu' becomes obligatory.

Key Terms
تَمَتُّع (tamattu'): A type of Hajj where one performs Umrah during the months of Hajj and then Hajj in the same year, with a sacrificial obligation (dam).
دَم (dam): A sacrificial animal (sheep or equivalent) required as compensation for missing a wajib or for tamattu'.
فَسَاد (fasad): Invalidation of the act of worship, requiring its completion and later repetition (qada).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Staying in Makkah After Invalid Umrah: When Tamattu' Does Not Apply
Consensus ruling on non-tamattu' for those who become Makki by staying.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which a person who performed an invalid Umrah and stayed in Makkah is not considered a mutamatti', and identify the reason based on the Hanafi ruling.

Core Idea
A person who stays in Makkah after an invalid Umrah becomes a resident (Makki), so tamattu' is inapplicable.

A common scenario arises when a pilgrim invalidates his Umrah and then remains in Makkah instead of traveling away. Later, he performs a new Umrah during the Hajj months and then Hajj in the same year. Is he considered a mutamatti' who owes a dam? The Hanafi school, by consensus, rules that he is not mutamatti'. This lesson unpacks the reasoning: his first journey ended with the invalid Umrah, and his subsequent Umrah is from Makkah, making him a Makki resident. Since tamattu' is only for those who come from outside the miqat (afaqi), the ruling changes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is combining an Umrah (performed during Hajj months) and Hajj in the same year after an invalid Umrah and staying in Makkah. The ruling: he is not mutamatti' by consensus, and no dam is required.
2
Recognize the key factor: residency in Makkah
By staying in Makkah without leaving to a miqat, the person becomes a resident (Makki) for the purpose of this ruling. His Umrah is considered 'Makkan' (from inside the Haram).
The first journey ended with the invalid Umrah; he is no longer a traveler.
3
Apply the principle: no tamattu' for residents of Makkah
The established Hanafi principle (and general Islamic law) is that tamattu' is reserved for those who travel from outside the miqat (afaqi). Residents of Makkah do not qualify.
This principle is confirmed by consensus among the Hanafi imams.
4
Note the practical consequence
Since he is not mutamatti', no dam (sacrifice) is required. His Hajj is valid without additional obligations.
If he had left Makkah and returned from a miqat, the ruling would differ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ بَقِي مَكَّةَ وَلَمْ يَخْرُجُ إِلَى الْبَصْرَةِ حَتَّى اعْتَمَرَ فِي أَشْهُرِ الْحَقِّ وَحَجَّ مِنْ عَامِهِ لَا يَكُونُ مُتَمَتِّعَا بِالْإِنْفَاقِ لِاَنَّ عُمْرَتَهُ مَكَّيَّةُ وَالسَّفَرُ الْأَوَّلُ إنتهى بالعُمْرَةِ الْفَاسِدَةِ وَلاَ تَمَتُّع لأهل مكة ترجمہ اور اگر وہ مکہ میں ٹھہر گیا اور بصرہ کو نہیں گیا حتی کہ حج کے مہینوں میں عمرہ کیا اور اسی سال حج کیا تو بالا تفاق متمتع نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ اس کا عمرہ کی ہے اور پہلا سفر عمرہ فاسدہ سے ختم ہو گیا اور اہل مکہ کے واسطے تمتع نہیں ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ، اگر کوئی شخص عمرہ فاسدہ سے فارغ ہو کر مکہ ہی میں مقیم رہانہ بصرہ گیا اور نہ اپنے وطن گیا حتی کہ ایام حج میں عمرہ کیا اور اسی سال حج کیا تو بالا تفاق متمتع نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ پہلا سفر تو فاسد عمرہ کے ساتھ ختم ہو گیا پس اس کا یہ عمرہ کی ہوگا یعنی اس نے اس عمرہ کا احرام مکہ سے باندھا ہے اور یہ بات معلوم ہی ہے کہ اہل مکہ کے لئے تمتع نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے یہ شخص متمتع نہ ہوگا۔
And if he remained in Makkah and did not go to Basra until he performed Umrah in the months of Hajj and performed Hajj in the same year, he is not mutamatti' by consensus, because his Umrah is Makkan and the first journey ended with the invalid Umrah, and there is no tamattu' for the people of Makkah.
Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This passage states a unanimous Hanafi ruling that if a person who invalidated his Umrah remains resident in Makkah without going to Basra or returning to his homeland, and then performs a new Umrah during the Hajj months followed by Hajj in the same year, he is not considered a mutamatti'. The reason is that his first journey ended when he completed the invalid Umrah. Therefore, his subsequent Umrah is performed as a resident of Makkah (Makkan Umrah). Since tamattu' is not applicable to the residents of Makkah (ahl Makkah), he does not qualify as a mutamatti' and no dam is required.

Key Terms
مکی (Makki): A person who is a resident of Makkah, for whom tamattu' is not applicable when combining Umrah and Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a person who stays in Makkah after an invalid Umrah not considered a mutamatti' when he later performs Umrah and Hajj?
A) Because he did not return to his homeland.
B) Because he did not go to Basra.
C) Because his Umrah is Makkan and tamattu' is not for residents of Makkah.
D) Because he did not invalidate the Umrah.

Key Takeaway
A person who remains in Makkah after an invalid Umrah becomes a resident (Makki), and tamattu' is inapplicable, so no dam is required.

Ruling on Invalidating One of the Two Rites in Tamattu'
Ruling on necessity to complete invalidated rite and dropping of dam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a mutamatti' who invalidates one rite and explain why the dam al-tamattu' drops.

Core Idea
An invalidated rite must be completed, but the dam drops because no two sound rites were combined.

In tamattu', a person performs Umrah during Hajj months and then Hajj. If one of these rites becomes invalid, a specific set of rules applies. This passage clarifies that the invalidated rite must still be fulfilled due to the obligation of ihram, while the compensatory dam (dam al-tamattu') is waived. Understanding this ruling highlights the condition for the dam's obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and legal category
The person is a mutamatti' (performing tamattu'). The act is combining Umrah and Hajj in one journey. One of the two rites is invalidated.
Invalidation can occur through actions like marital relations before completing the rite.
2
State the ruling for the invalidated rite
The invalidated rite must still be completed. One cannot exit ihram except by performing the actions of that rite.
This applies whether Umrah or Hajj is invalidated.
3
State the ruling for the dam al-tamattu'
The dam al-tamattu' is dropped (no longer wajib). The condition for the dam is the performance of two sound rites in one journey; if one is invalid, the condition is not met.
The dam is a compensation for the convenience of combining, not for partial performance.
4
Explain the rationale
The dam is wajib only when both rites are sound. Since the invalidated rite is no longer sound, the basis for the dam disappears.
The obligation to complete the invalidated rite is independent of the dam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنِ إِعْتَمَرَ فِي أَشْهُرِ الْحَج وَحَجَّ مِنْ عَامِهِ فَايَهُمَا أَفْسَدَ مَضَى فِيهِ لأَنَّهُ لَا يُمكنُهُ الْحُرُوجُ عَنْ عُهَدَةِ الإحرام إلا بالأفعالِ وَسَقَطَ دَمُ الْمُبْعَةِ لأنه لم يترفَّقَ بِأدَاءِ تَسكين صَحِيحَيْنِ فِي سَفَرَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ ترجمہ اور جس شخص نے حج کے مہینوں میں عمرہ کیا اور اسی سال حج کیا تو دونوں میں سے جس کو فاسد کرنے اس کو کر گذرے کیونکہ اس کے لئے عہدہ احرام سے نکلنا ممکن نہیں مگر ادائے افعال کے ساتھ اور دم تمتع ساقط ہو گیا کیونکہ اس کو ایک سفر میں دونسک صحیح ادا کرنے کی توفیق نہیں ہوئی۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے ایام حج میں عمرہ کیا اور اسی سال حج کیا تو ان دونوں میں سے جس کو فاسد کرے اس کو پورا کرنا ضروری ہے کیونکہ بغیر افعال ادا کئے احرام سے نکلنا ممکن نہیں ہے۔ ہاں البتہ ہم تمتع ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ دم تمتع اس پر واجب ہوتا ہے جو ایک سفر میں صحیح دونسک ( عمرہ اور حج ) جمع کرے اور یہاں چونکہ ایک فاسد ہو گیا اس لئے صحیح درونسک جمع نہ کرنے کی وجہ سے متمتع نہ ہوگا۔
And whoever performs Umrah in the months of Hajj and performs Hajj in the same year, then whichever of the two he invalidates, he must proceed with it because he cannot exit the obligation of ihram except by performing the actions, and the dam of tamattu' drops because he did not benefit by performing two sound rites in one journey.
Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling for a person who sets out to perform tamattu' (Umrah in Hajj months, then Hajj) but ends up invalidating one of the two rites, either Umrah or Hajj. In such a case, the invalidated rite must still be completed because once in ihram, one cannot exit except by completing the actions. However, the sacrificial animal (dam) required for tamattu' is waived. The reason is that the dam is obligatory only for a person who successfully combines two sound rites in a single journey. If one of them becomes invalid, he no longer qualifies as a mutamatti', and thus the obligation of dam falls away.

Key Terms
دم تمتع (dam al-tamattu'): A sacrificial animal (sheep or goat) required from a mutamatti' as compensation for the convenience of combining Umrah and Hajj in one journey.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to the dam al-tamattu' if one of the two rites is invalidated?
A) It remains obligatory because the intention was tamattu'.
B) It is dropped because no two sound rites were combined.
C) The person must still sacrifice but for a different reason.
D) The dam becomes wajib on both rites.

Key Takeaway
When one rite in tamattu' is invalidated, the invalidated rite must be completed, but the dam al-tamattu' is waived because the condition of two sound rites is not fulfilled.

Eid Sacrifice Cannot Replace Dam al-Tamattu'
Ruling on a woman's Eid sacrifice not sufficing for dam al-tamattu'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a mutamatti's Eid sacrifice is not valid for dam al-tamattu' and explain the role of intention in distinguishing separate wajib acts.

Core Idea
Intention determines which obligation a sacrifice fulfills; Eid sacrifice is a separate act from dam al-tamattu'.

A common question during Hajj is whether an animal sacrificed on Eid can also satisfy the required dam for tamattu'. This lesson clarifies that the two are distinct acts of worship, each with its own ruling and intention. The passage from Al-Hidayah gives a clear answer: the Eid sacrifice does not count, and the same applies to men.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the passage and determine what act is being evaluated and what the ruling says. The act: a woman performing tamattu' sacrifices a sheep on Eid. The ruling: this does not suffice for the dam al-tamattu'.
2
Examine the reason given
The passage gives the reason: 'because she performed it for other than the obligatory (i.e., for Eid)'. Recognize that the Eid sacrifice is an act of worship with its own niyyah, distinct from the wajib dam.
The term 'wajib' here refers to the dam al-tamattu' which is obligatory for a mutamatti'.
3
Understand the role of intention (niyyah)
The ruling hinges on intent. Since the woman intended the Eid sacrifice, she cannot repurpose it for the dam. The same ruling applies to men, confirming that the principle is general.
In Hanafi fiqh, acts are judged by intentions (al-umur bi-maqasidiha).
4
Apply to a practical scenario
Consider a mutamatti' who sacrifices an animal on Eid without specifically intending the dam. According to the ruling, this does not fulfill the dam. The person must still offer a separate sacrifice with the correct intention.
This illustrates the importance of specifying niyyah when performing sacrificial duties during Hajj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا تَسَمَّتَعَتِ الْمَرْأَةٌ فَضَحَتَ بِشَاةٍ لَمْ يُجْزَهَا مِنْ دَمِ الْمُتَعَةِ لأَنَّهَا أُنتَ بِغَيْرِ الْوَاجِبِ وَكَذَا الْجَوَابُ فِي الرَّجُلِ ترجمہ اگر عورت نے تمتع کیا اور اس نے بقر عید کی قربانی کی تو یہ قربانی تمتع کی قربانی سے کفایت نہ کرے گی کیونکہ عورت نے غیر واجب کی نیت کی اور یہی جواب مرد میں ہے۔ (آگے کاٹا گیا)
And when a woman performs tamattu' and sacrifices a sheep (for Eid), it does not suffice for the dam of tamattu' because she performed it for other than the obligatory (i.e., for Eid), and the same answer applies to a man.
Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This passage addresses a practical situation: a woman who is performing tamattu' (combining Umrah and Hajj) decides to sacrifice a sheep on the day of Eid al-Adha. Does this sacrifice fulfill the requirement of the dam al-tamattu'? The ruling is clear: it does not. The reason is that the Eid sacrifice is an act of worship performed for a different purpose (it is a sunnah or wajib for those who have the means, but it is not specifically the dam due for tamattu'). The intention (niyyah) behind the sacrifice matters. Since she sacrificed for Eid, it cannot count towards the obligatory dam for tamattu'. The same ruling applies to men. Therefore, she must offer a separate sacrifice specifically for the dam al-tamattu' if she wishes to fulfill that obligation.

Key Terms
دم المتعة (dam al-mut'ah): A sacrificial animal required from a mutamatti' as compensation for the convenience of combining Umrah and Hajj in one journey.
ضحية (dahiyyah): A sacrificial animal offered on the days of Eid al-Adha, which is a separate act of worship from dam al-tamattu'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, because it is a sacrifice during Hajj.
B) No, because the Eid sacrifice is intended for a different act of worship.
C) Yes, but only if she is poor.
D) No, because women are exempt from dam.

Key Takeaway
A mutamatti' must offer a separate sacrifice for dam al-tamattu', distinct from the Eid sacrifice, with the correct intention.

When Umrah in Hajj Months Does Not Make One Mutamatti: The Makkan Exemption
Ruling with proof explaining the Makkan exemption from tamattu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a person is not considered mutamatti despite performing Umrah in the Hajj months, and explain the reasoning based on the Makkan exemption.

Core Idea
A Makkan Umrah cannot create tamattu—the journey must begin from outside the mīqāt to qualify for the dam.

This lesson examines a specific scenario from the Hidayah: a person who performed an invalid Umrah, then stayed in Makkah, and later performed a valid Umrah in Hajj months followed by Hajj. The text rules by consensus that this person is not a mutamatti. We will unpack the reasoning: the invalid Umrah ended the original journey, making the subsequent Umrah a Makkan one, and tamattu is negated for Makkans.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
Read the Arabic text: the person stayed in Makkah (did not return to Basra or his homeland), performed Umrah in the Hajj months, and then performed Hajj in the same year. The ruling: 'by consensus he is not a mutamatti'.
The ruling is clear: no dam required.
2
Analyze the reasoning (talīl) provided
The text gives two reasons: (1) his Umrah is Makkan (مكية), meaning he entered iḥrām from Makkah itself, and (2) there is no tamattu for the people of Makkah (لا تمتع لأهل مكة). The first journey ended with the invalid Umrah, so he became a resident of Makkah.
The invalid Umrah (fāsidah) still counts as a completed journey that ends his travel from beyond the mīqāt.
3
Understand the legal principle behind the exemption
Tamattu requires that the Umrah be performed from beyond the mīqāt, i.e., the person must come from outside the sacred territory for that Umrah. A Makkan (or someone who has become a Makkan resident) performing Umrah from Makkah cannot be a mutamatti because his Umrah is not a 'journey Umrah' but a 'residence Umrah'.
This principle is unique to the Hanafi school; other schools allow tamattu even for Makkans (as long as they are not in the state of iḥrām for Hajj at the time of Umrah).
4
Apply the principle to similar cases
Consider a person who comes from Madinah, performs a valid Umrah, then stays in Makkah for a year, and the next year performs Umrah in Shawwāl and then Hajj. Is he mutamatti? According to the Hanafi school, no, because his Umrah is Makkan (having stayed in Makkah for a full year, he is considered a Makkan resident). The journey from Madinah ended with the first Umrah.
The duration of stay matters; a short stay (e.g., a few days) may not make one a Makkan resident. The Hanafi rule: if the person stays in Makkah with the intention of residence (iṭān) or for a period that makes him a resident (e.g., one year), then he is treated like a Makkan.
5
Distinguish from the case of a true mutamatti
A true mutamatti is someone who comes from beyond the mīqāt, performs Umrah in the Hajj months, removes iḥrām (tahlīl), and later performs Hajj in the same year without leaving Makkah. The dam is wajib. In our case, the key difference is that the valid Umrah was not performed from beyond the mīqāt.
The invalid Umrah (even though it required completion and a dam) terminated the original journey, so the second Umrah is considered a new, local act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ بَقِيَ مَكَّةَ وَلَمْ يَخْرُجْ إِلَى الْبَصْرَةِ حَتَّى اعْتَمَرَ فِي أَشْهُرِ الْحَجِّ وَحَجَّ مِنْ عَامِهِ لَا يَكُونُ مُتَمَتِّعًا بِالِاتِّفَاقِ لِأَنَّ عُمْرَتَهُ مَكِّيَّةٌ وَالسَّفَرُ الْأَوَّلُ انْتَهَى بِالْعُمْرَةِ الْفَاسِدَةِ وَلَا تَمَتُّعَ لِأَهْلِ مَكَّةَ. ترجمہ: اور اگر وہ مکہ میں ٹھہر گیا اور بصرہ کو نہیں گیا حتی کہ حج کے مہینوں میں عمرہ کیا اور اسی سال حج کیا تو بالاتفاق متمتع نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ اس کا عمرہ مکی ہے اور پہلا سفر عمرہ فاسدہ سے ختم ہو گیا اور اہل مکہ کے واسطے تمتع نہیں ہے۔ تشریح: مسئلہ، اگر کوئی شخص عمرہ فاسدہ سے فارغ ہو کر مکہ ہی میں مقیم رہا نہ بصرہ گیا اور نہ اپنے وطن گیا حتی کہ ایام حج میں عمرہ کیا اور اسی سال حج کیا تو بالاتفاق متمتع نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ پہلا سفر تو فاسد عمرہ کے ساتھ ختم ہو گیا پس اس کا یہ عمرہ مکی ہوگا یعنی اس نے اس عمرہ کا احرام مکہ سے باندھا ہے اور یہ بات معلوم ہی ہے کہ اہل مکہ کے لئے تمتع نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے یہ شخص متمتع نہ ہوگا۔
And if he stayed in Makkah and did not go out to Basra until he performed Umrah in the months of Hajj and performed Hajj in that same year, by consensus he is not a mutamatti, because his Umrah is Makkan, and the first journey ended with the invalid Umrah, and there is no tamattu for the people of Makkah.
Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This is a ruling from the chapter on Hajj explaining the conditions for tamattu. The text clarifies that a person who initially set out for an Umrah that became invalid (fāsidah), then stayed in Makkah without returning home, and subsequently performed a valid Umrah in the Hajj months followed by Hajj in the same year, is not considered a mutamatti by consensus. The reason is twofold: first, his valid Umrah is considered a Makkan Umrah because he was already residing in Makkah after the invalid one; second, the people of Makkah do not have tamattu. Therefore, he is not obliged to offer the dam of tamattu. The commentary emphasizes that the key is the original journey ending with an invalid Umrah, making him a resident of Makkah.

Key Terms
تمتع (tamattu): A type of Hajj where one performs Umrah in the Hajj months and then Hajj in the same year, with a break of tahlīl in between, requiring a dam.
عمرة فاسدة (ʿumrah fāsidah): An Umrah that is rendered invalid (fasid) during its performance, requiring completion and a dam, but still counts as a journey.
أشهر الحج (ashhur al-ḥajj): The months of Hajj: Shawwāl, Dhul-Qaʿdah, and the first ten days of Dhul-Ḥijjah according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a person who stays in Makkah after an invalid Umrah and then performs Umrah in Hajj months and Hajj not considered a mutamatti?
A) Because his Umrah is invalid.
B) Because his Umrah is Makkan and there is no tamattu for Makkans.
C) Because he did not intend tamattu.
D) Because he did not perform Umrah first.

Key Takeaway
A person who becomes a Makkan resident before performing Umrah in the Hajj months cannot be a mutamatti, as tamattu requires a journey from beyond the mīqāt.

Ruling on Corrupting One of the Two Rituals in Tamattu
Explains that corrupting Umrah or Hajj requires completing it and drops the dam of tamattu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a mutamatti corrupts one of the two rituals and explain the reason for dropping the dam of tamattu.

Core Idea
Corrupting one ritual in tamattu requires completing it, but the dam is dropped because two valid rituals were not performed.

The mutamatti combines Umrah and Hajj in one journey, incurring the obligation of a dam (penalty). If either ritual becomes invalid (fasid), the pilgrim cannot simply exit ihram; he must continue and complete that ritual. However, the dam of tamattu is waived because the convenience of two valid rituals in one journey was not realized. This lesson explains the ruling and its underlying reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
Recognize that the subject is a mutamatti (one performing tamattu) who corrupts (afsada) either the Umrah or the Hajj. The ruling: he must continue and complete the corrupted ritual.
The ruling applies whether Umrah or Hajj is corrupted.
2
Understand the rationale for completion
The text states that exiting ihram is only possible through completing the actions (afʿāl) of the ritual. Therefore, the corrupted ritual must be completed.
This is based on the principle that ihram obligates specific acts until discharged.
3
Analyze the dropping of the dam
The dam of tamattu is normally owed because the pilgrim benefits from performing two rituals in one journey with a break. If one ritual becomes invalid, that benefit is lost, so no dam is due.
The dam is tied to the condition of both rituals being valid (sahih).
4
Consider the cross-madhhab perspective
Some other schools may require a dam in this situation, but the Hanafi position, supported by this reasoning, deems it dropped.
The Hanafi position is from the zahir al-riwayah.
5
Apply to a hypothetical case
If a mutamatti corrupts his Umrah, he must still perform all acts of Umrah (tawaf, sa'i) and then proceed to Hajj. No dam is required for tamattu.
The same applies if Hajj is corrupted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنِ اعْتَمَرَ فِي أَشْهُرِ الْحَجِّ وَحَجَّ مِنْ عَامِهِ فَأَيَّهُمَا أَفْسَدَ مَضَى فِيهِ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يُمْكِنُهُ الْخُرُوجُ عَنْ عُهْدَةِ الْإِحْرَامِ إِلَّا بِالْأَفْعَالِ وَسَقَطَ دَمُ الْمُتْعَةِ لِأَنَّهُ لَمْ يَتَرَفَّقْ بِأَدَاءِ نُسُكَيْنِ صَحِيحَيْنِ فِي سَفَرَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ. ترجمہ: اور جس شخص نے حج کے مہینوں میں عمرہ کیا اور اسی سال حج کیا تو دونوں میں سے جس کو فاسد کرے اس کو کر گذرے کیونکہ اس کے لئے عہدہ احرام سے نکلنا ممکن نہیں مگر ادائے افعال کے ساتھ اور دم تمتع ساقط ہو گیا کیونکہ اس کو ایک سفر میں دونسک صحیح ادا کرنے کی توفیق نہیں ہوئی۔ تشریح: مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے ایام حج میں عمرہ کیا اور اسی سال حج کیا تو ان دونوں میں سے جس کو فاسد کرے اس کو پورا کرنا ضروری ہے کیونکہ بغیر افعال ادا کئے احرام سے نکلنا ممکن نہیں ہے۔ ہاں البتہ دم تمتع ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ دم تمتع اس پر واجب ہوتا ہے جو ایک سفر میں صحیح دونسک (عمرہ اور حج) جمع کرے اور یہاں چونکہ ایک فاسد ہو گیا اس لئے صحیح دونسک جمع نہ کرنے کی وجہ سے متمتع نہ ہوگا۔
And whoever performs Umrah in the months of Hajj and performs Hajj in that same year, then whichever of the two he corrupts, he must continue in it because he cannot exit the obligation of ihram except by actions, and the blood of tamattu is dropped because he did not obtain the benefit of performing two valid rituals in one journey.
Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This ruling addresses a situation where a person intending tamattu corrupts (afsada) either the Umrah or the Hajj after starting both. The text states that the person must complete the corrupted ritual because one cannot exit ihram without completing the actions (acts of Hajj or Umrah). However, the dam of tamattu (a penalty for combining Umrah and Hajj with a break) is dropped. The reason given is that the dam is only obligatory when one performs two valid rituals in one journey, thereby gaining the convenience (taraffuq). If one becomes invalid, the benefit is lost, so the dam is waived. The commentary confirms that this is the same rule whether the Umrah or Hajj is corrupted.

Key Terms
دم المتعة (dam al-mutʿah): A penalty of slaughtering a sheep or equivalent for performing tamattu, obligatory on the mutamatti.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a mutamatti corrupts either his Umrah or Hajj?
A) Both become invalid and he must repeat both.
B) He must complete the corrupted one and the dam of tamattu is dropped.
C) He may exit ihram without any consequence.
D) He must offer a dam for the corrupted ritual.

Key Takeaway
Corrupting one ritual in tamattu requires completing it, and the dam of tamattu is dropped because the condition of two valid rituals in one journey is not fulfilled.

Ruling on a Woman's Eid Sacrifice Not Sufficing for Dam of Tamattu
Explains that a woman's Eid sacrifice does not fulfill the obligation of the tamattu dam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a non-obligatory act (Eid sacrifice for a traveler) cannot substitute for an obligatory one (dam of tamattu) and apply this principle to similar scenarios.

Core Idea
A non-obligatory act cannot fulfill an obligatory requirement.

When performing tamattu, a mutamatti must offer a dam as a wajib act. However, many pilgrims also sacrifice an animal for Eid al-Adha. A question arose: can a woman’s Eid sacrifice count for her dam of tamattu? Imam Abu Hanifa ruled it does not, because the Eid sacrifice is not wajib upon her as a traveler. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and its broader application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The act: a woman performs tamattu and offers an Eid sacrifice. The ruling: it does not suffice for the dam of tamattu. Note that the tamattu itself is valid.
2
Determine the Legal Status of Each Sacrifice
For the traveler (which includes most pilgrims), the Eid sacrifice (udhiyah) is not wajib. In contrast, the dam of tamattu is wajib. Establish this distinction clearly.
Hanafi view: udhiyah is wajib only for the resident who has the means.
3
Identify the Principle
A non-wajib act cannot substitute for a wajib act. Even if both are sacrifices, the difference in obligation level is decisive.
General Hanafi principle: one wajib cannot be fulfilled by another act unless specifically intended and allowed (e.g., combining intentions if both are nafl).
4
Note the Common Misapplication
Some might think that any sacrifice during Hajj days suffices for the dam. The lesson corrects this: the specific wajib requires its own sacrifice with proper intent.
5
Confirm the Universality of the Ruling
The same ruling applies to men, though the question was originally asked by a woman. The gender is incidental; the key is the traveler status.
The reason (illah) is the traveler’s exemption from udhiyah, which applies equally to men.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا تَمَتَّعَتِ الْمَرْأَةُ فَضَحَّتْ بِشَاةٍ لَمْ يُجْزِهَا مِنْ دَمِ الْمُتْعَةِ لِأَنَّهَا أَتَتْ بِغَيْرِ الْوَاجِبِ وَكَذَا الْجَوَابُ فِي الرَّجُلِ. ترجمہ: اگر عورت نے تمتع کیا اور اس نے بقر عید کی قربانی کی تو یہ قربانی تمتع کی قربانی سے کفایت نہ کرے گی کیونکہ عورت نے غیر واجب کو ادا کیا ہے اور یہی حکم مرد کا ہے۔ تشریح: مسئلہ، ایک عورت نے تمتع کیا اور بقر عید کی قربانی کی تو یہ قربانی دم تمتع کا قائم مقام نہ ہو سکے گی۔ کیونکہ اس کے مسافر ہونے کی وجہ سے اس پر بقر عید کی قربانی واجب نہیں ہے اور دم تمتع واجب ہے پس غیر واجب واجب کے قائم مقام کس طرح ہو سکتا ہے۔ یہی حکم مرد کا ہے۔ نوٹ: اس مسئلہ میں خاص طور پر عورت کا ذکر اس لئے کیا گیا ہے کہ امام ابو حنیفہ سے اس مسئلہ کو ایک عورت ہی نے دریافت کیا تھا ورنہ حکم مرد کا بھی یہی ہے۔
And when a woman performs tamattu and sacrifices a sheep, it does not suffice her for the blood of tamattu because she performed a non-obligatory act; and the same answer applies to a man.
Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This ruling clarifies that a woman performing tamattu who sacrifices a sheep for Eid al-Adha cannot count that sacrifice as the required dam of tamattu. The reason is that the Eid sacrifice is not wajib upon her as a traveler (she is in a state of hajj and considered a traveler, for whom udhiyah is not obligatory in the Hanafi madhhab). The dam of tamattu, however, is wajib. A non-obligatory act cannot substitute for an obligatory one. The commentary adds that the same ruling applies to men, though the question was originally posed by a woman to Imam Abu Hanifah. This highlights a specific point: the intent and obligation matter; one cannot fulfill a wajib with a nafl or sunnah act.

Key Terms
دم المتعة (dam al-mutʿah): The obligatory sacrifice for a mutamatti, usually a sheep or equivalent.
أضحية العيد (udhiyat al-ʿīd): The sacrificial animal offered on Eid al-Adha, which is sunnah mu’akkadah for the resident, not obligatory for the traveler.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does a woman's Eid sacrifice not count as the dam of tamattu?
A) Because she is a woman and women's sacrifices are not accepted.
B) Because the Eid sacrifice is not wajib on her as a traveler, while the dam is wajib.
C) Because she performed tamattu incorrectly.
D) Because the dam must be a sheep, not any animal.

Key Takeaway
An obligatory duty cannot be fulfilled by a non-obligatory act; each wajib must be performed with its specific intention.

Ruling on a Menstruating Woman at the Time of Ihram
Ruling on a menstruating woman's Hajj with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings for a menstruating woman in Hajj: enter ihram, perform all rites except tawaf until pure, and omit tawaf as-sadr after tawaf ziyarah without penalty.

Core Idea
A menstruating woman may perform all Hajj rites except tawaf; once tawaf ziyarah is done, she may leave without farewell tawaf.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a common concern: Can a woman in her menses perform Hajj? The answer is yes, with specific adjustments. The Prophet's guidance to Aisha provides the foundation, and the Hanafi school applies it with a rational distinction between acts in the mosque and acts in the open.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two temporal scenarios
Identify whether menstruation occurs at the time of ihram (before entering ihram) or after wuquf and tawaf ziyarah. The ruling differs in each case.
2
Apply the general rule for menstruation during Hajj
For the first scenario, she may perform ghusl and enter ihram, and perform all acts except tawaf until she becomes pure. This is based on the hadith of Aisha.
Tawaf is prohibited in the mosque because of impurity; other acts in open spaces are allowed.
3
Identify the two types of tawaf
Distinguish between tawaf ziyarah (rukn) and tawaf sadr (wajib). This distinction determines the consequence of omission.
Tawaf ziyarah is essential and must be made up; tawaf sadr can be omitted by concession.
4
Analyze the second scenario
If menstruation occurs after wuquf and tawaf ziyarah, the rukn is already fulfilled. The remaining wajib (tawaf sadr) is dropped due to the Prophet's concession, so she may leave without penalty.
5
Consolidate with the proofs
The hadith of Aisha provides the primary proof. The rationale (ta'lil) that tawaf is in the mosque and wuquf is in the open field supports the distinction.
The ghusl for ihram is valid because it is for cleanliness, not prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا حَاضَتِ الْمَرْأَةُ عِنْدَ الْإِحْرَامِ اغْتَسَلَتْ وَأَحْرَمَتْ وَصَنَعَتْ كَمَا يَصْنَعُهُ الْحَاجُ غَيْرَ أَنَّهَا لَا تَطُوفُ بِالْبَيْتِ حَتَّى تَطْهُرَ لِحَدِيثِ عَائِشَةَ حِينَ حَاضَتْ بِسَرَفٍ وَلِأَنَّ الطَّوَافَ فِي الْمَسْجِدِ وَالْوُقُوفَ فِي مَفَازَةٍ وَهَذَا الِاغْتِسَالُ لِلْإِحْرَامِ لَا لِلصَّلَاةِ فَيَكُونُ مُفِيدًا. فَإِنْ حَاضَتْ بَعْدَ الْوُقُوفِ وَطَوَافِ الزِّيَارَةِ انْصَرَفَتْ مِنْ مَكَّةَ وَلَا شَيْءَ عَلَيْهَا لِطَوَافِ الصَّدْرِ لِأَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ رَخَّصَ لِلنِّسَاءِ الْحَيِّضِ فِي تَرْكِ طَوَافِ الصَّدْرِ. ترجمہ: اور جب احرام کے وقت عورت حائضہ ہو گئی تو غسل کر کے احرام باندھے اور جیسے حاجی لوگ کریں گے وہ بھی کرے مگر یہ کہ بیت اللہ کا طواف نہ کرے یہاں تک کہ پاک ہو جائے۔ دلیل حدیث عائشہ ہے کہ جس وقت وہ مقام سرف پر حائضہ ہو گئیں۔ اور اس لئے کہ طواف مسجد میں واقع ہوتا ہے اور وقوف جنگل میں ہوتا ہے۔ اور یہ غسل کرنا احرام کے لئے ہے نہ کہ نماز کے لئے اس لئے مفید ہوگا۔ اور اگر وقوف اور طواف زیارت کے بعد حائضہ ہوئی تو وہ مکہ سے رخصت ہو جائے اور طواف صدر کی وجہ سے اس پر کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے حائضہ عورتوں کو طواف صدر چھوڑنے کی اجازت دی ہے۔ تشریح: مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جب عورت احرام کے وقت حائضہ ہوگئی تو وہ احرام کے لئے غسل کر کے احرام باندھ لے اور حج کے تمام افعال ادا کرے سوائے طواف بیت اللہ کے یہاں تک کہ پاک ہو جائے۔ دلیل حدیث عائشہ ہے یعنی حضرت عائشہ مقام سرف میں حائضہ ہو گئیں رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم تشریف لائے تو دیکھا صدیقہ عائشہ رو رہی ہیں آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے خود ہی فرمایا شاید حیض آگیا کہنے لگیں ہاں یہی بات ہے۔ آپ نے فرمایا یہ تو ایسی چیز ہے جو تمام بنات آدم کے لئے لازم ہے اس سے کسی عورت کو مفر نہیں ہے۔ پس حاجی جو کچھ ادا کرتا ہے تم بھی ادا کر مگر بیت اللہ کا طواف نہ کرنا جب تک کہ تم پاک نہ ہو جاؤ۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ طواف مسجد حرام میں کیا جاتا ہے اور حائضہ عورت کے لئے مسجد میں داخل ہونا حرام ہے اور وقوف میدان میں کیا جاتا ہے اور حائضہ کے لئے میدان میں جانے پر کوئی پابندی نہیں ہے اس لئے طواف کرنے کی ممانعت ہوگی لیکن طواف کے علاوہ دوسرے ارکان وقوف وغیرہ ادا کرنے کی ممانعت نہ ہوگی۔ اگر کوئی اعتراض کرے کہ حائضہ عورت کے لئے غسل کیونکر مفید ہوگا تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ غسل حصول نظافت کے واسطے احترام کی وجہ سے ہے نہ کہ نماز کے لئے اور جب حصول نظافت مقصود ہے تو بالیقین مفید ہو گا۔ اور اگر عورت وقوف عرفہ اور طواف زیارت کے بعد حائضہ ہوئی تو وہ مکہ سے رخصت ہو جائے اور طواف صدر ترک کرنے کی وجہ سے اس پر کوئی چیز لازم نہ ہوگی کیونکہ رسول خدا صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے حائضہ عورتوں کو طواف صدر چھوڑنے کی اجازت دی ہے۔
And when a woman menstruates at the time of ihram, she performs ghusl, enters ihram, and does what the pilgrim does, except that she does not perform tawaf of the House until she becomes pure, due to the hadith of Aisha when she menstruated at Sarif, and because tawaf is in the mosque while standing (wuquf) is in the open desert. This ghusl is for ihram, not for prayer, so it is beneficial. If she menstruates after the standing (wuquf) and tawaf az-ziyarah, she departs from Makkah and nothing is required of her for tawaf as-sadr, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) granted concession to menstruating women to omit tawaf as-sadr.
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This comprehensive ruling addresses a menstruating woman in Hajj. If she menstruates at the time of ihram (i.e., before entering ihram), she should perform ghusl (even though she is menstruating) and enter ihram. She then performs all acts of Hajj except tawaf of the Kaaba until she becomes pure. The proof is the hadith of Aisha (ra) who menstruated at Sarif, and the Prophet told her to do everything the pilgrims do except tawaf. Additionally, a rational proof is given: tawaf occurs inside the Masjid al-Haram, which is forbidden for a menstruating woman, whereas wuquf (standing at Arafat) occurs in an open field, which is permissible. The ghusl for ihram is valid because it is for cleanliness and reverence, not for prayer. If she becomes pure after wuquf and tawaf az-ziyarah (the obligatory tawaf of Hajj), she may leave Makkah and she does not owe anything for omitting tawaf as-sadr (the farewell tawaf), as the Prophet allowed menstruating women to omit it. The commentary elaborates on the hadith and answers a potential objection about the validity of ghusl while menstruating, explaining it is for purification of the body (nazafah) not ritual purity.

Key Terms
طواف الزيارة (tawaf az-ziyarah): The obligatory tawaf of Hajj, performed after returning from Mina on the 10th or 11th of Dhul-Hijjah; it is a rukn.
طواف الصدر (tawaf as-sadr): The farewell tawaf performed when leaving Makkah; it is wajib in the Hanafi school.
وقوف (wuquf): Standing at Arafah on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah; a rukn of Hajj that is valid even for a menstruating woman.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does a menstruating woman do if she becomes pure after performing wuquf and tawaf az-ziyarah?
A) She must stay in Makkah until she becomes pure and perform tawaf as-sadr.
B) She may depart from Makkah and owes nothing for omitting tawaf as-sadr.
C) She must offer a dam for omitting tawaf as-sadr.
D) She must repeat the Hajj.

Key Takeaway
A menstruating woman's Hajj is valid if she performs all rites except tawaf; she may omit farewell tawaf after performing the essential tawaf ziyarah.

Menstruating Woman in Hajj: Tawaf Exemptions
Ruling on menstruation during ihram with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings for a menstruating woman during Hajj and apply the exemption from tawaf al-sadr.

Core Idea
Menstruation exempts a woman from tawaf until purity, and after key rites, even farewell tawaf is waived.

This passage addresses a specific scenario: a woman menstruating during Hajj. It clarifies that she may perform all rites except tawaf, based on the Prophet's instruction to Aisha. Moreover, if menstruation occurs after Arafat and tawaf al-ziyarah, she may leave without tawaf al-sadr, as a concession. This lesson unpacks the proofs and the rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What does the passage rule for a menstruating woman at the time of ihram? She performs ghusl, enters ihram, and does all rites except tawaf until purification.
The ghusl is for cleanliness, not prayer.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of Aisha (menstruating at Saraf) and a rational proof: tawaf is in the mosque (forbidden for menstruating women), while wuquf is in the open (permissible).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? The Prophet told Aisha to do all pilgrim acts except tawaf, indicating exemption. The rational proof distinguishes place of acts.
4
Note the special case after wuquf
If menstruation occurs after wuquf and tawaf al-ziyarah, she may omit tawaf al-sadr with no penalty. This is based on a specific concession.
Tawaf al-sadr is normally wajib, but here waived.

تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جب عورت احرام کے وقت حائضہ ہوگئی تو وہ احرام کے لئے غسل کر کے احرام باندھ لے اور حج کے تمام افعال ادا کرے سوائے طواف بیت اللہ کے یہاں تک کہ پاک ہو جائے دلیل حدیث عائشہ ہے یعنی حضرت عائشہ مقام سرف میں حائضہ ہو گئیں رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم تشریف لائے تو دیکھا صدیقہ عائشہ رو رہی ہیں آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے خود ہی فرمایا شاید حیض آگیا کہنے لگیں ہاں یہی بات ہے۔ آپ نے فرمایایہ تو ایسی چیز ہے جو تمام بنات آدم کے لئے لازم ہے اس سے کسی عورت کو مفر نہیں ہے۔ پس حاجی جوار کان ادا کرتا ہے تم بھی ادا کر دیگر بیت اللہ کا طواف نہ کرنا جب تک کہ تم پاک نہ ہو جاؤ۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ طواف مسجد حرام میں کیا جاتا ہے اور حائضہ عورت کے لئے مسجد میں داخل ہونا حرام ہے اور وقوف میدان میں کیا جاتا ہے اور حائضہ کے لئے میدان میں جانے پر کوئی پابندی نہیں ہے اس لئے طواف کرنے کی ممانعت ہوگی لیکن طواف کے علاوہ دوسرے ارکان وقوف وغیرہ ادا کرنے کی ممانعت نہ ہوگی۔ اگر کوئی اعتراض کرے کہ حائضہ عورت کے لئے غسل کیونکر مفید ہوگا تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ نسل حصول نظافت کے واسطے احترام کی وجہ سے ہے نہ کہ نماز کے لئے اور جب حصول نظافت مقصود ہے تو بالیقین مفید ہو گا۔ اور اگر عورت وقوف عرفہ اور طواف زیارت کے بعد حائضہ ہوئی تو وہ مکہ سے رخصت ہو جائے اور طواف صدر ترک کرنے کی وجہ سے اس پر کوئی چیز لازم نہ ہوگی کیونکہ رسول خدا صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حائضہ عورتوں کو طواف صدر چھوڑ نے کی رخصت دی ہے۔
And when a woman menstruates at the time of ihram, she performs ghusl, enters ihram, and does as the pilgrim does, except that she does not perform tawaf of the House until she becomes pure, due to the hadith of Aisha when she menstruated at Saraf, and because tawaf is in the mosque while standing is in the open plain, and this ghusl is for ihram not for prayer, so it is beneficial. If she menstruates after standing (at Arafat) and tawaf al-ziyarah, she departs from Makkah and nothing is required of her for tawaf al-sadr, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) granted concession to menstruating women to omit tawaf al-sadr.

Explanation of the issue: When a woman menstruates at the time of ihram, she should perform ghusl for ihram, tie the ihram, and perform all the rites of Hajj except tawaf of the Kaaba until she becomes pure. The proof is the hadith of Aisha: when she menstruated at Saraf, the Prophet (peace be upon him) came and saw her crying and said, 'Perhaps you have menstruated?' She said yes. He said, 'This is a matter decreed for all daughters of Adam; there is no escape from it. So do as the pilgrim does, except do not perform tawaf of the House until you become pure.' The second proof is that tawaf is performed in the Sacred Mosque, and entering the mosque is forbidden for a menstruating woman, while standing (wuquf) is performed in the open plain, and there is no restriction for a menstruating woman to go to the plain. Therefore, prohibition applies to tawaf but not to other rites like standing. If someone objects that a menstruating woman cannot benefit from ghusl, the answer is that this ghusl is for cleanliness and out of respect, not for prayer, and since cleanliness is intended, it is undoubtedly beneficial. If a woman menstruates after standing at Arafat and tawaf al-ziyarah, she may depart from Makkah, and nothing is obligatory upon her for omitting tawaf al-sadr, because the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) granted concession to menstruating women to omit tawaf al-sadr.
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the status of a menstruating woman during Hajj. The author presents the core ruling: if a woman menstruates at the time of ihram, she should perform ghusl (bath) for ihram (not for prayer, as clarified later), enter ihram, and perform all rites of Hajj except tawaf of the Kaaba until she becomes pure from menstruation. The proof is the well-known hadith of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) who menstruated at Saraf, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) instructed her to do all that pilgrims do except tawaf. A second rational proof is given: tawaf is performed inside the Sacred Mosque, which a menstruating woman may not enter, while wuquf (standing at Arafat) occurs in the open plain, which is permissible for her. Hence the prohibition is limited to tawaf. The author then addresses a potential objection: how can a menstruating woman's ghusl be beneficial? The answer is that this ghusl is for the purpose of cleanliness and respect in the state of ihram, not for ritual purity for prayer, so it is valid and beneficial. Finally, the passage addresses the scenario after wuquf and tawaf al-ziyarah (the obligatory tawaf of Hajj): if she menstruates after these, she may leave Makkah without performing tawaf al-sadr (the farewell tawaf), and no compensation is required. This is based on the Prophet's concession to menstruating women to omit tawaf al-sadr.

Key Terms
طواف الصدر (tawaf al-sadr): The farewell tawaf performed upon leaving Makkah, wajib on non-residents.
حائض (ha'id): A woman in the state of menstruation.

Tawaf al-Sadr for the Makkan Resident: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tawaf al-sadr for Makkan residents

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the exception to the ruling that a Makkan is not required to perform tawaf al-sadr and evaluate the positions of Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
A Makkan needs no farewell tawaf unless the obligation arose before residence — timing is decisive.

This passage addresses a nuanced question in Hajj jurisprudence: does a person who makes Makkah his permanent home ever need to perform tawaf al-sadr (farewell tawaf)? The general rule is clear — no tawaf for residents. However, Imam Abu Hanifa introduces an exception based on timing, sparking an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf with Imam Muhammad. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply rules when obligations have already been triggered.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling and its rationale
Read the first part of the passage: a person who adopts Makkah as a home has no tawaf al-sadr. Why? Because tawaf al-sadr is for those departing (to their homeland), not for those staying.
The ruling is described as conditional on the absence of the cause of obligation — departure.
2
Recognize the exception and its source
The phrase 'unless he adopts it as a home after the first incursion' signals an exception reported from Abu Hanifa (and some narrate it from Muhammad). Mark the timing: after 12th Dhul-Hijjah, when the time for departure (nafar awwal) has entered.
The exception hinges on when the residence intention occurs.
3
Analyze the proof (talil) for Abu Hanifa's position
The reasoning: tawaf al-sadr became obligatory with the entry of its time (the 13th). Once wajib, it cannot be dropped by a subsequent intention of residence. The author provides a qiyas (analogy) with fasting in Ramadan: if a resident starts fasting and then travels, the fast remains obligatory.
This is a classic case of obligation crystallizing before a change of status.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if a pilgrim decides to settle in Makkah on the 13th, Abu Hanifa says tawaf al-sadr is wajib; Muhammad (in some narrations) says it is not. The mufta bihi (operative ruling) follows Abu Hanifa.
The dispute is within the school, not with other madhahib.
5
Reflect on the epistemological weight
The exceptive ruling is transmitted as a narration (riwayah) from Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, not from the standard Zahir al-Riwayah. This places it in the category of nawadir (rare transmissions), yet it is relied upon due to strong reasoning.
Understanding authority weight prevents overgeneralization.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنِ اتَّخَذَ مَكَّةَ دَارًا فَلَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ طَوَافُ الصَّدْرِ لِأَنَّهُ عَلَى مَن يَصْدُرُ إِلَّا إِذَا اتَّخَذَهَا دَارًا بَعْدَ مَاحَلَّ النَّفَرُ الْأَوَّلُ فِيْمَا يُرُوى عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَيَرْوِيهِ الْبَعْضُ عَنْ مُحَمَّدٍ لِأَنَّهُ وَجَبَ عَلَيْهِ بِدُخُولِ وَقْتِهِ فَلَا يَسْقُطُ بِنِيَّةِ الْإِقَامَةِ بَعْدَ ذلِكَ وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ بِالصَّوَابِ

تشریح اگر کسی آفاقی نے مکہ المکرمہ کو وطن بنا لیا تو اس پر طواف صدر واجب نہ ہوگا کیونکہ طواف صدر یعینی و داعی طواف اس پر واجب ہوتا ہے جو مکہ سے کوچ کر کے اپنے وطن لوٹے گا۔ حالانکہ یہ شخص مکہ کو دارا قامت بنانے کی وجہ سے ایسا کرنے کا اراد ہ نہیں رکھتا اس لئے اس پر طواف صدر واجب نہ ہوگا ۔ ہاں اگر بارہویں ذی الحجہ کے بعد تیر ہوئیں ذی الحجہ کو مکہ میں اقامت کی نیت کی تو ابوحنیفہ کی روایت کے مطابق اس پر طواف صدر واجب ہوگا ۔ اور بعض حضرات اس کو امام محمد سے روایت کرتے ہیں ۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ تیرہویں ذی الحجہ میں روانگی کا وقت آجانے کی وجہ سے اس پر طواف صد ر واجب ہو گیا۔ اب اس کے بعد اقامت کی نیت کرنے سے واجب شدہ طواف ساقط نہ ہو گا ۔ جیسے کسی مقیم نے رمضان کی صبح کی پھر سفر شروع کر دیا تو اب اس کے لئے افطار کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
And whoever adopts Makkah as a home, there is no tawaf al-sadr upon him, because it is for one who departs (to his home), unless he adopts it as a home after the first incursion (nafar awwal) has become permissible, according to what is narrated from Abu Hanifa, and some narrate it from Muhammad, because it became obligatory upon him with the entry of its time, so it is not dropped by intention of residence after that. And Allah knows best.

Explanation: If a non-Makkan (afaqi) makes Makkah al-Mukarramah his home, tawaf al-sadr is not obligatory upon him, because tawaf al-sadr, the farewell tawaf, is obligatory upon one who departs from Makkah returning to his homeland. Since this person has made Makkah his residence, he does not intend to do that, so tawaf al-sadr is not obligatory. However, if after the 12th of Dhul-Hijjah, on the 13th, he intends residence in Makkah, then according to the narration from Abu Hanifa, tawaf al-sadr becomes obligatory upon him. And some narrate this from Muhammad. The proof is that with the arrival of the time of departure on the 13th of Dhul-Hijjah, tawaf al-sadr became obligatory upon him. After that, intending residence does not drop the already obligatory tawaf. For example, if a resident (muqim) begins fasting in Ramadan then starts a journey, it is not permissible for him to break the fast. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling and an intra-Hanafi dispute about tawaf al-sadr for someone who makes Makkah his home. The basic ruling: a person who adopts Makkah as his permanent residence (i.e., becomes a Makkan) is not required to perform tawaf al-sadr (farewell tawaf), because this tawaf is for those departing from Makkah to their home. Since he is not departing but staying, it is not obligatory. However, there is an exception reported from Imam Abu Hanifa (and some narrate it from Imam Muhammad): if he makes Makkah his home after the time for the first incursion (nafar awwal, i.e., the 12th of Dhul-Hijjah) has arrived, then tawaf al-sadr becomes obligatory on him. The reasoning is that the obligation of tawaf al-sadr was already established upon him with the entry of its time (the 13th of Dhul-Hijjah, the time for departure). Since it was already wajib, a subsequent intention of residence does not nullify it. The author gives a parallel: a resident who begins fasting in Ramadan and then travels is still obliged to complete the fast; he cannot break it. Similarly, tawaf al-sadr once wajib remains wajib. The dispute is within the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa holds that it becomes wajib if he makes it home after the nafar awwal, while some narrate from Muhammad that it does not. The relied-upon position (according to the text) is that of Abu Hanifa, as it is supported by reasoning.

Key Terms
طواف الصدر (tawaf al-sadr): The farewell tawaf performed when leaving Makkah, wajib on those departing.
النفر الأول (al-nafar al-awwal): The first day of departure from Mina, i.e., the 12th of Dhul-Hijjah after stoning the jamarat.
آفاقي (afaqi): A person who comes from outside the miqat, a non-Makkan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Always
B) Only if he makes it home before the Hajj season
C) If he makes it home after the first incursion (nafar awwal)
D) Never

Key Takeaway
A Makkan resident is exempt from tawaf al-sadr, except when the obligation was already triggered by the entry of its time (after nafar awwal) per the mufta bihi view of Abu Hanifa.

Kaffarah for a Muhrim Applying Perfume
Ruling on kaffarah for a muhrim using perfume

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the kaffarah for a muhrim applying perfume and distinguish between a complete limb and less, citing the Hanafi ruling.

Core Idea
A muhrim must sacrifice a dam only if perfume covers a complete limb or more; less requires sadaqah.

In the chapter on Hajj penalties, the ruling on perfume is foundational. This passage from Al-Hidayah states the penalty with precise conditions. You will learn the threshold for the full dam and understand the reasoning (talil) behind the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and general rule
A muhrim applying perfume incurs kaffarah. The general rule is that any perfume use requires a penalty.
The passage states 'When a muhrim applies perfume, kaffarah is due.'
2
Determine the threshold for full penalty
The full dam is due only when the perfume covers a complete limb or more. Examples: head, shin, thigh.
Less than a complete limb triggers a lesser sadaqah (inferred).
3
Understand the talil
The prohibition is perfected when utilization (intifa') is complete, which occurs when a whole limb is covered. Hence the full penalty corresponds to full coverage.
The reasoning: 'because the prohibition is perfected with the perfection of utilization'.
4
Apply the distinction
For less than a complete limb, the ruling is that a lesser sadaqah (e.g., half a sa') is due. This is derived from the passage's logic.
The passage implies that kaffarah scales with the extent of coverage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْجِنَايَاتِ

وَإِذَا تَطِيبَ الْمُحْرِمُ فَعَلَيْهِ الكَفَّارَةُ فَإِن طِيبَ عُضَرًا كَامِلَا فَما زَادَ فَعَلَيْهِ دَم و ذلك مِثْل الرَّأْسِ وَالسَّاقِ وَالْفَخِذِ وَمَا أَشَبَهَ ذَلِكَ لِأَنَّ الْحِمَايَةَ تَتَكَامَلُ بِتَكَاملِ الْاَرْتِفَاقِ وذلك فِي الْعُضَو الكاملِ فَيَتَرَتْبُ عَلَيْهِ كَمَالَ الْمَرْجَبِ
Chapter of Offenses (Jinayat).

And when a muhrim applies perfume, kaffarah is due upon him. If he perfumes a complete limb or more, then a dam (sacrifice) is due. Examples: the head, shin, thigh, and the like. Because the prohibition is perfected with the perfection of utilization, and that is in a complete limb, so the full penalty follows.
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on jinayat (offenses) in Hajj. It is a ruling statement on the kaffarah for a muhrim who applies perfume. The general rule: any application of perfume requires kaffarah (penalty). The specific ruling: if the perfume is applied to a complete limb (like the whole head, whole shin, whole thigh) or more than a limb, then the full penalty of a dam (one sheep) is required. The reasoning (talil) given: the prohibition of perfume for a muhrim is perfected when the utilization (intifa') is complete, and that occurs when a full limb is covered. Therefore, a full penalty (dam) is due for a full limb. For less than a limb, the kaffarah would be different (sadaqah). The examples clarify what constitutes a complete limb: the head, leg, thigh, and similar. This is a concise, foundational ruling from the matn.

Key Terms
محرم (muhrim): A person in the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (sheep or goat) as penalty.
عضو كامل (udw kamil): A complete limb such as head, shin, thigh, arm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How much perfume use triggers a dam as kaffarah for a muhrim?
A) Any amount
B) A complete limb or more
C) Only the head
D) More than one limb

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the full penalty for perfume during ihram (a dam) is only due when the perfume covers a complete limb or more.

Tawaf al-Sadr for One Who Makes Makkah a Home: Intra-Hanafi Exception
Intra-Hanafi dispute on exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general Hanafi ruling on Tawaf al-Sadr for a resident of Makkah and explain the exception regarding timing after nafr awwal.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Sadr is not required for residents of Makkah, but if residency begins after the departure time, it becomes wajib according to Abu Hanifa.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a specific scenario within Hajj: a pilgrim who decides to settle in Makkah. The general rule exempts such a person from the farewell tawaf (Tawaf al-Sadr). However, an intra-Hanafi dispute arises when the decision to settle occurs after the first departure (nafr awwal). We will analyze the reasoning behind the two narrations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the general ruling
The act under discussion is Tawaf al-Sadr, and the general ruling is that it is not wajib for one who makes Makkah their home.
This is the zahir al-riwayah position.
2
Locate the exception from Abu Hanifa
If the person makes Makkah a home after the time of the first departure (nafr awwal), then according to a narration from Abu Hanifa (and some from Muhammad), Tawaf al-Sadr becomes wajib.
The key condition is the timing: after the time when pilgrims begin to leave.
3
Understand the dalil for the exception
The obligation enters with the arrival of its time (by the departure of others) and cannot be removed by a later intention to stay. The text gives an analogy: like a fasting person who cannot break the fast after starting it, even if they later travel.
This reasoning emphasizes that once an obligation is fixed, subjective intent cannot nullify it.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
The opposing view (likely the general position of the school) holds that even in that case, it is not wajib because the intention to stay fundamentally changes the status.
The passage does not provide the opposing dalil explicitly, but it is implied that residence eliminates the precondition of departure.
5
Apply the reasoning to a practical scenario
Consider a pilgrim from outside Makkah who, on the 12th of Dhul Hijjah after completing Hajj, decides to settle in Makkah. According to Abu Hanifa's narration, Tawaf al-Sadr becomes wajib because the time for departure has entered; according to the other view, it is not wajib.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is whether the pilgrim must perform one extra tawaf.
