وَمَنِ اتَّخَذَ مَكَّةَ دَارًا فَلَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ طَوَافُ الصَّدْرِ لِأَنَّهُ عَلَى مَن يَصْدُرُ إِلَّا إِذَا اتَّخَذَهَا دَارًا بَعْدَ مَاحَلَّ النَّفَرُ الْأَوَّلُ فِيْمَا يُرُوى عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَيَرْوِيهِ الْبَعْضُ عَنْ مُحَمَّدٍ لِأَنَّهُ وَجَبَ عَلَيْهِ بِدُخُولِ وَقْتِهِ فَلَا يَسْقُطُ بِنِيَّةِ الْإِقَامَةِ بَعْدَ ذلِكَ وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ بِالصَّوَابِ ترجمہ اور جس شخص نے ملکہ کوگھر بنالیا اس پر طواف صدر نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ طواف صدر اس پر ہے جو مکہ اپنے وطن کو واپس ہو گا مگر جبکہ اس نے نفر اول کا وقت آجانے کے بعد مکہ کو گھر بنایا ہو۔ اس روایت میں جو ابو حنیفہ سے مروی ہے اور بعض اس کو امام محمد سے روایت کرتے ہیں کیونکہ طواف صدر اس پر واجب ہو گیا اس کے وقت کے آجانے سے پس اس کے بعد اقامت کی نیت سے ساقط نہ ہو گا۔ تشریح اگر کسی آفاقی نے مکہ المکرمہ کو وطن بنا لیا تو اس پر طواف صدر واجب نہ ہوگا کیونکہ طواف صدر یعینی و داعی طواف اس پر واجب ہوتا ہے جو مکہ سے کوچ کر کے اپنے وطن لوٹے گا۔ حالانکہ یہ شخص مکہ کو دارا قامت بنانے کی وجہ سے ایسا کرنے کا اراد ہ نہیں رکھتا اس لئے اس پر طواف صدر واجب نہ ہوگا ۔ ہاں اگر بارہویں ذی الحجہ کے بعد تیر ہوئیں ذی الحجہ کو مکہ میں اقامت کی نیت کی تو ابوحنیفہ کی روایت کے مطابق اس پر طواف صدر واجب ہوگا ۔ اور بعض حضرات اس کو امام محمد سے روایت کرتے ہیں ۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ تیرہویں ذی الحجہ میں روانگی کا وقت آجانے کی وجہ سے اس پر طواف صد ر واجب ہو گیا۔ اب اس کے بعد اقامت کی نیت کرنے سے واجب شدہ طواف ساقط نہ ہو گا ۔ جیسے کسی مقیم نے رمضان کی صبح کی پھر سفر شروع کر دیا تو اب اس کے لئے افطار کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب - جمیل احمد غفرلہ
And whoever makes Makkah a home, then there is no Tawaf al-Sadr upon him, because it is only upon one who departs (to his homeland), except if he made it a home after the time of the first departure, according to what is narrated from Abu Hanifa, and some narrate it from Muhammad, because it became obligatory upon him by the entry of its time, so it does not fall by the intention of staying after that. And Allah knows best the truth. Translation: And the person who made Makkah a home, there is no Tawaf al-Sadr upon him. Because Tawaf al-Sadr is upon one who will return to his homeland from Makkah, except when he made Makkah a home after the time of the first departure had arrived. This narration is from Abu Hanifa, and some narrate it from Imam Muhammad, because Tawaf al-Sadr became obligatory upon him by the arrival of its time, so after that it will not be nullified by the intention of staying. Commentary: If an afaaqi (one from outside) makes Makkah al-Mukarramah his home, then Tawaf al-Sadr will not be obligatory upon him, because Tawaf al-Sadr, i.e., the farewell tawaf, is obligatory only on one who departs from Makkah to return to his homeland. However, since this person does not intend to do so because he made Makkah his home, therefore Tawaf al-Sadr will not be obligatory. But if he intends to stay in Makkah after the 12th of Dhul Hijjah on the 13th of Dhul Hijjah, then according to the narration of Abu Hanifa, Tawaf al-Sadr will be obligatory upon him. And some honorable ones narrate this from Imam Muhammad. The proof is that because the time of departure on the 13th of Dhul Hijjah has arrived, Tawaf al-Sadr became obligatory. Now after that, the obligatory tawaf will not be nullified by the intention of staying. Like a resident who started fasting in Ramadan and then began a journey, then breaking the fast is not permissible for him. And Allah knows best the truth. - Jameel Ahmad, may He forgive him.
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute passage from the chapter of Hajj regarding the obligation of Tawaf al-Sadr for a person who makes Makkah their permanent home. The author (al-Quduri) states the general rule: if a person makes Makkah their home, Tawaf al-Sadr is not obligatory because this tawaf is intended for those departing to their homeland. However, an exception is narrated from Abu Hanifa and some from Imam Muhammad: if the person made Makkah their home after the time for the first departure (nafr awwal, i.e., after the 12th of Dhul Hijjah), then Tawaf al-Sadr becomes obligatory because its time has entered (as the pilgrims begin to leave). The obligation cannot be removed by subsequently intending to stay, analogous to a fasting person in Ramadan who cannot break his fast once he has started it, even if he then travels. The commentary explains that the analogy is that once an obligation is fixed by its time, it cannot be nullified by a later intention. The passage leaves the dispute unresolved, saying 'Allah knows best.' The two narrations represent differing views within the Hanafi school on whether the obligation is triggered by the mere passage of time or is contingent upon actual departure.

Key Terms
طواف الصدر (Tawaf al-Sadr): The farewell circumambulation performed when leaving Makkah after completing Hajj.
نفر أول (nafr awwal): The first departure from Mina to Makkah, which occurs on the 12th of Dhul Hijjah. After this time, pilgrims are allowed to leave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the narration from Abu Hanifa, when does making Makkah a home not exempt one from Tawaf al-Sadr?
A) When one makes Makkah a home before the nafr awwal
B) When one makes Makkah a home after the nafr awwal
C) Always, regardless of timing
D) Only if one is a resident of Makkah originally

Key Takeaway
The obligation of Tawaf al-Sadr for a resident of Makkah is contingent on the timing of the decision to stay; if after nafr awwal, it remains wajib according to one Hanafi narration.

Penalties for Applying Perfume While in Ihram
Rulings on jinayat for muhrim applying perfume with intra-Hanafi differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on applying perfume while in ihram, explain the distinction between full limb and less than full limb, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on the penalty for less than a limb.

Core Idea
Applying perfume in ihram requires kaffarah: a dam for a full limb, sadaqah for less.

In this lesson, we examine the chapter of jinayat (crimes during ihram) from the Hajj section. The text establishes that applying perfume while in the state of ihram is a prohibited act that necessitates expiation. The key factor determining the penalty is the extent of the limb perfumed. The passage also introduces an intra-Hanafi difference of opinion regarding the penalty when less than a full limb is perfumed, setting the stage for a later discussion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Note that applying perfume while in ihram is a jinaya (prohibited act) that necessitates kaffarah. The text states this at the beginning.
The act is not simply makruh; it incurs a specific penalty.
2
Distinguish between full limb and less than full limb
The penalty depends on the extent of the body part perfumed. A complete limb (e.g., head, shin, thigh) or more requires a dam; less requires sadaqah. Understand the reasoning: complete benefit equals complete penalty.
Examples given: head, shin, thigh.
3
Examine the dalil and its wajh al-dalalah
The hadith 'الحاج الشعث النفل' is used as proof that perfume removes the desired state of dishevelment, so it is a crime. The dalil is zanni in thubut and dalala, and can be overridden by istihsan.
This is a dalil naqli from ahad hadith.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Muhammad suggests proportional dam for less than a limb; al-Muntaqa suggests full dam for a quarter limb by analogy to shaving. The main position (Quduri) holds to sadaqah. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.
The text promises to explain the difference later.

Chapter of Jinayat (Crimes). Translation: This chapter is about explaining jinayat. Commentary: After finishing the types and rulings of muhrims, now mention will be made of those incidental matters that affect ihram. Jinayat is the plural of janabah. A jinayat is an act that is prohibited by shariah. For a muhrim, applying perfume necessitates kaffarah; if he applies perfume to a complete limb or more, then dam (sacrifice) is required. And when a muhrim applies perfume, then the kaffarah is upon him: if he applied to a complete limb or more, then upon him is dam, such as the head, shin, thigh, and the like, because the crime is complete by complete benefit, and that is in the complete limb, so the complete obligation follows. And if he applied perfume to less than a limb, then upon him is sadaqah due to the deficiency of the crime. And Muhammad said: proportional to that from the dam is obligatory, considering the part to the whole. And in al-Muntaqa it is that if he applied to a quarter of a limb, then upon him is dam, by analogy to shaving. And we will mention the difference between them later, if Allah wills. Then the obligatory dam is fulfilled by a sheep in all places except two places which we will mention in the chapter of al-Hady, if Allah wills.
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This is a ruling from the chapter of jinayat (crimes during ihram) in the Hajj section. The text begins by defining jinayat as actions prohibited by shariah. Then it states the ruling on applying perfume while in ihram: it requires kaffarah (expiation). The ruling distinguishes based on the amount of perfume applied. If applied to a complete limb (e.g., head, shin, thigh) or more, then the kaffarah is a dam (sacrifice of a sheep). The reason given is that the crime is complete when the benefit derived from the perfume is complete, and a complete limb provides complete benefit. If less than a full limb is perfumed, then the kaffarah is sadaqah (charity). The proof cited is the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'The pilgrim is disheveled and dusty'—meaning the state of a muhrim is to be without adornment; perfume removes this state, so it is a crime. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Muhammad holds that for less than a limb, the dam should be proportional (e.g., half limb -> half dam), based on qiyas (analogy). However, the author (al-Quduri) maintains the view that sadaqah is fixed. Additionally, al-Muntaqa (a later Hanafi work) reports a third view: applying perfume to a quarter of a limb requires a full dam, analogizing to shaving a quarter of the head in ihram, which requires a dam. The text promises to differentiate between these views later. Finally, it notes that the dam (when required) is fulfilled by slaughtering a sheep, except in two specific cases to be mentioned in the chapter on hady (sacrificial animals).

Key Terms
جنایات (jinayat): Crimes or prohibited actions committed during ihram, such as applying perfume, which require expiation (kaffarah).
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (sheep or goat) sacrificed as expiation for certain violations during ihram.
صدقہ (sadaqah): Charity, here meaning a specific amount of food (e.g., half a sa' of wheat) given to the poor as expiation for a lesser jinaya.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the main Hanafi position (Quduri), what is the required kaffarah for applying perfume to less than a full limb while in ihram?
A) A full dam
B) Sadaqah (charity)
C) Proportional dam (e.g., half dam for half limb)
D) No penalty at all

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the penalty for applying perfume in ihram depends on the extent of the limb: a full limb requires a dam, less than a full limb requires sadaqah, though there is intra-madhhab disagreement on the latter.

Penalty for Perfuming Less than a Limb in Ihram: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on penalty for perfuming less than a limb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the penalty for perfuming less than a limb in ihram and explain the reasoning behind each.

Core Idea
For less than a limb, sadaqah suffices; but some Hanafi masters require proportional or full dam by analogy.

When a muhrim applies perfume to part of a limb, the penalty is not uniform among Hanafi authorities. This passage from al-Hidayah presents the primary ruling of sadaqah, then introduces two variant views—one requiring proportional dam, another a full dam for a quarter limb. Understanding these differences reveals how qiyas and istihsan operate in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling
The matn states that if a muhrim perfumes less than a whole limb, the penalty is sadaqah (charity). The reason given is 'due to the deficiency of the offense' (li qusur al-jinayah).
Sadaqah here is a specific measure, typically half a sa' of wheat.
2
Examine Imam Muhammad's view
Imam Muhammad argues for a proportional amount of dam (blood sacrifice) based on a part-to-whole analogy (qiyas). He considers the part equivalent to the whole in triggering the major penalty.
This qiyas is of the jaliy type.
3
Examine the view from al-Muntaqa
The author of al-Muntaqa holds that if one perfumes a quarter of a limb, a full dam is required, analogizing to shaving a quarter of the head (which requires dam).
This is a different qiyas based on a different original case.
4
Understand the rationale for the primary view
Abu Hanifa rejects the analogy because the part is not equivalent to the whole; the crime is incomplete and therefore should incur a lesser penalty.
This reflects Hanafi istihsan.
5
Note the promise of further clarification
The commentator promises to mention the difference between the two qiyas later, indicating the complexity of the issue.
This passage is a summary; a fuller discussion likely follows in the original text.

Source Text

وَإِن تَطَيَّبَ أَقَلَّ مِن عُضْوِ فَعَلَيْهِ الصَّدَقَةُ لِقُصُورِ الْجِنَايَةِ وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدُ يَجِبُ بِقَدْرِهِ مِنَ الدَّمِ اعْتَبَارَا الجُزْءِ بِالْكُلَّ وَ فِي الْمُتَقَى أَنَّهُ إِذَا طَيِّبَ رُبَعَ الْعُضْوِ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمُ اِعْتِبَارَا بِالْخَلْقِ وَ نَحْنُ نَذَكَّرُ الْفَرَقَ بَيْنَهُمَا مِن بعد انشَاءَ الله
And if he perfumed less than a limb, then upon him is charity (sadaqah) due to the deficiency of the offense. And Muhammad said: There is incumbent according to its measure of blood (dam), drawing analogy of part to whole. And in al-Muntaqa: That if he perfumed a quarter of a limb, then upon him is a dam, drawing analogy to shaving. And we will mention the difference between them later, if Allah wills.
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the penalty for a muhrim who applies perfume to less than a full limb. The primary ruling (attributed to the matn) states that only sadaqah (charity) is required because the violation is less severe. However, Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani analogizes the part to the whole, requiring a proportional amount of dam (blood sacrifice). Meanwhile, the text of al-Muntaqa holds that if a quarter of a limb is perfumed, a full dam is due, drawing an analogy to shaving a quarter of the head. The commentator promises to explain the distinction later. The Hanafi relied-upon position is the matn's ruling of sadaqah for less than a limb, but the student should note the existence of these alternative views.

Key Terms
صَدَقَة (sadaqah): Charitable penalty for minor ihram violations, here for perfuming less than a limb.
دَم (dam): Blood sacrifice (goat) as penalty for major ihram violations.
جِنايَة (jinayah): Offense or violation committed during ihram, here specifically the act of applying perfume.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the matn's ruling, what is the penalty for a muhrim who applies perfume to less than a limb?
A) Dam (blood sacrifice)
B) Sadaqah (charity)
C) Nothing
D) Two dams

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the penalty for perfuming less than a limb in ihram is sadaqah, though proportional or full dam are variant opinions.

Fulfilling the Obligatory Dam with a Goat
Ruling that dam is fulfilled by a goat except two cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rule for fulfilling the obligatory dam in Hajj and identify that there are two exceptions.

Core Idea
The obligatory dam is generally fulfilled by a goat, except in two specific cases.

In Hajj, various violations require a dam (blood sacrifice). This passage lays down the foundational rule: the dam is fulfilled by a goat. However, there are two exceptions that will be covered later in the chapter on Hady. This rule is a key memorization anchor for understanding dam obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligation
The act under discussion is the obligatory dam (wajib dam) owed for violations of ihram.
2
State the general ruling
The passage declares that the dam is fulfilled by a goat (shah) in all places, meaning generally applicable.
Shah can refer to a goat or sheep.
3
Note the exception
The text explicitly says there are two cases where this does not apply, but does not detail them here.
The exceptions are mentioned later in the chapter on Hady.
4
Recognize the significance
This is a foundational principle; knowing it helps avoid errors in fulfilling dam obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ وَاجِبُ اللَّهِ يَادَى بِالشَّاةِ فِي جَمِيعِ المَوَاضِع إِلا فِي مَوْضِعَينِ نَذْكُرُهُمَا فِي بَابِ الْهَدَى إِنشَاءَ اللهُ
Then the obligatory dam is fulfilled by a goat in all places except two places which we will mention in the chapter of Hady, if Allah wills.
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This is a general ruling from the matn stating that whenever a dam (blood sacrifice) is obligatory upon a muhrim due to a violation, it is fulfilled by sacrificing a goat (shah). This applies universally to all types of dam except two specific cases which will be explained later in the chapter on Hady. The two exceptions are: 1) when Tawaf al-Ziyarah is performed in a state of janabah or hayd/nifas, and 2) when sexual intercourse occurs after Wuquf at Arafah. In those cases, a camel or cow is required, not a goat.

Key Terms
دَم (dam): Obligatory blood sacrifice for ihram violations.
شاة (shah): Goat (or sheep) used for the sacrifice.

Default Sadaqah Amount in Ihram: Half Sa' of Wheat
Specification of the amount of unspecified sadaqah in ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default amount of sadaqah in ihram for unspecified violations and identify the exception for killing a louse or grasshopper.

Core Idea
Default unspecified sadaqah in ihram is half a sa' of wheat, except for killing louse/grasshopper.

This lesson establishes a clear default measure for sadaqah penalties when a muhrim commits a violation that requires compensation but no specific amount is given in the texts. The Hanafi school, based on a narration from Imam Abu Yusuf, sets the standard at half a sa' of wheat. A sa' is a volume measure, roughly 2.4 kg of wheat. However, this fixed measure does not apply when the violation is killing a louse or grasshopper, where the amount is left unquantified.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The text states that every unspecified sadaqah in ihram is half a sa' of wheat. Understand that this applies only when the violation's penalty is not otherwise specified in the sources.
2
Recognize the exception
Note the exception: 'except what is obligatory due to killing a louse or a grasshopper.' For these two cases, the amount is not fixed; the muhrim may give any amount.
3
Attribute the narration
The text attributes this ruling to Imam Abu Yusuf. In Hanafi fiqh, this gives the ruling a strong basis within the school's transmitted rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَكُلُّ صَدَقَةٍ فِي الْإِخْرَامٍ غَيْرُ مُقَدَّرَةٍ فَهِيَ نِصْفُ صَاعِ مِنَ بُرَ إِلَّا مَايَجِبُ بِقَتْلِ الْقُمَّلَةِ وَالْجَرَادَةِ هَكَذَا رُوِيَ عَنْ أَبِي يُوسُفَ
And every charity (sadaqah) in ihram that is not fixed in amount is half a sa' of wheat, except what is obligatory due to killing a louse or a grasshopper. Thus it is narrated from Abu Yusuf.
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This matn statement establishes the standard amount for unspecified sadaqah in ihram. When a muhrim commits a violation that requires sadaqah (charity) but no specific amount is mentioned in the texts, the default amount is half a sa' of wheat. A sa' is approximately 2.4 kg, so half a sa' is about 1.2 kg of wheat. However, this does not apply to killing a louse or a grasshopper, where the amount is left to the discretion of the muhrim. This ruling is narrated from Imam Abu Yusuf, indicating its authority within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
صاع (sa'): Unit of volume, approximately 2.4 kg of wheat in Hanafi school.
بر (burr): Wheat, the grain used for the sadaqah measurement.
صَدَقَة (sadaqah): Charitable penalty for minor ihram violations; here a fixed amount of wheat.

Henna in Ihram: Perfume and Covering
Ruling on henna as perfume causing dam, with additional dam for matted hair

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for applying henna to the head in ihram and identify when one or two dams are required.

Core Idea
Henna is perfume; applying it in ihram requires a dam, and matted hair adds a second dam for covering.

In ihram, perfuming and covering the head are prohibited. This lesson examines the ruling on henna, which the Prophet declared perfume. The text from Al-Hidayah explains the penalty and the additional penalty if the hair becomes matted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is applying henna to the head in ihram. What is the hukm of the act, and what penalty does it incur?
The act itself is haram (prohibited). The penalty is a dam (wajib compensation).
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? The hadith: 'Henna is perfume.'
This hadith is ahad, zanni al-thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this hadith prove the ruling? Perfuming in ihram is prohibited, so applying henna, being perfume, is prohibited and incurs dam.
The classification of henna as tib directly links to the prohibition of perfume in ihram.
4
Examine the condition of matted hair
If the henna causes the hair to become matted (mulabbad), it constitutes covering, which is also prohibited. How does this affect the penalty?
Two dams: one for perfume, one for covering.
5
Note the simultaneous prohibitions
A single act can violate multiple ihram restrictions. Here, both perfume and covering are present.
Each prohibition independently requires a dam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ فإن حَضَبَ رَأْسَهُ بِجَمَاء فَعَلَيْهِ دَمُ لأنه طيب قَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ الْحِمَاء طِيبُ وَإِن صَارَ مُلَبَدًا فَعَلَيْهِ دمان دَمُ للتَّطيِّبِ وَدَمُ لِلتَّعْطِيَةٍ وَلَو خَضَبَ رَأْسَهُ بِالْوَسمَةِ لَا شَيْ عَلَيْهِ لأَنَّهَا لَيْسَتْ بِطِيبٍ وَعَنْ أَبِي يُوْسُفَ أَنَّهُ إِذَا خطب رَأسَهُ بِالوَسَمَةِ لأجلِ الْمُعَالَجَةِ مِنَ الصُّداع فعليه الجَزَاء بِإِعْتِبار أنه يُعلق رأسه وهذَا هُوَ الصَّحِيح ثُمَّ ذَكَرَ فِى الأَصل رَأْسَهُ وَلِحْيَةُ واقتصر على ذكر الراس فى الجامع الصغير دَلَّ أَنْ كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا مَضمُونَ
He said: If he dyed his head with henna, then upon him is a dam because it is perfume. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Henna is perfume.' And if it becomes matted, then upon him are two dams: a dam for perfuming and a dam for covering. And if he dyed his head with woad, there is nothing upon him because it is not perfume. And from Abu Yusuf: That if he dyed his head with woad for the purpose of treatment from headache, then upon him is the penalty (jaza') with the consideration that he covers his head, and this is the correct (view). Then he mentioned in al-Asl: his head and beard, and confined to mentioning the head in al-Jami' al-Saghir, indicating that each one of them is liable.
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This passage covers several rulings. First, applying henna (hina) to the head in ihram is considered perfuming (tayyib) because the Prophet ﷺ declared henna to be perfume. Therefore, a dam is required. If the henna causes the hair to become matted (mulabbad), meaning the hair clumps together, then two dams are due: one for the perfume and one for covering the hair (taghtiya), which is also forbidden in ihram. Second, woad (wasma) is generally not perfume, so dyeing the head with it does not incur any penalty. However, Imam Abu Yusuf reports that if woad is used for medical treatment of headache, then it becomes a form of covering the head, and thus a penalty is due. This is considered the correct view. The matn in al-Asl mentions both head and beard, but al-Jami' al-Saghir only mentions the head, implying that both are covered by the same ruling.

Key Terms
حِنَّاء (hinna): Henna plant used for dyeing; considered perfume in ihram.
مُلَبَّد (mulabbad): Matted hair; here refers to hair clumped with dye, considered a form of covering.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a muhrim applies henna and his hair does not become matted, how many dams does he owe?
A) None
B) One
C) Two
D) Depends on intention

Key Takeaway
Henna is perfume in ihram, and matted hair adds a dam for covering.

Woad in Ihram: General Permissibility and Medical Exception
Ruling on woad: generally permissible, but Abu Yusuf adds penalty for medical covering

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rule for woad in ihram and apply Abu Yusuf's exception for medical covering.

Core Idea
Woad is not perfume, but covering the head with it for treatment incurs a penalty.

Woad is a plant dye that is not considered perfume. Therefore, a muhrim may apply it to his head without penalty. However, if used for medical treatment, it becomes a form of covering, and according to Imam Abu Yusuf, a penalty is due. This lesson explores this intra-Hanafi difference.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
What is the default ruling for applying woad to the head in ihram?
No penalty because woad is not perfume.
2
Identify the exception
What did Abu Yusuf say?
If used for medical treatment of headache, it becomes a covering and incurs penalty.
3
Understand the rationale
Why does covering trigger a penalty even if the substance is not perfume?
Covering the head in ihram is prohibited regardless of the material.
4
Note the tarjih
Which view is considered correct in the text?
Abu Yusuf's view is declared correct.

Source Text

Therefore, a dam is required. If the henna causes the hair to become matted (mulabbad), meaning the hair clumps together, then two dams are due: one for the perfume and one for covering the hair (taghtiya), which is also forbidden in ihram. Amount of Unspecified Sadaqah in Ihram
Defines the standard amount of unspecified sadaqah in ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the standard Hanafi ruling for unspecified sadaqah in ihram and identify the exception for killing lice or locusts.

Core Idea
Unspecified sadaqah in ihram defaults to half a sa' of wheat, except for killing a louse or locust where no fixed amount is required.

The source text defines the standard expiation for ihram violations where no specific amount is mentioned in the primary sources. The Hanafi school relies on a narration from Imam Abu Yusuf to set the default at half a sa' of wheat. However, an exception is made for minor acts like killing a louse or locust, where the expiation is left flexible, as indicated by a statement of Umar ibn al-Khattab (RA).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the passage addresses sadaqah (charitable expiation) for unspecified ihram violations. The ruling is that a fixed amount of half a sa' of wheat is obligatory (wajib).
2
Note the default amount
The default amount for any unspecified sadaqah is half a sa' of wheat, as narrated from Abu Yusuf. This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
The Hanafi sa' is approximately 3.2 liters (about 2.5 kg of wheat).
3
Identify the exception
Killing a louse or a locust is excluded from the default. No fixed amount is prescribed; the pilgrim may give any sadaqah, even a single date.
The saying of Umar ('A date is better than a locust') supports this flexibility.
4
Understand the evidence
The ruling is based on a narration from Abu Yusuf, which is part of the zahir al-riwayah. The exception is supported by a companion's statement.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a pilgrim who shaves his hair due to illness (an unspecified violation). He must give half a sa' of wheat. Another pilgrim kills a louse; he may give a small amount like a date.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
احرام میں واجب ہونے والے صدقہ کی مقدار
وَكُلُّ صَدَقَةٍ فِي الْإِخْرَامٍ غَيْرُ مُقَدَّرَةٍ فَهِيَ نِصْفُ صَاعِ مِنَ بُرَ إِلَّا مَايَجِبُ بِقَتْلِ الْقُمَّلَةِ وَالْجَرَادَةِ هَكَذَا رُوِيَ عَنْ أَبِي يُوسُفَ ترجمہ اور ہر صدقہ احرام میں جس کی کوئی مقدار معین نہیں ہے تو وہ گندم کا نصف صاع ہے مگر وہ جو جوں اور ٹڈی کے مارڈالنے سے واجب ہوتا ہے۔ ایسا ہی امام ابو یوسف سے مروی ہے۔ تشریح فرمایا کہ احترام کے جرم میں اگر ویسا صدقہ واجب ہوا جس کی کوئی مقدار معین مذکور نہیں ہے تو ایسی صورت میں گندم کا آدھا حصال واجب ہو گا ہاں اگر کسی نے بحالت احرام جوں ماردی یا نڈی مارڈالی تو اس میں جو چاہے صدقہ کر دے اس میں کوئی مقدار معین نہیں ہے۔ حضرت عمر نے فرمایا التَّمَرَةُ خَيْرٌ مِنَ الْجَرَادَةِ ندی سے تو ایک چھوہارہ ہی بہتر ہے۔
The amount of sadaqah obligated in ihram. Every sadaqah in ihram that is not specified in quantity is half a sa' of wheat, except that which is obligatory due to killing a louse or a locust. Thus it is narrated from Abu Yusuf. Translation: And every sadaqah in ihram for which no specific quantity is mentioned is half a sa' of wheat, except that which becomes obligatory by killing a louse or a locust. This is narrated from Imam Abu Yusuf. Explanation: He said that if in the crime of ihram such a sadaqah becomes obligatory for which no specific quantity is mentioned, then in that case half a sa' of wheat becomes obligatory. Yes, if someone in the state of ihram kills a louse or kills a locust, then he may give whatever sadaqah he wishes; no specific quantity is fixed for it. Hadrat Umar said: 'A date is better than a locust.' So a single date is better than a locust.
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the Hanafi school on the standard quantity of sadaqah (charitable expiation) when no specific amount is mentioned in the texts of ihram violations. The relied-upon position (madhhab) is that such unspecified sadaqah is half a sa' of wheat, as narrated from Imam Abu Yusuf. This applies to various minor violations in ihram where the expiation is not precisely defined, such as cutting nails or wearing sewn clothes unintentionally. However, killing a louse or a locust is an exception: no fixed amount is prescribed; one may give any sadaqah, even a single date, as indicated by the statement of 'Umar. This flexibility reflects the minimal harm caused by these insects. The passage follows the order: first the general rule, then the exception, then an explanatory note with a companion's saying.

Key Terms
صاع (sa'): A measure of volume, approximately 2.5 kg of wheat, used in Hanafi fiqh for zakat and expiations.
صدقہ (sadaqah): Charitable expiation given as compensation for specific violations in ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A full sa' of wheat
B) Half a sa' of wheat
C) A handful of dates
D) One dirham

Key Takeaway
Unspecified sadaqah in ihram is half a sa' of wheat by default, but killing a louse or locust has no fixed amount.

Henna and Wasmah Dye in Ihram: When Does Dam Become Wajib?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on dam for hair dyes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on dyeing with henna and wasmah in ihram, and distinguish between the positions of Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf regarding wasmah.

Core Idea
Henna is a perfume requiring dam; wasmah is not, but covering the head with it may still incur dam.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a common hajj issue: dyeing hair while in ihram. The Hanafi school categorizes henna as a perfume (tib), making its application a violation. But what about wasmah, a plant-based dye? Here we find a nuanced dispute between the founding imams, resolved by later authorities based on the underlying cause of covering the head.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling on henna
Read Imam Muhammad's statement: dyeing the head with henna incurs dam because henna is a perfume, supported by the hadith 'Al-hinna' tib'.
The dam is a sacrifice (e.g., a sheep) as expiation.
2
Analyze the additional penalty for matted hair
If the hair becomes matted (mulabbad) due to henna, two dams are required: one for the perfume and one for covering the head.
Covering the head is a separate violation in ihram.
3
State the default ruling on wasmah
Imam Muhammad's position: dyeing with wasmah incurs no dam because it is not a perfume.
Wasmah is a plant dye (like indigo), not considered tib.
4
Understand Abu Yusuf's exception
Abu Yusuf holds that if wasmah is used for treatment (e.g., headache), it requires dam because it covers the head, regardless of perfume status.
Covering the head is the operative cause (illa).
5
Resolve the textual discrepancy
In al-Mabsut, both head and beard are mentioned; in al-Jami' al-Saghir, only head. This indicates that dyeing either part individually incurs dam.
Each part is an independent basis for liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حنا کا خضاب لگانے سے دم لازم ہے
قال فإن حَضَبَ رَأْسَهُ بِجَمَاء فَعَلَيْهِ دَمُ لأنه طيب قَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ الْحِمَاء طِيبُ وَإِن صَارَ مُلَبَدًا فَعَلَيْهِ دمان دَمُ للتَّطيِّبِ وَدَمُ لِلتَّعْطِيَةٍ وَلَو خَضَبَ رَأْسَهُ بِالْوَسمَةِ لَا شَيْ عَلَيْهِ لأَنَّهَا لَيْسَتْ بِطِيبٍ وَعَنْ أَبِي يُوْسُفَ أَنَّهُ إِذَا خطب رَأسَهُ بِالوَسَمَةِ لأجلِ الْمُعَالَجَةِ مِنَ الصُّداع فعليه الجَزَاء بِإِعْتِبار أنه يُعلق رأسَه وهذَا هُوَ الصَّحِيح ثُمَّ ذَكَرَ فِى الأَصل رَأْسَهُ وَلِحْيَةُ واقتصر على ذكر الراس فى الجامع الصغير دَلَّ أَنْ كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا مَضمُونَ ترجمہ امام محمد نے کہا کہ اگر محترم نے اپنے سر میں حنا سے خضاب کیا تو اس پر دم واجب ہے کیونکہ حنا خوشبو سے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ حنا خوشبو ہے۔ اور اگر سر ملبد ہو گیا تو اس پر دودم میں ایک دم خوشبو لگانے کی وجہ سے اور ایک دم سر ڈھانکنے کی وجہ سے ۔ اور اگر مرد نے انی سر وسمہ سے خضاب کیا تو اس پر کچھ لازم نہیں ہے کیونکہ وسمہ خوشبو نہیں ہے۔ اور ابو یوسف سے مروی ہے کہ جب محرم نے وسمہ سے درد صرف طلاق کی وجہ سے اپنے سر کا خضاب کیا تو اس پر کفارہ ہے اس اعتبار سے کہ وہ اپنے سر کو ڈ ھانکتا ہے اور یہی بیج ہے پھر مبسوط میں سر اور دار کی جانا کہ کیا ہے اور جامع صفیہ میں سر کے ذکر پر اکتفاء کیا ہے ہاں جامع صغیر سے ولالت ہوئی کہ ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک مضمون تشریح مسئلہ کو کسی محرم نے اپنے سر میں مہندی کا خضاب کیا تو اس جرم کی پاداش میں اس پر دم یعنی ایک قربانی واجب ہے کیونکہ مہندی ایک طرح کی خوشبو ہے چنانچہ حضور ۱۰ کا ارشاد ہے الجبار طیب اور احرام کی حالت میں مہندی لگانا جرم ہے اس لئے اس پر دم جنایت واجب ہوگا۔ اور اگر حالت احترام میں مہندی کا لیپ اس طرح کر دیا گیا کہ بال جم گئے تو اس محرم پر دو قربانیاں واجب ہوں گی بشر طیکہ یہ لیپ ایک رات یا ایک دن پورے سر یا چوتھائی سر پر رہے۔ ایک قربانی تو خوشبو لگانے کی وجہ سے واجب ہوئی اور دوسری قربانی
سرڈھانکنے کی وجہ سے واجب ہوئی۔
اور اگر کسی محرم نے اپنے سر کا خضاب وسمہ درخت کی پتیوں سے کیا تو اس پر کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہ خوشبو شمار نہیں کی جاتی ۔ اور امام ابو یوسف سے مروی ہے کہ اگر وسمہ سے سر کا خضاب کیا تا کہ سر کا دردزائل ہو جائے یعنی بغرض علاج اس کا استعمال کیا تو اس پر کفارہ واجب ہو گا مگر کفارہ کا وجوب اس لئے نہیں ہو گا کہ اس نے خوشبو لگائی بلکہ اس لئے واجب ہوگا کہ وہ وسمہ کے خضاب سے اپنے سر کو ڈھانک لیتا ہے اور حالت احرام میں سرکا ڈھانکنا بالاتفاق موجب دم ہے یہی صحیح ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے مبسوط اور جامع صغیر کی روایتوں میں فرق کرتے ہوئے ذکر کیا کہ مبسوط میں داڑھی اور سر دونوں کا ذکر ہے اور جامع صغیر میں فقط سر کا ذکر ہے۔ جامع صغیر کی روایت سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ دم واجب ہونے کے لئے سر اور داڑھی دونوں پر علی سبیل الاجتماع خضاب کرنا شرط نہیں ہے بلکہ ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کا خضاب قربانی واجب کرتا ہے۔
Dyeing with henna necessitates dam. He (Imam Muhammad) said: If he dyes his head with henna, then upon him is a dam, because it is a perfume. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Henna is a perfume.' And if it becomes matted, then upon him are two dams: a dam for perfuming and a dam for covering. And if he dyes his head with wasmah, there is nothing upon him, because it is not a perfume. And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that if he dyes his head with wasmah for the purpose of treating a headache, then upon him is kaffarah, considering that he covers his head, and this is the correct (view). Then in al-Asl (Mabsut) he mentioned both head and beard, but in al-Jami' al-Sagheer he confined mention to the head, indicating that each of them is liable (individually). Translation: Imam Muhammad said: If a muhrim dyes his head with henna, then dam is obligatory upon him because henna is a perfume; the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Henna is a perfume.' And if the head becomes matted, then upon him are two dams: one dam due to applying perfume and one dam due to covering the head. And if a man dyes his head with wasmah, then nothing is obligatory upon him because wasmah is not a perfume. And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that when a muhrim dyes his head with wasmah due to a headache (for treatment), then upon him is kaffarah, considering that he covers his head, and this is the correct (view). Then in Mabsut he mentioned both head and beard, but in Jami' Sagheer he sufficed with mentioning the head, indicating that each of them is liable (individually). Explanation: The issue: If a muhrim dyes his head with henna, then in penalty for this crime, a dam i.e. one sacrifice is obligatory because henna is a kind of perfume. Thus the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Al-hinna' tib (Henna is a perfume). And applying henna in the state of ihram is a crime, so dam jinayat becomes obligatory. And if in the state of ihram the henna paste is applied in such a way that the hair become matted, then upon that muhrim two sacrifices are obligatory, provided that this paste remains for one night or one day on the whole head or a quarter of the head. One sacrifice became obligatory due to applying perfume, and the second sacrifice became obligatory due to covering the head. And if some muhrim dyes his head with wasmah, leaves of a tree, then nothing is obligatory upon him, because it is not counted as perfume. And it is narrated from Imam Abu Yusuf that if he dyes his head with wasmah so that the headache goes away, i.e. uses it for treatment, then kaffarah is obligatory. But the obligation of kaffarah is not because he applied perfume, but rather it becomes obligatory because by the wasmah dye he covers his head, and covering the head in the state of ihram is unanimously a cause for dam. This is the correct view. The author of Hidayah, mentioning the difference between the narrations of Mabsut and Jami' Sagheer, said that in Mabsut both beard and head are mentioned, and in Jami' Sagheer only the head is mentioned. From the narration of Jami' Sagheer it is understood that for dam to be obligatory, dyeing both head and beard jointly is not a condition; rather, dyeing each of them individually also necessitates a sacrifice.
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the obligation of dam (sacrificial expiation) for a muhrim who dyes his hair. The base ruling from Imam Muhammad states that dyeing with henna incurs dam because henna is considered a perfume (tib), supported by a hadith. If the hair becomes matted (mulabbad) due to the application, then two dams are required: one for perfuming and one for covering the head (covering being a separate violation). For dyeing with wasmah (a plant dye), the general ruling is no dam because it is not a perfume. However, Imam Abu Yusuf distinguishes: if wasmah is used for treatment (e.g., for headache), then dam becomes obligatory because it involves covering the head, and covering the head in ihram is a violation. The text also clarifies a textual discrepancy: in al-Mabsut, Imam Muhammad mentions both head and beard, but in al-Jami' al-Saghir he mentions only the head. This indicates that each part independently can incur dam, not necessarily together. The commentary follows the original order: first the ruling on henna, then wasmah, then Abu Yusuf's view, then the textual analysis.

Key Terms
حنا (hinna'): Henna, a plant-based dye considered a perfume (tib) by the Hanafi school.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (e.g., a sheep) offered as expiation for specific ihram violations.
وسمہ (wasmah): A plant used for dyeing (indigo or similar), not considered a perfume.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school, when does dyeing with wasmah require dam?
A) In all cases, because it covers the head
B) Only when used for treatment that involves covering the head
C) Never, because it is not a perfume
D) Only if mixed with henna

Key Takeaway
Henna requires dam as perfume; wasmah requires dam only when used in a way that covers the head (e.g., for treatment), per the relied-upon view.

Olive Oil in Ihram: Dam or Sadaqah? Intra-Hanafi and Inter-Madhhab Ikhtilaf
Dispute on expiation for olive oil use in ihram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the positions of Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the expiation for applying olive oil in ihram, and identify the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) between their rulings.

Core Idea
Olive oil's dual nature as perfume and edible creates an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: dam vs sadaqah.

For a muhrim, even applying pure olive oil triggers a significant ikhtilaf among the Hanafi imams themselves and with the Shafi'i school. This lesson unpacks the proofs given by each side and shows how the classification of the oil as a 'complete' or 'deficient' crime determines the expiation. Understanding this dispute clarifies the Hanafi method of weighing multiple attributes in a single substance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and the Dispute
The act is a muhrim applying pure olive oil (or sesame oil). Three positions exist: Abu Hanifa says dam, the Sahibayn say sadaqah, and Imam al-Shafi'i says dam if applied to hair, nothing otherwise.
Note that the dispute is only for pure oils; perfumed oils are unanimous.
2
Analyze the Proof of the Sahibayn
The Sahibayn argue that olive oil is primarily an edible item (min al-at'imah). Its additional benefits (killing vermin, removing dishevelment) are secondary, making it a 'deficient crime' (jinayah qasirah) that only warrants sadaqah.
Study the concept of jinayah qasirah – it is a partial violation incurring a lesser penalty.
3
Analyze the Proof of Abu Hanifa
Abu Hanifa argues that olive oil is the origin of perfume and contains a type of perfume, kills vermin, softens hair, and removes dirt. These multiple benefits make the crime 'complete' (mutakamil), thus requiring dam. He draws analogy to saffron (za'faran), which is both edible and a perfume.
The reasoning is based on the totality of benefits, not just one.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i Position and the Hanafi Response
Imam al-Shafi'i focuses only on removing dishevelment (sha'th), which only occurs when oil is applied to hair. The Hanafi response is that the oil has effects beyond hair, so its use anywhere triggers the full penalty.
This shows a difference in considering multiple vs singular effects.
5
Apply to Perfumed Oils and Determine the Practical Consequence
Perfumed oils (e.g., violet, jasmine) are unanimously dam because they are clearly perfumes. The practical difference: a Hanafi mufti following Abu Hanifa would require a sacrifice, while one following the Sahibayn would require only charity. A Shafi'i would require sacrifice only if applied to hair.
The thamarah al-khilaf is significant: a full animal vs half a sa' of wheat.

Source Text

زیتون کا تیل لگانے سے دم لازم ہے یا صدقہ ، اقوال فقہاء
فَإِن ادمنَ بزَيْتِ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ عِندَابِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَا عَلَيْهِ الصَّدَقَةُ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ إِذَا اسْتَعْمَلَهُ فِي الشَّعْرِ فَعَلَيْهِ دَم الإِزالَةِ الشَّعِثِ وَان اسْتَعْمَلَهُ فِي وَكُونَهُ مَطَعُومَا لا يُنَافِيهِ كَالرَّغْفَرَانِ وَهذَا الْخِلافُ فِى الزَّيْتِ الْبَحْتِ وَالْحَلَ الْبَحْتِ أَمَّا الْمُطَيِّبُ مِنْهُ كَالْبِنَفْسَج والزنبق وما أشُبَهَهُمَا يَجِبُ بِاِسْتِعْمَالِهِ الدَّمُ بِالْاِتِّفَاقِ لأنَّهُ طِيبٌ وَهَذَا إِذَا اسْتَعْمَلَهُ عَلَى وَجْهِ التَّطيِّبِ ترجمہ پس اگر زیتون کا تیل لگایا تو ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اس پر دم واجب ہے اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ اس پر صدقہ واجب ہے اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ جب اس نے روغن زیتون کو بال میں استعمال کیا تو اس پر دم واجب ہے۔ کیونکہ اس نے بالوں کی پراگندگی کو دور کیا ہے اور اگر اس نے بالوں کے علاوہ میں اور میل کچیل اور پراگندگی کو دور کرتا ہے۔ پس ان سب کی وجہ سے جرم پورا ہو جائے گا۔ اس لئے دم کو واجب کرے گا۔ اور اس کا مطعوم ہوتا ان چیزوں کے منافی نہیں ہے جیسے زعفران اور یہ اختلاف خالص روغن زیتون اور خالص تلی کے نیل میں ہے۔ ربا روغن زیتون یا تل میں سے جو خوشبو دار کیا گیا ہو جیسے بنفشہ، چنبیلی اور اس کے مانند تو اس کے استعمال سے بالا تفاق دم واجب ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وہ خوشبو ہے اور یہ اس صورت میں ہے کہ شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر اس نے روغن زیتون بالوں میں لگایا تو اس پر دم واجب ہوگا۔ اور اگر
Applying olive oil necessitates dam or sadaqah, statements of jurists. If he applies olive oil, then according to Abu Hanifa, upon him is dam; and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: upon him is sadaqah. And al-Shafi'i said: If he uses it on the hair, then upon him is dam for removing dishevelment (sha'th); and if he uses it on other than the hair, then nothing is upon him due to the lack of removal (of dishevelment). And for them (the Sahibayn) the proof is that it is from the edible items, except that there is benefit in it in the sense of killing vermin and removing dishevelment, so it is a deficient crime (jinayah qasirah). And for Abu Hanifa, the proof is that it is the origin of perfume and is not free from some type of perfume, and it kills vermin, softens hair, removes dirt and dishevelment; so the crime becomes complete (mutakamil) due to these combined factors, thus it necessitates dam. And its being edible does not contradict this, like za'faran (saffron). And this difference is concerning pure olive oil and pure sesame oil. As for perfumed types like banafshaj (violet), zanabaq (jasmine), and similar, by using them dam is obligatory by consensus because it is perfume. And this is when he uses it for the purpose of perfuming. Translation: So if he applied olive oil, according to Abu Hanifa dam is obligatory upon him, and the Sahibayn said that sadaqah is obligatory upon him. And Imam Shafi'i said: When he uses olive oil on the hair, then dam is obligatory due to removing dishevelment; and if he uses it on other than hair, nothing is obligatory because dishevelment is not removed. And the Sahibayn's proof is that olive oil is from the edible items, but there is a kind of benefit in it in killing lice and removing dishevelment, so this benefit is a deficient crime. And Abu Hanifa's proof is that olive oil is the origin of perfume and itself is not free from a type of perfume, and it kills lice etc., softens hair, removes dirt and dishevelment. So due to all these, the crime becomes complete, so it will necessitate dam. And its being edible is not contradictory, like saffron. And this difference is regarding pure olive oil and pure sesame oil. As for perfumed types like violet, jasmine, and similar, by their use dam is obligatory by consensus because it is perfume. And this is when he uses it for the purpose of perfuming. Explanation: The issue: If a muhrim applies olive oil, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, dam jinayat becomes obligatory. And the Sahibayn said that sadaqah will be obligatory. And Imam Shafi'i said that if he applies olive oil on the hair, then dam is obligatory; and if...
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute (involving Hanafi and Shafi'i) along with an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the penalty for applying olive (or sesame) oil in ihram. The text presents three positions: (1) Abu Hanifa holds that dam (a full sacrifice) is required because olive oil has properties of perfume and multiple benefits (killing lice, softening hair, removing dirt), making the crime complete. (2) The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that only sadaqah (charity, half sa' of wheat) is required because olive oil is primarily an edible item; any benefit is supplementary, making it a 'deficient crime' (jinayah qasirah). (3) Imam al-Shafi'i differentiates: if used on hair, dam is required for removing dishevelment (sha'th); if used elsewhere, nothing is required. The Hanafi school also distinguishes between pure oil (containing the ikhtilaf) and perfumed oils (like violet, jasmine) which unanimously require dam because they are clearly perfumes. The passage follows the order: ruling summary, proof of Sahibayn, proof of Abu Hanifa, then the exception for perfumed oils.

Key Terms
دم (dam): A full sacrificial animal (e.g., a goat) as expiation for major ihram violations.
صدقہ (sadaqah): Here, half a sa' of wheat or equivalent, for minor violations.
جنايت قاصرة (jinayah qasirah): A 'deficient crime' where the violation is partial, incurring a lesser penalty (sadaqah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), what is the expiation for a muhrim applying pure olive oil in ihram?
A) Dam is obligatory.
B) Sadaqah is obligatory.
C) Nothing is obligatory.
D) Dam is obligatory only if applied to hair.

Key Takeaway
The expiation for olive oil in ihram depends on whether it is considered a complete crime (dam) or deficient crime (sadaqah), with an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Ruling on a Muhrim Using Olive Oil: Dam or Sadaqah?
Dispute on whether olive oil use requires dam or sadaqah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a muhrim using olive oil, distinguish between the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and apply the condition of intent (perfume vs medicine) to determine the atonement.

Core Idea
Olive oil is not perfume but its origin; using it as perfume incurs dam per Abu Hanifa, sadaqah per Sahibayn; medicinal use exempts.

This passage from the Hidayah examines a dispute among Hanafi imams and with other schools regarding the atonement for a muhrim using olive oil. While the substance itself is food, it has perfuming qualities and can kill lice, leading to differing assessments of whether the violation is complete (kamila) or deficient (qasirah). The text also establishes a critical condition: the ruling depends on the intention behind the use—perfume versus medicine. Understanding this nuance is essential for correctly applying the atonement rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed ruling
The act is a muhrim applying olive oil to the hair or body. The dispute is whether it requires dam (animal sacrifice) or sadaqah (charity) as atonement.
2
Collect the proofs for each position
Imam Abu Hanifa argues that olive oil is the origin of perfume and has perfuming qualities, making it a complete jinayah requiring dam. The Sahibayn argue it is a food item with minor benefit, making it a deficient jinayah requiring only sadaqah. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that applying to hair incurs dam due to the hadith about the disheveled pilgrim, but other areas incur nothing.
Pay attention to how each imam defines the nature of olive oil.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Within the Hanafi school, the difference hinges on whether the violation is complete or deficient. Abu Hanifa focuses on the inherent qualities of olive oil, while the Sahibayn emphasize its primary use as food.
This is a classic example of ikhtilaf within the madhhab.
4
Identify the key condition: intent of use
The text explicitly states that these rulings apply only when the oil is used as perfume. If used for medicinal purposes (e.g., on a wound or cracked foot), no atonement is due. Pure perfumes like musk still require atonement even for medicinal use.
The condition is based on the fact that olive oil is not perfume in itself.
5
Determine the mufta bihi ruling
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of Imam Abu Hanifa: using pure olive oil as perfume requires dam. The Sahibayn's view (sadaqah) is also transmitted but is considered weaker in this context.
The author of Hidayah seems to lean towards Abu Hanifa's view.

اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم
بالوں کے علاوہ میں لگایا تو اس پر کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا یہی امام مالک کا مذہب ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بالوں میں روغن زیتون کا استعمال بالوں کی پراگندگی اور میل پکھیل کو دور کر دیتا ہے حالانکہ حاجی کے لئے اس پرا گندگی کا دور کرنا ممنوع ہے جیسا کہ حدیث الحائج الشَّعِتُ التَّفْلُ شاہد ہے۔ اور حالت احرام میں فعل ممنوع کا ارتکاب موجب دم ہے اس لئے اس صورت میں دم واجب ہوگا۔ اور بالوں کے علاوہ میں استعمال کرنے کی صورت میں چونکہ پراگندگی اور میل کچیل کا دور کرنا نہیں پایا جاتا۔ اس لئے اس صورت میں دم واجب نہ ہو
صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ روغن زیتون کھانے کی چیزوں میں سے ہے نہ کہ خوشبو کی کوئی چیز ہے اور نہ آرائش کی ، ہاں اتنی بات ضرور ہے کہ اس میں جوں مار ڈالنے اور پراگندگی کو دور کرنے کا تھوڑا سا نفع ہے اس لئے روغن زیتون کا تیل استعمال کرنا محرم کے لئے جنایت تو ہو گا مگر جنایت قاصرہ ہوگا اور جنایت قاصرہ کی وجہ سے صدقہ واجب ہوتا ہے نہ کہ دم اس لئے روغن زیتون لگانے کی وجہ سے صدقہ واجب ہوگا دم واجب نہ ہوگا۔
امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ روغن زیتون بلاشبہ خوشبو نہیں لیکن خوشبو کی اصل اور جڑ ہے۔ پس جس طرح خوشبو کے استعمال سے دم واجب ہوتا ہے اسی طرح اس کی اصل اور جڑ کے استعمال سے بھی دم واجب ہوگا۔ نیز روغن زیتون میں ایک گونہ خوشبو ہوتی ہے اور وہ جون وغیرہ کو مار ڈالتا ہے بالوں کو نرم کرتا ہے اور پراگندگی اور میل کچیل کو دور کرتا ہے۔ پس ان سب باتوں کی وجہ سے جنایت کال ہوگئی اور جنایت کا ملہ موجب دم ہے اس لئے روغن زیتون لگانے کی وجہ سے اس پر دم واجب ہوگا ۔ اور صاحبین کا یہ کہنا کہ روغن زیور کھانے کی چیزوں میں سے ہے بلا شبہ کھانے کی چیز ہے مگر کھانے کی چیز ہو نا مذکورہ چیزوں ( نوع طیب قتل ہوام وغیرہ) کے منافی نہیں ہے۔ جیسے زعفران کہ بالا تفاق کھانے کی چیز بھی ہے اور خوشبو بھی ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ امام صاحب، صاحبین اور امام شافعی کے درمیان اختلاف جو بیان کیا گیا ہے وہ خالص روغن زیتون اور خالص متل کے تیل میں ہے ورنہ اگر روغن زیتون یا تل کے تیل میں ہفتہ یا چنبیلی وغیرہ خوشبو ملا کر اس کو خوشبو دار کر لیا ہو تو ں کے استعمال سے بالا تفاق دم واجب ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ اب یہ ایک خوشبو ہے۔ یہ تمام تفاصیل اس وقت ہیں جبکہ اس کو خوشبو لگانے کے طور پر متعمال کیا ہو۔ زخم یا پاؤں کے شگاف پر دوا لگائی تو کفارہ لازم نہیں
ولو داری به جرحه أو شقوق رجله فَلا كَفَّارَة عَلَيْهِ لأنه ليس بطيب فى نَفْسِهِ إِنَّمَا هُوَ أَصْلُ لطَّيْب أَوْ هُوَ طيب من وجهِ فَيُشترط استعماله على وجه الطيب بخلاف ما إذا تدَاوَىٰ بِالْمِسْكِ وَمَا أَشْبَهُهُ
ترجمہ اور اگر روغن زیتون کے ساتھ اپنے زخم یا پاؤں کے شگاف کا علاج کیا تو اس پر کفارہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ روغن بتون بذات خود خوشبو نہیں وہ تو خوشبو کی اصل ہے یا وہ من وجہ خوشبو ہے اس لئے خوشبو لگانے کے طور پر اس کے استعمال کی شرط ہے برخف اس کے جبکہ مشک اور اس کے مانند سے دوا کی ۔
تشریح مسئلہ، اگر محرم نے زخم یا پاؤں کے شگاف کا علاج کرنے کے لئے روغن زیتون استعمال کیا تو اس پر دم یا صدقہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ روغن زیتون اولا تو بذات خود خوشبو نہیں ہے، بلکہ خوشبو کی اصل اور جڑ ہے یا من وجہ خوشبو ہے اس لئے یہ شرط آئی گئی ہے کہ اگر اس کا
۴۱۳
اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم کتاب الحج استعمال بطور خوشبو کے کیا گیا ہے تب تو کفارہ یعنی دم یا صدقہ واجب ہوگا اور اگر بطور علاج استعمال کیا گی تو اس پر کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اور اگر مشک یا عنبر یا کافور وغیرہ کا استعمال بطور دوا کیا تب بھی کفارہ واجب ہوگا کیونکہ یہ چیزیں عین خوشبو میں ان میں کفارہ واجب ہونے کے لئے بطور خوشبو استعمال کرنے کی شرط نہیں ہے۔
Book of Hajj. 412. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah volume three. If he applied it to other than hair, then nothing becomes wajib upon him. This is also the madhhab of Imam Malik. The proof of Imam al-Shafi'i is that using olive oil on the hair removes the dishevelment and dirt of the hair, whereas removing this dishevelment is prohibited for the pilgrim, as the hadith 'al-Hajju al-sha'ithu al-tafil' witnesses. And in the state of ihram, committing a prohibited act necessitates dam, so in this case dam becomes wajib. And in the case of using it on other than hair, since removing dishevelment and dirt is not found, so in this case dam is not wajib. The proof of the Sahibayn is that olive oil is among food items, not a perfume item nor an adornment. However, it does have a slight benefit of killing lice and removing dishevelment. Therefore, using olive oil is a jinayah for the muhrim, but it is a jinayah qasirah, and for a jinayah qasirah, sadaqah is wajib, not dam. So due to applying olive oil, sadaqah is wajib, not dam. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that olive oil is definitely not perfume, but it is the origin and root of perfume. So just as using perfume incurs dam, similarly using its origin and root also incurs dam. Also, olive oil has a kind of perfume, and it kills lice etc., softens the hair, and removes dishevelment and dirt. So due to all these reasons, the jinayah becomes kamila, and a kamila jinayah incurs dam. Therefore, applying olive oil incurs dam. And the Sahibayn's claim that olive oil is among food items: it is indeed a food item, but being a food item does not contradict the mentioned characteristics (type of perfume, killing vermin, etc.). Like saffron, which by consensus is both a food and a perfume. The author of Hidayah says: The disagreement that was mentioned between Imam Sahib, the Sahibayn, and Imam al-Shafi'i is concerning pure olive oil and pure sesame oil. Otherwise, if olive oil or sesame oil is mixed with jasmine or musk etc. and made fragrant, then its use incurs dam by consensus. Because now it is a perfume. All these details are when it is used as a perfume. If applied as medicine to a wound or cracked feet, then atonement is not binding. 'And if he applies it to his wound or fissures of his foot, then there is no atonement upon him, because it is not perfume in itself; rather it is the origin of perfume or it is perfume from one aspect. So its use is conditioned on being in the manner of perfume, unlike when he treats with musk and the like.' Translation: And if he treated his wound or fissures of his foot with olive oil, then there is no atonement upon him, because olive oil is not perfume in itself; rather it is the origin of perfume, or it is perfume from one aspect. So its use is conditioned on the manner of perfume, unlike when he treats with musk and the like. Explanation of the issue: If a muhrim used olive oil to treat a wound or fissures of his foot, then dam or sadaqah is not wajib upon him. Because olive oil is not perfume in itself; rather it is the origin and root of perfume, or from one aspect it is perfume. Therefore, it is conditioned that if it is used as perfume, then atonement (dam or sadaqah) becomes wajib, but if used as treatment, then no atonement. And if musk, ambergris, camphor, etc., are used as medicine, then still atonement is wajib because these are pure perfume; for them, the condition of using as perfume is not required for atonement.
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab) regarding the ruling on a muhrim (pilgrim in ihram) using olive oil. The text presents three positions: Imam Abu Hanifa rules that using olive oil (on hair or body) requires dam (sacrifice of an animal), while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) say it requires sadaqah (charity). Imam al-Shafi'i is also mentioned: he requires dam for the hair due to the hadith 'al-Hajju al-sha'ithu al-tafil' (the pilgrim is disheveled and dusty), but for other areas he agrees with the Sahibayn? Actually the first paragraph attributes to Shafi'i that using on hair incurs dam, and on other areas nothing. But the main dispute is among Hanafis. Abu Hanifa's proof: olive oil is the origin of perfume and has a perfuming quality; it kills lice, softens hair, etc., so it is a complete jinayah requiring dam. The Sahibayn: it is food, not perfume; its benefit is minor, so it is a deficient jinayah requiring sadaqah. The text then notes that this disagreement is for pure olive/sesame oil; if mixed with perfume, all agree on dam. Then it adds a crucial condition: the ruling depends on the intent of use. If used as perfume (for adornment or scent), then dam (or sadaqah according to Sahibayn) is wajib. But if used for treatment of a wound or cracked feet, no penalty at all. This is because olive oil is not perfume in itself; its use is judged by its manner. However, for pure perfumes like musk, even medicinal use incurs atonement. The commentary (sharh) explains the matn's Arabic quote and reinforces the details.

Key Terms
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (sheep or goat) required as atonement for certain violations during Hajj/Umrah.
صدقہ (sadaqah): Charity, here specifically half a sa' of wheat or equivalent value, given as atonement for minor violations.
جنایت قاصرہ (jinayah qasirah): A deficient violation that does not fully achieve the prohibited benefit; incurs lesser atonement (sadaqah).
روغن زیتون (raughan zaytun): Olive oil; considered a food item with some perfuming qualities, not a pure perfume.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling if a muhrim applies pure olive oil to his hair as perfume?
A) Nothing is wajib because olive oil is food.
B) Dam is wajib per Imam Abu Hanifa, sadaqah per Sahibayn.
C) Only sadaqah is wajib by consensus.
D) Dam is wajib by consensus.

Key Takeaway
Using olive oil as perfume during ihram requires atonement (dam per Abu Hanifa, sadaqah per Sahibayn); medicinal use is exempt for pure oil but not for mixtures with pure perfumes.
